The Prophet's Humility and True Pride
Commentary on the Prophet's hadith about being master and true pride.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's statement of being master is a declaration of honor without pride, and that true pride lies in servitude to Allah.

Core Idea
True pride is found in servitude to Allah, not in personal status.

This brief commentary unpacks a profound hadith of the Prophet, clarifying that his unique status as master of humanity is not a source of personal boastfulness. Instead, the Prophet redirects all honor to Allah, teaching that genuine pride lies in complete servitude to the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the Hadith and Commentary
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two statements made by the Prophet and the concluding remark by the commentator.
The Arabic is reconstructed from OCR, so refer to the translation for clarity.
2
Identify the Key Phrase 'ولا فخر'
The Prophet repeats 'ولا فخر' (no pride) after declaring his high status. Ask yourself: why does he add this? What does it teach about humility?
3
Understand the Shift to True Pride
The commentary shifts from the Prophet's status to the definition of true pride. Note that the phrase 'إنما الفخر بالعبودية لله' redirects all pride to servitude to Allah.
This is the central teaching of the passage.
4
Reflect on the Lesson
Consider how this teaching applies to your own understanding of honor and humility. The highest honor is being a servant of Allah, not any worldly rank.
The Prophet's example is a model for all believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنا سيد ولد آدم ولا فخر، وأنا حامل لواء الحمد يوم القيامة ولا فخر. إنما الفخر بالعبودية لله.
I am the master of the children of Adam, and no pride; and I am the carrier of the banner of praise on the Day of Resurrection, and no pride. Indeed, pride lies in servitude to Allah.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Prophet's hadith. The author quotes the Prophet saying that he is the master of humanity but without any pride, and he will carry the banner of praise on Judgment Day without any pride. The author then explains that true pride lies in complete servitude to Allah. The Prophet emphasizes humility despite his high rank, teaching that all honor comes from Allah's grace, not from personal boasting.

Key Terms
سيد ولد آدم
الفخر
العبودية
لواء الحمد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the Prophet's statement about being master implies he is superior and has reason to boast.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly denies pride, showing that his status is a gift from Allah, not a cause for arrogance. True pride is in being a servant of Allah.

Checkpoint
What does the Prophet emphasize by saying 'ولا فخر' (no pride)?
A) That he is not actually the master of Adam's children
B) That his high status is a gift from Allah, not a cause for arrogance
C) That he will not carry the banner on Judgment Day
D) That servitude is shameful

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's humility teaches that all honor is from Allah, and true pride is in complete servitude to Him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet, the master of all humanity, said 'no pride' about his rank. When you achieve something or receive praise, do you feel a sense of personal pride? How can you train yourself to attribute every good you have to Allah alone, just as the Prophet taught?
?
If true pride lies in servitude to Allah, how much of your daily effort is spent seeking visible status versus seeking Allah's pleasure in hidden acts of worship? What is one concrete step you can take today to shift your focus from worldly recognition to humble servitude?
?
Read the hadith again: 'I am the master... and no pride; I am the carrier of the banner of praise... and no pride.' Can you honestly say that you would still pursue the highest ranks in this life if they came with no recognition from people? Examine your heart: are you satisfied with Allah knowing your deeds, even if no one else does?

Introducing Prophethood: The Tripartite Method Applied
Sanusi opens the prophethood section with a tripartite classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi applies the same tripartite classification of necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes to the prophets, mirroring the earlier discussion on God's attributes.

Core Idea
Prophethood is analysed using the same three rational categories as divinity.

Sanusi now turns to a new topic: prophethood. Just as he classified attributes for Allah, he applies the same three categories—necessary, impossible, and permissible—to the messengers. This short opening paragraph sets the stage for the detailed lists that follow. Pay attention to the structural parallel; it reveals the systematic nature of Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it announces three categories for the messengers: necessary (واجب), impossible (مستحيل), and permissible (جائز).
This is exactly the same method used for God's attributes earlier.
2
Identify the structural parallel
Compare this passage with the beginning of the section on Allah's attributes. Sanusi uses identical phrasing, showing that his theological method is consistent.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why would the same three categories apply to both God and prophets? Think about what it means for prophets to have necessary attributes (like truthfulness) and impossible ones (like lying).
This prepares you for the detailed lessons on each attribute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوَّات ] ما يجب للرُّسُلِ الكرام مِنَ الصفاتِ ، وما يستحيلُ، وما يجوز ] وأمَّا الرُّسُلُ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام : فيجب في حقهم :
Discussion on prophethood] What is necessary for the noble messengers of attributes, and what is impossible, and what is permissible] As for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: necessary in their right:
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage marks the transition to a new topic: prophethood (nubuwwat). Sanusi announces that he will apply the same tripartite classification (necessary, impossible, permissible) to the prophets. The text only gives the introductory sentence before the page ends, indicating that the actual lists of prophetic attributes will follow on subsequent pages. It serves as a heading and structural parallel to the earlier section on God's attributes.

Key Terms
النبوَّات
الرسل
الواجب
المستحيل
الجائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets have no impossible attributes; they are sinless but can have any human trait.
Correction: Prophets have specific impossible attributes (e.g., lying, treachery) that contradict their mission. Sanusi will enumerate these.

Checkpoint
What three categories does Sanusi announce for the attributes of messengers?
A) Necessary, optional, forbidden
B) Necessary, impossible, permissible
C) Positive, negative, neutral
D) Essential, accidental, possible

Key Takeaway
Sanusi introduces the attributes of prophets using the same three rational categories as for God: necessary, impossible, and permissible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that prophethood is analysed using the same three rational categories as Allah. Does your faith in the prophets rest on this rational foundation, or have you taken their attributes for granted? Starting today, commit to studying the life of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ through this tripartite lens—what is necessary, impossible, and permissible for him—and see how it strengthens your love and certainty.
?
The systematic approach in this lesson is not just academic; it is a mercy from Allah to protect your iman. In your daily life, do you approach your religion with disciplined reflection, or are you content with mindless repetition? Choose one aspect of your faith this week—such as belief in angels or the Day of Judgment—and examine it using the same wajib/mustahil/ja'iz framework. Will you do it?
?
If you truly internalise that prophets must be truthful and trustworthy, how does that change the way you listen to their stories in the Quran? Do you hear them as mere tales or as authoritative guidance? Make a firm intention tonight to recite the Quran with the awareness that every word from the prophets is true, and ask yourself: are you living according to that truth?

Prophethood

Classification of Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi enumerates the three categories of prophetic attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of prophetic attributes: necessary, impossible, and permissible, as outlined by Sanusi.

Core Idea
Prophetic attributes are divided into three rational categories.

Sanusi begins by establishing the framework for understanding what can be said about prophets. Just as with Allah, prophets have attributes that are necessary, impossible, and permissible. This classification is essential for distinguishing true prophethood from false claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the three categories. Then read the translation to understand the terms.
Notice the parallel structure: necessary attributes are listed first, then their opposites.
2
Identify the necessary and impossible attributes
List the three necessary attributes (truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveyance) and their corresponding impossible opposites (lying, betrayal, concealment).
These are the core of prophetic character.
3
Understand the permissible category
Note that permissible attributes are human experiences that do not lower the prophet's rank, such as illness.
This shows prophets are human but sinless.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why this classification is important for theology. It helps us know what to believe about prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوات ما يجب للرسل الكرام من الصفات ، وما يستحيل، وما يجوز وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب في حقهم : الصدق ، والأمانة ، والتبليغ . ويستحيل عليهم : الكذب ، والخيانة ، والكتمان . ويجوز في حقهم : ما يجوز في حق سائر البشر ؛ لكن إن كان مما لا يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليا ؛ كالمرض ونحوه . دلائل ما سبق من الصفات لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام والدليل على وجوب صدقهم : المعجزات ؛ ولو لم يكونوا أمناء لكانوا خائنين ، ولو لم يبلغوا لكانوا كاتمين وذلك محال ودليل جواز الأعراض البشرية عليهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : مشاهدة وقوعها بهم لأهل زمانهم ، وتقلت إلينا بالتواتر .
The discourse on prophethood: what is necessary for the noble messengers of attributes, what is impossible, and what is permissible. As for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: necessary for them are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance. Impossible for them are lying, betrayal, and concealment. Permissible for them is what is permissible for other human beings, provided it does not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, such as illness and the like. Proofs for what preceded of attributes for them, peace and blessings be upon them: And the proof for the necessity of their truthfulness is miracles; and if they were not trustworthy they would be betrayers, and if they did not convey they would be concealers, and that is impossible. And the proof for the permissibility of human experiences upon them, peace and blessings be upon them: is the observation of their occurrence among them by the people of their time, and it has been transmitted to us by tawātur (continuous transmission).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof section on the attributes of prophets. It first divides prophetic attributes into three categories: necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and permissible (jā'iz). The necessary attributes are three: truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amāna), and conveyance of the message (tablīgh). The corresponding impossible opposites are: lying (kidhb), betrayal (khiyāna), and concealment (kitmān). The permissible attributes are those human experiences (like illness) that do not detract from their lofty rank. Then the passage provides proofs: the proof for the necessity of truthfulness is the miracles (mu‘jizāt) they bring, which authenticate their message. The necessity of trustworthiness and conveyance is shown by reductio: if they were not trustworthy, they would be betrayers; if they did not convey, they would be concealers—both impossible given their mission. The proof for the permissibility of human experiences (a‘rāḍ bashariyya) is empirical: people of their time observed these occurrences, and the reports have reached us via tawātur (uninterrupted, mass transmission), which yields certain knowledge.

Key Terms
رسل
صدق
أمانة
تبليغ
كذب
خيانة
كتمان
جواز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot experience any human ailments or needs.
Correction: Prophets can experience permissible human things like illness, as long as it does not lower their status.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a necessary attribute of prophets according to this passage?
A) Lying
B) Betrayal
C) Truthfulness
D) Illness

Key Takeaway
Prophets are characterized by truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance, and are free from their opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe in the Prophet ﷺ and his truthfulness. But when the Prophet’s command goes against your convenience, do you truly obey without hesitation? Examine a recent situation where you prioritized your desire over his command. What will you change today?
?
The prophets were entrusted with the message and delivered it fully, concealing nothing. Are you entrusted with any knowledge of Islam? Is there a truth you are hiding from others for fear of rejection or discomfort? Write down one truth you need to convey and commit to sharing it with someone this week.
?
If the prophets are free from even small betrayals, how can you justify breaking a trust—even a minor one—in your daily life? Recall a trust you violated and make a concrete plan to restore it, whether by apology or by amending your behavior.

Proofs for Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi provides proofs for the necessary and permissible attributes of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proofs for the necessary and permissible attributes of prophets, especially the role of miracles and tawātur.

Core Idea
Miracles prove truthfulness; human experiences are proven by observation and tawātur.

After classifying prophetic attributes, Sanusi provides the rational and empirical proofs. The most powerful proof for a prophet's truthfulness is the miracle he brings, which cannot be matched by others. For the permissibility of human experiences, the proof is simply that people observed them and the reports have been transmitted reliably.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof passage
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the proof structures. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice that the proof for truthfulness is direct, while the proof for permissibility is based on observation and transmission.
2
Understand the miracle-based proof for truthfulness
The passage states that miracles prove the necessity of truthfulness. Think about why: miracles are signs from Allah confirming the prophet's message.
Also note the reductio for trustworthiness and conveyance.
3
Understand the proof for permissible human experiences
The proof is empirical: people observed these experiences, and the reports reached us via tawātur (continuous transmission), which yields certain knowledge.
This shows that prophets are human in permissible ways.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Combine the classification and proof to see how Sanusi defends the integrity of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوات ما يجب للرسل الكرام من الصفات ، وما يستحيل، وما يجوز وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب في حقهم : الصدق ، والأمانة ، والتبليغ . ويستحيل عليهم : الكذب ، والخيانة ، والكتمان . ويجوز في حقهم : ما يجوز في حق سائر البشر ؛ لكن إن كان مما لا يؤدي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليا ؛ كالمرض ونحوه . دلائل ما سبق من الصفات لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام والدليل على وجوب صدقهم : المعجزات ؛ ولو لم يكونوا أمناء لكانوا خائنين ، ولو لم يبلغوا لكانوا كاتمين وذلك محال ودليل جواز الأعراض البشرية عليهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : مشاهدة وقوعها بهم لأهل زمانهم ، وتقلت إلينا بالتواتر .
The discourse on prophethood: what is necessary for the noble messengers of attributes, what is impossible, and what is permissible. As for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: necessary for them are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance. Impossible for them are lying, betrayal, and concealment. Permissible for them is what is permissible for other human beings, provided it does not lead to deficiency in their high ranks, such as illness and the like. Proofs for what preceded of attributes for them, peace and blessings be upon them: And the proof for the necessity of their truthfulness is miracles; and if they were not trustworthy they would be betrayers, and if they did not convey they would be concealers, and that is impossible. And the proof for the permissibility of human experiences upon them, peace and blessings be upon them: is the observation of their occurrence among them by the people of their time, and it has been transmitted to us by tawātur (continuous transmission).
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof section on the attributes of prophets. It first divides prophetic attributes into three categories: necessary (wājib), impossible (mustaḥīl), and permissible (jā'iz). The necessary attributes are three: truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amāna), and conveyance of the message (tablīgh). The corresponding impossible opposites are: lying (kidhb), betrayal (khiyāna), and concealment (kitmān). The permissible attributes are those human experiences (like illness) that do not detract from their lofty rank. Then the passage provides proofs: the proof for the necessity of truthfulness is the miracles (mu‘jizāt) they bring, which authenticate their message. The necessity of trustworthiness and conveyance is shown by reductio: if they were not trustworthy, they would be betrayers; if they did not convey, they would be concealers—both impossible given their mission. The proof for the permissibility of human experiences (a‘rāḍ bashariyya) is empirical: people of their time observed these occurrences, and the reports have reached us via tawātur (uninterrupted, mass transmission), which yields certain knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The truthfulness of prophets is proven by their good character alone.
Correction: The primary proof is the miracle they bring, which authenticates their claim.

Checkpoint
What is the proof for the necessity of truthfulness in prophets according to this passage?
A) Continuous transmission (tawātur)
B) Their good character
C) The miracles they bring
D) The fact they are messengers

Key Takeaway
Miracles are the definitive proof of a prophet's truthfulness, while tawātur confirms their human experiences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the miracles of the prophets are sufficient evidence for your faith, or do you rely on other factors like upbringing or culture? What would change if you had to base your certainty solely on the proof of miracles as described here?
?
When you hear reports about the Prophets (peace be upon them) experiencing hardship or illness, does your heart accept that as part of their humanity, or do you subconsciously doubt their status? How can you use the concept of tawātur to strengthen your conviction?
?
If you were entrusted with a message from God, would you convey it fully without alteration or concealment? What fears or desires might tempt you to hold back, and how does the necessity of trustworthiness in this lesson challenge your own integrity?

Prophetic Attributes: Necessary, Impossible, Permissible
Sanusi classifies prophetic attributes with examples and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of prophetic attributes (necessary, impossible, permissible) and the proofs for each.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and convey the message.

This lesson introduces the rational classification of prophetic attributes according to Sanusi. Just as we classified attributes of Allah, we now apply the same categories to prophets. The passage defines what is necessary, impossible, and permissible for prophets, and provides evidence from miracles and observation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall structure.
Notice the three clear categories: wajib, mustahil, ja'iz.
2
Identify the three categories and examples
List the necessary attributes (sidq, amana, tabligh) and their opposites (kadhib, khiyana, kitman). Then note the permissible attributes with the restriction.
The restriction is key: permissible traits must not lower the prophet's rank.
3
Understand the proof for necessary attributes
Sanusi uses miracles as proof. Why? Because miracles confirm truthfulness; if a prophet were treacherous or concealed the message, miracles would not accompany them.
This is a rational proof based on the nature of miracles.
4
Understand the proof for permissible attributes
The proof is observation by contemporaries and tawatur. We know prophets experienced human traits like illness because it was witnessed and transmitted.
This is an empirical proof.
5
Reflect on the additional attributes
Some scholars add attributes like intelligence, freedom, masculinity, and pure lineage. Consider why these are necessary due to the restriction.
These are derived from the requirement that prophets hold the highest rank.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الصدقُ، والأمانة، والتبليغ. ويستحيل عليهم: الكذبُ، والخيانة، والكتمان. ويجوزُ في حقهم: ما يجوزُ في حق سائر البشر؛ لكن إنْ كانَ ممَّا لا يؤدّي إلى نقص في مراتبهم العليَّة (۱)؛ كالمرض ونحوه (۲). والدليل على وجوبِ صدقهم: المعجزات؛ ولو لم يكونوا أمناء لكانوا خائنينَ، ولو لم يبلغوا لكانوا كاتمين وذلك محال. ودليلُ جواز الأعراض البشريَّةِ عليهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام: مشاهدة وقوعها بهم لأهل زمانهم، وتُقلَتْ إلينا بالتواتر. (۱) فوجب لهم بهذا القيد: الفطانة، وبعضهم يزيد: الحرية، والحضرية والذكورة، وطهارة النسب آباء وأمهات، وغير ذلك. (۲) وهذا تمثيل للجائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
Truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance. And impossible upon them: lying, treachery, and concealment. And permissible in their right: what is permissible in the right of the rest of humans, but if it is something that does not lead to a deficiency in their high ranks (1); like illness and the like (2). And the proof for the obligation of their truthfulness: miracles; and if they were not trustworthy they would be treacherous, and if they did not convey they would be concealers, and that is impossible. And the proof for the permissibility of human accidents upon them, peace and blessings be upon them: observation of their occurrence to them by the people of their time, and it was transmitted to us by tawatur. (1) So due to this restriction, intelligence is obligatory for them, and some add: freedom, civilness, masculinity, purity of lineage from fathers and mothers, and other than that. (2) And this is an example of what is permissible in their right, peace and blessings be upon them.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage classifies prophetic attributes into three categories: wajib (necessary), mustahil (impossible), and ja'iz (permissible). It first lists the necessary attributes: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveyance (tabligh). Then the impossible: lying (kadhib), treachery (khiyana), and concealment (kitman). Permissible attributes include any human trait that does not detract from their high rank, such as illness. The author then provides proofs: for the necessity of truthfulness, miracles are cited, because if a prophet were not truthful, he would be treacherous or conceal the message, which is impossible. For permissible human accidents, the proof is direct observation by contemporaries and tawatur (mass transmission). In a footnote, the author explains that intelligence (fatana) is obligatory due to the restriction of maintaining high rank, and some scholars add other qualities like freedom, urban residence, masculinity, and pure lineage. Another footnote clarifies that illness and such are examples of permissible human traits.

Key Terms

الأمانة
التبليغ
الكذب
الخيانة
الكتمان
المعجزات
الفطانة
الحرية
الحضرية
الذكورة
طهارة النسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any human trait is permissible for prophets without restriction.
Correction: Permissible attributes must not lower the prophet's rank; e.g., illness is permissible but not defects that diminish honor.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, which proof establishes the necessity of truthfulness for prophets?
A) Observation by contemporaries
B) Miracles
C) Tawatur
D) Intelligence

Key Takeaway
Prophets are truthful, trustworthy, and convey revelation; their human traits do not diminish their rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the Prophet’s truthfulness (sidq). Is there any area of your life where your words or actions are not fully aligned? How does knowing that the Prophet was absolutely truthful challenge you to be more honest today?
?
The prophets were entrusted with the greatest message. Are you trustworthy with the smaller trusts given to you—your time, your relationships, your responsibilities? What would it mean to live with the amana of a prophet?
?
Prophet's human experiences like illness did not lower their rank. When you face personal trials or weaknesses, do you feel your spiritual status is diminished? How can you maintain your dignity and faith while embracing your humanity, like the prophets did?

The Three Obligatory Attributes of Messengers
Sanusi enumerates three obligatory attributes for messengers with definitions and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three obligatory attributes of messengers—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveying—and the rational proofs for each.

Core Idea
Prophets are defined by three inseparable attributes: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveying.

In this passage, Sanusi lays out the three essential qualities that every messenger must possess. These attributes are not just moral recommendations; they are logically necessary for the function of prophethood. We will look at the definition of each and the evidence that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening enumeration
Read the passage from 'وأما الرسل' up to the point where the comparative analysis begins. Notice the three attributes listed in order.
2
Examine each attribute's definition and proof
For each attribute (truthfulness, trustworthiness, conveying), identify its precise definition and the proof Sanusi provides. Note how the proofs differ: miracles for truthfulness, imitation for trustworthiness, consensus for conveying.
Truthfulness is proven by miracles; trustworthiness by the command to imitate; conveying by consensus.
3
Reflect on the logical necessity
Consider why these specific proofs are appropriate for each attribute and how they establish the attribute as obligatory.
The proofs are tailored to each attribute's role in prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ الكلام على النبوَّاتِ ] وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب لهم الصدقُ ؛ أي : مطابقةُ كلِّ ما أخبروا بهِ مِنْ أحكام وثواب وعقاب وغيرها لما في نفس الأمرِ ؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى قد صدَّقَهم بما تنزَّلَ مِنَ المعجزِ الذي خصَّهُمُ اللهُ بهِ منزلة قوله تعالى : صدق عبدي في كلِّ ما يبلغ عنِّي . ويجب لهم الأمانةُ ؛ أي : حفظ ظواهرهم وبواطنهم مِنَ الوقوع في محرَّم أو مكروه؛ لأن أتباعهم أمروا بالاقتداء بهم في جميع أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، وذلك يستلزم عصمتهم فيها مِنْ كلَّ منهي عنه ويجب لهم أيضاً أنَّهم بلغوا كلَّ ما أمرهم المولى سبحانَهُ بتبليغه ، ولم يتركوا شيئاً منهُ ، لا نسياناً ولا عمداً ، عمداً فلما سبق في الأمانة ، وأمَّا نسياناً فللإجماع . فالواجبُ الأَوَّلُ يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً ، ويزيدُ على التبليغ بمنع الزيادة على ما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً ، وتزيد الأمانة على الصدق بمنع وقوع المخالفة في كذب اللسانِ ، وعلى التبليغ بمنع المخالفة في غيرِ التبليغ ، ويزيدُ التبليغ على الصدق بمنع ترْكِ شيء مما
[Discussion of prophethood] And as for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: wajib for them is truthfulness (sidq), i.e., conformity of everything they inform about—of rulings, reward, punishment, etc.—to the reality of the matter; because God, exalted, has verified them by the miracle that has been sent down, which God has specially granted them, analogous to His saying: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.' And wajib for them is trustworthiness (amanah), i.e., guarding their outward and inward from falling into anything forbidden or disliked; because their followers are commanded to emulate them in all their words and actions, and that necessitates their infallibility from everything prohibited. And it is also wajib for them that they have conveyed everything which their Lord, glorified, commanded them to convey, and did not omit anything from it, whether due to forgetfulness or intentionally. As for intentionally, it is because of what preceded regarding trustworthiness; as for forgetfulness, it is because of consensus. The first wajib (i.e., sidq) exceeds trustworthiness by preventing accidental falsehood, and exceeds conveying by preventing addition to what they were commanded to convey intentionally or forgetfully. And trustworthiness exceeds truthfulness by preventing violation in spoken falsehood, and exceeds conveying by preventing violation in non-conveying. And conveying exceeds truthfulness by preventing omission of anything from...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines three obligatory attributes for prophets and messengers: sidq (truthfulness), amanah (trustworthiness), and tabligh (conveying the message). For each, the author gives a definition and a proof. For sidq: it is correspondence of their reports to reality, proven by the miracles God gives them which verify their truth. For amanah: it is inward and outward protection from sin, proven because followers must imitate them. For tabligh: they must convey everything commanded, without omission, proven by consensus and by the other attributes. Then the author compares the three attributes, explaining how each adds a specific protection that others do not: sidq adds protection from accidental falsehood; amanah adds protection from intentional falsehood in speech and from misconduct in non-conveying actions; tabligh adds protection from omission. The passage ends mid-sentence on page 97, but the main comparative analysis is present.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These attributes are optional or redundant; a prophet could be truthful without being trustworthy.
Correction: Each attribute is obligatory and distinct; they cover different aspects of prophetic infallibility.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what proves that messengers must be truthful?
A) Rational necessity
B) The miracles God gives them
C) Consensus of the community
D) Their own statements

Key Takeaway
The three obligatory attributes of messengers are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveying, each proven by a distinct rational argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophets are perfectly truthful in everything they report from Allah. How truthful are you in your own speech about Allah? When you speak of His attributes or His commands, do you ensure that you convey only what you know to be true, or do you sometimes add your own assumptions? Will you commit to verifying every religious statement you make before uttering it?
?
The prophets are entrusted with the message and they guard themselves from sin and disliked actions. Are you guarding your heart and actions from what Allah dislikes, especially when you are in a position of influencing others? What is one hidden sin or disliked habit that you have been excusing, but which you will now resolve to abandon in order to be a better example?
?
The prophets conveyed the entire message without omission. Are you selective in conveying the teachings of Islam to others, sharing only what is comfortable or convenient? What is one truth about Islam that you have been too shy, or too afraid, to tell someone? Will you now find the courage to convey it?

Distinctions Among the Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi compares the three attributes, showing their distinct scopes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each prophetic attribute uniquely covers a different aspect of infallibility and how they interrelate.

Core Idea
Each attribute adds a specific protection that the others do not cover.

After defining the three attributes, Sanusi explains how they are not redundant. Truthfulness prevents falsehood, trustworthiness prevents sin, and conveying prevents omission. This comparative analysis shows the precision of theological reasoning in defining prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the comparative statements
Read from 'فالواجب الأول يزيد' to the end of the passage. Identify each comparison: sidq vs amanah, sidq vs tabligh, amanah vs tabligh, etc.
2
Understand what each attribute adds
For each comparison, note what specific protection the first attribute provides that the second does not.
Example: sidq adds protection from accidental falsehood beyond amanah.
3
See the logical relationships
Trace how the attributes overlap and complement each other to ensure complete infallibility.
The attributes are not isolated; they work together.

The Obligation of Truthfulness for Messengers
Sanusi defines ṣidq for messengers and proves its obligation via miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of truthfulness (ṣidq) for messengers and the rational proof for its obligation based on divine verification through miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles are Allah's stamp of approval on a messenger's truthfulness.

Sanusi turns from divine attributes to the messengers. Among the necessary attributes of prophets is truthfulness (ṣidq). Before exploring other attributes, we must grasp what truthfulness means in this context and why it is obligatory. The proof is elegant: miracles are not just signs, but divine declarations that the messenger speaks truly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm. Then read the literal translation. Notice the definition of ṣidq and the proof.
The Arabic uses a concise style typical of Sanusi.
2
Understand the definition of ṣidq
Identify that ṣidq is defined as conformity of all prophetic information to reality. This includes rulings, reward, punishment, and other matters.
This definition is broader than just 'not lying'.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof is that Allah verifies the messenger via miracles (al-muʿjiz). The miracle functions as divine testimony: 'My servant has spoken truly.'
Consider why a miracle uniquely confirms truthfulness.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Some may think truthfulness is not a separate attribute. But here it is explicitly established with its own proof, showing it is distinct and fundamental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فيجب لهم الصدقُ ؛ أي : مطابقةُ كلِّ ما أخبروا بهِ مِنْ أحكام وثواب وعقاب وغيرها لما في نفس الأمرِ ؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى قد صدَّقَهم بما تنزَّلَ مِنَ المعجزِ الذي خصَّهُمُ اللهُ بهِ منزلة قوله تعالى : صدق عبدي في كلِّ ما يبلغ عنِّي .
As for the messengers, upon them peace and blessings: truthfulness (ṣidq) is obligatory for them, meaning: conformity of everything they inform of—rulings, reward, punishment, and other matters—to what is in actual fact; because Allah the Exalted has verified them by [virtue of] the miracle (al-muʿjiz) that was sent down, which Allah has exclusively given them, in the status of His statement: 'My servant has spoken truly in everything he conveys from Me.'
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines the first necessary attribute (wājib) for messengers: truthfulness (ṣidq). It begins by stating that truthfulness is obligatory for them. Then it defines truthfulness as the conformity of everything they inform about—whether rulings, reward, punishment, or other matters—to what is actually the case in reality (mā fī nafs al-amr). The proof for this obligation is given: because Allah has verified them (ṣaddaqahum) through the miracle (al-muʿjiz) that He sent down, which He has exclusively granted to them. This miracle serves the status of Allah's statement: 'My servant has spoken truly (ṣadaqa ʿabdī) in everything he conveys from Me.' In other words, the miracle is a divine confirmation that what the messenger says is true.

Key Terms
الصدق
المعجز
الرسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think truthfulness is not a distinct attribute for messengers, or that it is automatically implied by prophethood without a separate proof.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly presents ṣidq as a distinct wajib attribute and provides a specific proof (miracles) to establish it, showing that it requires rational justification.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of al-ṣidq (truthfulness) for messengers according to Sanusi?
A) Speaking only about religious matters.
B) Conformity of everything they inform about to actual reality.
C) Avoiding lies about God.
D) Being honest in daily dealings.

Key Takeaway
Truthfulness (ṣidq) is an obligatory attribute for messengers, proven by the miracle which serves as Allah's direct verification of their message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every word of the Prophet is verified by the miracle of the Quran, what one command of his have you been neglecting that you must now act upon without delay?
?
Sanusi says the miracle is like Allah saying 'My servant has spoken truly in everything he conveys from Me.' Are you willing to treat the Prophet's warnings about sin and punishment with the same certainty as you treat his promises of reward? Where have you been selective in your trust?
?
When you hear a religious teacher claim something about Allah or the afterlife, do you check it against the verified message of the Prophet, or do you accept it because it feels good? What is one belief you hold that might not survive this test?

The Obligation of Trustworthiness (al-Amānah) for Messengers
Sanusi defines the wajib attribute of trustworthiness (amānah) and gives its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of trustworthiness (amānah) as a necessary attribute of messengers and its proof based on the command to emulate them.

Core Idea
Trustworthiness protects messengers from all sin because followers must imitate them.

Sanusi now turns to the second necessary attribute of messengers: trustworthiness. He defines it broadly as preservation from both outward and inward sin, and then provides a rational proof rooted in the obligation of followers to emulate their prophets. This passage establishes why messengers must be infallible in all they say and do.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Notice the concise style of Sanusi and the key terms.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the definition of amānah
Look for the phrase 'أي: حفظ ظواهرهم وبواطنهم' which defines trustworthiness as preservation from forbidden and disliked actions, both outwardly and inwardly.
This is a comprehensive definition beyond mere honesty.
3
Analyse the proof
The proof is given after 'لأن': followers are commanded to emulate the messengers. Ask yourself why that necessitates infallibility.
Think about contradiction: if a messenger sins, emulation would lead to sin.
4
Reflect on the misconception
Note that trustworthiness here is not limited to financial honesty but covers all aspects of conduct, internal and external.
This guards against a narrow understanding of amānah.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you grasp the proof structure.
The correct answer is B.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب لهم الأمانةُ ؛ أي : حفظ ظواهرهم وبواطنهم مِنَ الوقوع في محرَّم أو مكروه؛ لأن أتباعهم أمروا بالاقتداء بهم في جميع أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، وذلك يستلزم عصمتهم فيها مِنْ كلَّ منهي عنه
And trustworthiness (al-amānah) is obligatory for them, meaning: preservation of their outward and inward aspects from falling into something forbidden or disliked; because their followers have been commanded to emulate them in all their words and deeds, and that necessitates their infallibility (ʿiṣmah) in these matters from everything prohibited.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines the second necessary attribute: trustworthiness (amānah). It defines amānah as the preservation (ḥifẓ) of both their outward actions (ẓawāhir) and inward states (bawāṭin) from falling into the forbidden (ḥarām) or the disliked (makrūh). The proof for this obligation is that their followers have been commanded to imitate (al-iqtidāʾ) them in all their words and deeds. This command to imitate would be impossible if the messengers themselves could commit prohibited acts, because that would lead to contradiction. Therefore, this necessitates their infallibility (ʿiṣmah) from everything forbidden.

Key Terms
الأمانة
العصمة
الاقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Trustworthiness only means not stealing or being honest in financial matters.
Correction: Trustworthiness for messengers includes preservation from all forbidden and disliked actions, both outward and inward.

Checkpoint

A) The miracle confirms their trustworthiness.
B) Followers are commanded to emulate them, so they must be infallible.
C) They are protected by Allah from all sin by nature.
D) They cannot commit any sin because they are angels.

Key Takeaway
Trustworthiness (amānah) means messengers are preserved from all sin, outward and inward, because their followers are commanded to emulate them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are commanded to emulate the Prophet ﷺ in all your words and deeds. Is there any area of your life where you knowingly follow your own desires rather than his example? What one specific change will you make today to align your actions more closely with his?
?
Sanusi proves that messengers must be free from all sin because of this command to emulate. How seriously do you take that command? If your inward thoughts and outward actions were examined against the Prophet's, where would you fall short? What hidden sin (inward or outward) are you tolerating that you need to repent from right now?
?
The attribute of trustworthiness includes preservation from both forbidden and disliked actions. Are you content with avoiding major sins only, while neglecting the 'minor' disliked matters? How does this lesson challenge your understanding of following the Prophet comprehensively?

The Obligation of Delivery for Messengers (al-Tablīgh)
Sanusi defines the wajib attribute of delivery (tablīgh) and gives its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational necessity of the attribute of tablīgh (delivery) for prophets, and how it is supported by trustworthiness and consensus.

Core Idea
Prophets must deliver every command perfectly—neither omission nor forgetfulness is allowed.

Sanusi continues his enumeration of the necessary attributes of prophets. Having established their trustworthiness, he now shows why complete delivery of the message is a logical requirement. This passage defines tablīgh and provides two proofs for why a prophet can neither intentionally nor forgetfully omit any part of the revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two types of omission
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi mentions two reasons why a prophet might leave out something: forgetfulness (nisyān) and intentional (ʿamdan).
2
Understand the proof against intentional omission
Sanusi refers back to the attribute of trustworthiness (amānah). Intentional omission would be a betrayal, which is impossible for a prophet.
3
Understand the proof against forgetful omission
For forgetfulness, Sanusi invokes consensus (ijmāʿ) of the scholars that prophets are protected from forgetfulness in matters of delivery.
This is a specific consensus among Muslim scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب لهم أيضاً أنَّهم بلغوا كلَّ ما أمرهم المولى سبحانَهُ بتبليغه ، ولم يتركوا شيئاً منهُ ، لا نسياناً ولا عمداً ، أما عمداً فلما سبق في الأمانة ، وأما نسياناً فللإجماع .
And it is also obligatory for them that they have delivered everything that the Lord, glorified be He, commanded them to deliver, and they did not leave out anything from it, neither out of forgetfulness nor intentionally. As for intentionally, it is due to what preceded in [the proof of] trustworthiness; and as for forgetfully, it is due to consensus (al-ijmāʿ).
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage defines the third necessary attribute: delivery (tablīgh). The author states that it is obligatory for messengers that they have delivered everything that Allah commanded them to deliver, and they did not omit anything from it, neither due to forgetfulness (nisyān) nor intentionally (ʿamdan). The proof for the prohibition of intentional omission is derived from what was already established in the proof of trustworthiness—since intentional concealment would be a form of treachery. The proof for the prohibition of forgetful omission is consensus (ijmāʿ) of the scholars that prophets are protected from forgetfulness in matters of delivery.

Key Terms
التبليغ
الإجماع
النسيان
الأمانة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets might accidentally forget to deliver some parts of the revelation.
Correction: Consensus of scholars establishes that prophets are protected from forgetfulness in matters of delivery.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why is it impossible for a messenger to intentionally omit part of what he was commanded to deliver?
A) Because that would be a lie.
B) Because it would contradict his trustworthiness (amānah).
C) Because there is consensus against it.
D) Because miracles prevent forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must deliver every part of the revelation without any omission, whether intentional or forgetful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If prophets are obligated to deliver every command without omission, how often do you withhold a truth when it is uncomfortable to share? What command of Allah are you neglecting to convey to those around you?
?
The prophets protected even from forgetfulness—yet you forget to act on what you know. What prevents you from taking the commands you know and implementing them fully, without excuse?
?
Reflect on the trustworthiness of the prophets: they never intentionally omitted anything. Is there any area in your life where you deliberately choose not to follow a command of Allah, knowing it is required? What will you change today?

Interrelations of the Three Wajib Attributes
Sanusi analyses the interrelations, overlaps, and distinctions of the three wajib attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three wajib attributes of messengers (truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery) relate to each other, what each uniquely adds, and what they share in common.

Core Idea
Each wajib attribute of messengers has a distinct function that the others do not cover.

Sanusi now deepens our understanding of the three essential attributes of messengers: truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amānah), and delivery (tablīgh). Rather than treating them as separate items, he shows how they interlock and complement each other. This passage is a precise logical analysis that reveals the unique contribution of each attribute and the overlaps between them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage closely
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the translation. Pay attention to the pattern of 'adds to... by preventing...'.
Notice that each attribute is defined both positively and negatively.
2
Identify the three attributes being compared
The passage compares truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amānah), and delivery (tablīgh). Note which one is called 'the first obligatory attribute'.
3
Trace the specific additions for each attribute
Follow the text to see what ṣidq adds to amānah and to tablīgh; what amānah adds to ṣidq and to tablīgh; and what tablīgh adds to ṣidq and to amānah.
Keep a mental or written note of each addition.
4
Reflect on the concluding remark
After the detailed comparisons, Sanusi says you can derive what the three share, what two share without the third, and what each one adds over the sum of the other two. Try to infer those from the analysis.
This is the key takeaway – the attributes have both common ground and unique functions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالواجبُ الأَوَّلُ يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً ، ويزيدُ على التبليغ بمنع الزيادة على ما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً ، وتزيد الأمانة على الصدق بمنع وقوع المخالفة في كذب اللسانِ ، وعلى التبليغ بمنع المخالفة في غيرِ التبليغ ، ويزيدُ التبليغ على الصدق بمنع ترْكِ شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً ، مع لزومِ الصدق فيما بلغوا مِنْ ذلك ، ويزيد على الأمانة بمنع تركِ شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه نسياناً . ولا يخفى عليك بعد هذا ما تشترك فيه الثلاثةُ ، وما يشترك فيه اثنان منها ، دونَ الثالث ، وما يزيدُ به كلُّ واحد منها على مجموع الباقيين .
The first obligatory [attribute, i.e., al-ṣidq] adds to trustworthiness (al-amānah) by preventing [inadvertent] lying (al-kadhib sahwan), and adds to delivery (al-tablīgh) by preventing addition to what they were commanded to deliver, intentionally or forgetfully. Trustworthiness adds to truthfulness by preventing the occurrence of violation in the lying of the tongue, and adds to delivery by preventing violation in other than delivery. Delivery adds to truthfulness by preventing the omission of something they were commanded to deliver, intentionally or forgetfully, with the necessity of truthfulness in what they deliver from that, and adds to trustworthiness by preventing the omission of something they were commanded to deliver forgetfully. And it is not hidden from you after this what the three share in common, and what two of them share without the third, and what each one adds over the sum of the remaining two.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed comparative analysis of the three wajib attributes: truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amānah), and delivery (tablīgh). The author systematically explains what each attribute adds beyond the others. The first attribute (ṣidq) adds to amānah by preventing inadvertent lying (kadhib sahwan), which amānah does not cover. It adds to tablīgh by preventing adding to the message. Amānah adds to ṣidq by preventing contradiction in the tongue's lie, and to tablīgh by preventing violation in actions other than delivery. Tablīgh adds to ṣidq by preventing omission (whether intentional or forgetful), and to amānah by preventing forgetful omission. At the end, the author notes that from this analysis one can derive the commonalities between the three, the commonalities between any two, and what each one uniquely adds beyond the sum of the other two.

Key Terms
الزيادة
الاشتراك
الكذب سهواً

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The three wajib attributes are identical in meaning.
Correction: Each attribute has a unique function that the others do not cover, as shown by the analysis.

Checkpoint
What does al-ṣidq (truthfulness) add that al-amānah (trustworthiness) does not cover?
A) Preventing intentional lies.
B) Preventing inadvertent lies (kadhib sahwan).
C) Preventing omission of the message.
D) Preventing addition to the message.

Key Takeaway
The three wajib attributes of messengers are distinct yet complementary, each covering a different potential flaw in prophetic communication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak about your religion, do you guard against both intentional and inadvertent errors? How often do you correct a mistake you made unintentionally, and does your conscience consider that a breach of amānah?
?
In your daily interactions, do you act on the principle that truthfulness must be paired with trustworthiness and full delivery? Where have you omitted part of a message that should have been conveyed, and what did that reveal about your own character?
?
Which of the three attributes—ṣidq, amānah, tablīgh—is weakest in your own life right now? What specific step will you take today to strengthen it, knowing that the prophets embodied all three perfectly as a standard?

Impossible and Permissible Attributes for Messengers
Sanusi enumerates impossible and permissible attributes for messengers with safeguards.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the impossible and permissible attributes for messengers, including the safeguards that clarify the proper understanding of their human experiences.

Core Idea
Messengers are immune to lying and treachery but experience human needs like illness.

Sanusi completes his discussion of prophetic attributes by addressing what cannot be attributed to messengers (the opposites of the three wajib attributes) and what can: human accidents that do not diminish their rank. He then introduces three safeguards to prevent common theological errors, such as deifying Jesus or denying the compatibility of humanity with prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the two categories and the safeguards.
Notice the concise style and technical terms like 'aḍdād' and 'iḥtirāzāt'.
2
Identify the two categories
Locate the sections on impossible (mustaḥīl) and permissible (jāʾiz) attributes. Note that impossible is defined as the opposites of the three wajib attributes.
The three wajib attributes are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveying the message.
3
Examine the evidence for permissible attributes
Sanusi gives evidence: observation (mushāhadah) of illness in prophets and hidden benefits. Reflect on why this empirical proof is sufficient.
This shows that kalam uses both rational and empirical evidence.
4
Study the three safeguards (iḥtirāzāt)
Each safeguard clarifies a term to prevent a specific doctrinal error. The first guards against Christian deification of Jesus, the second against the pre-Islamic denial of humanity in prophethood, and the third (partial) guards against attributing degrading traits.
The third safeguard is incomplete in the text but the purpose is clear from context.
5
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider how these safeguards establish a balanced view of prophets: fully human yet protected from sin and deficiency.
This balance is crucial for Islamic orthodoxy.

As for what is impossible (al-mustaḥīl) for them, upon them peace and blessings: they are the opposites (aḍdād) of these three [wajib attributes]. As for what is permissible (al-jāʾiz) for them, upon them peace and blessings: they are the human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyyah) that do not conflict with the loftiness of their rank, such as illness and the like, as evidenced by the observation of that in them, and in their being described with them there are benefits that are not hidden. Our statement 'the accidents' (al-aʿrāḍ) is a safeguard (iḥtirāz) against the doctrine of the Christians in their description of Jesus, peace be upon him, with the eternal attribute. And our statement 'that do not conflict with the loftiness of their rank' is a safeguard against the belief of the Jews and many ignorant historians and exegetes describing...

Commentary
This passage covers the remaining categories: impossible (mustaḥīl) and permissible (jāʾiz) attributes for messengers. For impossible, it is the direct opposites (aḍdād) of the three wajib attributes: lying, treachery, and concealment. For permissible, it lists human accidents (aʿrāḍ bashariyyah) that do not contradict their high rank, like illness. The evidence is empirical observation of such states in prophets. Then the author provides three iḥtirāzāt (safeguards) to clarify the wording. 'Al-aʿrāḍ' (accidents) excludes the Christian belief that Jesus had an eternal attribute (divinity). 'Al-bashariyyah' excludes the pre-Islamic belief that humanity is incompatible with prophethood. 'Illā lan yuqāraba' excludes the Jewish and ignorant historians who attribute to prophets.

The Three Obligatory Attributes of Prophets
Sanusi enumerates the three obligatory attributes of prophets and their logical relations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three attributes that are obligatory for prophets—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance—and how they interrelate.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and convey the message fully—even if forgetful.

Sanusi begins by establishing the core attributes that every prophet must possess. These attributes define their mission and ensure the integrity of revelation. In this passage, he enumerates three obligatory qualities and explains how they relate to one another.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about the three attributes
Read the Arabic and translation to get a sense of the classification.
2
Identify each attribute
Find truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance. Note the specific requirement for each.
Conveyance includes both deliberate and forgetful transmission.
3
Understand the interrelation
Reflect on what the three share, what two share without the third, and what each uniquely adds.
4
Apply the concept
Consider why this classification is important for understanding prophetic infallibility.
These attributes ensure the message is delivered reliably.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً ، مع لزومِ الصدق فيما بلغوا مِنْ ذلك ، ويزيد على الأمانة بمنع تركِ شيء مما أُمروا بتبليغه نسياناً .
ولا يخفى عليك بعد هذا ما تشترك فيه الثلاثةُ ، وما يشترك فيه اثنان منها ، دونَ الثالث ، وما يزيدُ به كلُّ واحد منها على مجموع الباقيين .
وأما المستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام :
فأضداد هذه الثلاثة
وأما الجائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فالأعراض البشريَّةُ التي لا تنافي علوّ رتبتهم ؛ كالمرضِ ونحوه ، بدليل مشاهدة ذلك فيهم ، وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا تخفى .
فقولنا : ( الأعراضُ ( احتراز مِنْ مذهب النصارى في وصفهم عيسى عليه السلام بالصفة القديمة
وقولنا : ( البشريَّةُ ( احتراز من اعتقادِ الجاهلية أنَّ البشريّة تنافي الرسالة
وقولنا : ( التي لا تنافي علو رتبتهم ( احترازُ مِن اعتقادِ اليهود وكثيرٍ مِنْ جهلةِ المؤرّخين والمفسرين اتصاف الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام بنقيصة المعصية والمكروه ونحوهما
•
وبهذا تعرفُ أنَّ كلَّ ما أوهم في حقهم أو حق الملائكة نقصاً مِنَ الكتاب أو السنة .. وجب تأويله .
They were commanded to convey it deliberately or forgetfully, while truthfulness is necessary in what they conveyed from that, and it adds to trustworthiness by prohibiting leaving out anything they were commanded to convey forgetfully. And it is not hidden from you after this what the three share, and what two of them share without the third, and what each one of them adds over the sum of the remaining two. As for the impossible in their right (upon them peace and blessings): they are the opposites of these three. As for the permissible in their right (upon them peace and blessings): they are human accidents that do not contradict their high rank, like illness and the like, evidenced by observing that in them, and in their being characterized by them are benefits that are not hidden. Our saying: 'accidents' is a caveat against the doctrine of the Christians in their describing Jesus (peace be upon him) with the eternal attribute. Our saying: 'human' is a caveat against the belief of the ignorant that humanity contradicts prophethood. Our saying: 'that do not contradict their high rank' is a caveat against the belief of the Jews and many of the ignorant historians and exegetes that the prophets (upon them peace and blessings) are characterized by the deficiency of sin, the disliked, and the like. And by this you know that everything that implies deficiency in their right or the right of the angels from the Book or the Sunnah must be interpreted.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the attributes of prophets (anbiya) into three categories: obligatory (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and permissible (ja'iz). It begins by discussing the obligatory attributes, specifically focusing on three: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveyance (tabligh). The text explains that prophets were commanded to convey the message whether deliberately or forgetfully—meaning they cannot omit anything even if they forget, which is an extension of trustworthiness. Truthfulness is necessary in what they convey. Then it notes that these three attributes share commonalities and differences, and each one adds something unique over the other two. Next, the impossible attributes are simply the opposites of these three (e.g., lying, betrayal, concealment of the message). The permissible attributes are human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) that do not contradict their high rank, such as illness, which is evidenced by observation. The text then provides three caveats (ihtirazat) to the definition: 'accidents' excludes the Christian belief that Jesus had an eternal attribute; 'human' excludes those who think humanity negates prophethood; 'that do not contradict their high rank' excludes those who attribute sin or disliked actions to prophets. Finally, it concludes that any apparent deficiency regarding prophets or angels in the Quran or Sunnah must be interpreted (ta'wil) to preserve their perfection.

Key Terms
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) To convey deliberately or forgetfully without omitting anything
D) To convey only the easy parts

Key Takeaway
Prophets must possess truthfulness, trustworthiness, and fullness of conveyance, with each attribute reinforcing the others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The passage links truthfulness to trustworthiness: being honest in what you say strengthens your reliability. In your daily interactions, where do you downplay or omit truths to make things easier for yourself? How does that undermine your trustworthiness in the eyes of others and of Allah?

What is Impossible and Permissible for Prophets
Sanusi classifies the impossible and permissible attributes of prophets with caveats and the rule of interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what attributes are impossible for prophets (their opposites of the obligatory) and what is permissible for them (human accidents that do not contradict their rank), along with the principle that any apparent deficiency must be interpreted.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot have any deficiency, but they can have ordinary human conditions like illness, and any scriptural suggestion otherwise must be interpreted.

Having established the obligatory attributes, Sanusi now turns to what is impossible and permissible for prophets. The impossible attributes are simply the opposites of the obligatory ones. The permissible attributes are human experiences that do not lower their status. He also provides three important caveats to ensure correct understanding and concludes with a rule for interpreting apparent deficiencies in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on impossible and permissible attributes
Read the Arabic and translation to see the full classification.
2
Understand the impossible attributes
Note that the impossible are the direct opposites of the three obligatory attributes.
3
Analyze the permissible attributes
Identify the definition of permissible as human accidents that do not contradict high rank, and study the three caveats.
Each caveat refutes a specific false belief.
4
Learn the rule of ta'wil
Understand that any apparent deficiency in scripture must be interpreted to preserve the perfection of prophets and angels.
5
Reflect on the benefits
Consider why these caveats and the rule of interpretation are important for correct belief.

The Obligation of Ta'wil for Apparent Deficiencies
Sanusi states the obligation of ta'wil for texts implying deficiency in prophets or angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation of figurative interpretation (ta'wil) for any scriptural text that appears to imply a deficiency in prophets or angels.

Core Idea
Any text implying deficiency in prophets or angels must be interpreted, not rejected.

This lesson presents a crucial hermeneutical principle in Sunni theology: when a Qur'anic verse or hadith seems to attribute a deficiency to a prophet or an angel, it must be interpreted figuratively (ta'wil). This preserves both the authority of revelation and the doctrine of 'isma (impeccability). As you read Sanusi's words, notice how the principle flows from the established truth that prophets are free from sin and disliked things.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow from the initial statement about prophets to the rule of ta'wil.
The first phrase is a continuation from the previous page.
2
Identify the key claim
Find the sentence that states what must be done with any text that suggests a deficiency. Underline or note the phrase 'وجب تأويله'.
3
Connect to 'isma
Reflect on why ta'wil is necessary: because prophets and angels are impeccable ('isma). The passage begins by affirming they are free from sin and disliked things.
4
Distinguish ta'wil from rejection
Note that the rule requires interpretation, not rejection. This is a key difference: the text remains authoritative but is understood metaphorically.
A common mistake is to think such texts should be dismissed.
5
Review the closing doxology
The passage ends with praise of the Prophet, his family, companions, and the traditional formula. Reflect on the devotional tone as a fitting conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام بنقيصة المعصية والمكروه ونحوهما • وبهذا تعرفُ أنَّ كلَّ ما أوهم في حقهم أو حق الملائكة نقصاً مِنَ الكتاب أو السنة .. وجب تأويله . وأفضلهم سيّدنا ومولانا محمَّدٌ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ وعلى آلِهِ عدَدَ ما ذكرَهُ الذاكرون وغفل عن ذكره الغافلون ، ورضي الله تعالى عن أصحاب رسولِ اللهِ أجمعين ، وسلام على المرسلين ، والحمدُ للهِ ربِّ العالمينَ .
The prophets, upon them prayer and peace, with deficiency of sin and disliked things and their like. • And by this you know that everything that suggests in their right or the right of the angels deficiency from the Book or the Sunnah .. its interpretation (ta'wil) is obligatory. And the best of them is our master and patron Muhammad, may God bless him and his family, to the number of what the rememberers remember and the heedless neglect, and may God be pleased with all the companions of the Messenger of God, and peace upon the messengers, and praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage concludes a discussion on the impeccable status of prophets and angels. The first phrase (likely continuing from earlier) establishes that prophets are not associated with deficiency, sin, or disliked things. The author then draws a hermeneutical rule: any text from the Qur'an or Sunnah that appears to imply a deficiency (naqs) in prophets or angels must be interpreted figuratively (ta'wil). This principle safeguards the doctrine of 'isma (impeccability) while maintaining the authority of revelation. The passage ends with praise of the Prophet Muhammad, a prayer for him and his family, and a request for God's pleasure upon the Companions, followed by the traditional closing formula.

Key Terms
تأويل (ta'wil)
نقص (naqs)
عصمة ('isma)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any text implying deficiency should be rejected as unreliable.
Correction: The author insists on interpretation (ta'wil) rather than rejection, preserving both the text's authority and the doctrine of 'isma.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what must be done with anything from the Book or Sunnah that seems to imply a deficiency in prophets or angels?
A) It must be rejected as unreliable.
B) It must be interpreted figuratively (ta'wil).
C) It must be accepted literally.
D) It must be ignored.

Key Takeaway
When a scriptural text seems to imply a deficiency in a prophet or angel, it must be interpreted figuratively, not taken literally or rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage ends with praising the Prophet Muhammad as the best. Do you truly place him above all others in your heart? If your actions do not reflect this – for example, if you follow social media trends over his sunnah – what can you change starting now to honour his station?

The Prophet as the Supreme Door to Allah's Pleasure
Sanusi venerates the Prophet as the supreme means to Allah's pleasure and the purpose of creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi positions the Prophet Muhammad as the supreme means to Allah's pleasure and the very purpose of creation.

Core Idea
The Prophet is not just a guide; he is the door and the reason for creation.

Sanusi opens this passage by declaring that the highest of all perfections is attaining Allah's pleasure and safety from His wrath. He then presents the Prophet Muhammad as the unique, incomparable door to this happiness in both worlds. The passage culminates in the profound statement that all creation—earthly and heavenly—was created for the Prophet's sake, and his intercession removes all calamities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Pay attention to the rhetorical question near the end.
The passage uses a question to emphasize the Prophet's central role.
2
Identify the central claim

The Prophet is described as incomparable.
3
Analyze the rhetorical question
The author asks 'How? And for his sake Allah created all perfections...' Understand that this answers why the Prophet is the supreme door.
This connects the Prophet to the purpose of creation.
4
Reflect on intercession
The passage concludes with the Prophet's intercession that removes calamities. Consider how intercession reinforces his role as the door.
Intercession is a key concept in Sunni theology.

The argument establishes the central role of the Prophet in both worldly and eternal felicity.

Obligation of Gratitude and Virtue of Salawat
Author states the obligation to thank Allah for the Prophet and the merit of sending blessings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why thanking Allah for the Prophet and sending blessings upon him are among the most important acts of devotion.

Core Idea
Gratitude for the Prophet and sending salawat are the highest means to Allah's favor.

This passage from Sanusi's work highlights the profound obligation to thank Allah for the blessing of the Prophet Muhammad (saw) and the immense virtue of sending blessings upon him. It grounds this practice in both rational recognition of the Prophet's station and authentic hadith, even linking it to spiritual development. Let's explore these teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the author's tone and the key terms like 'tawassul' and 'salawat'.
The passage begins with a strong statement about obligation.
2
Identify the two main claims
Find where the author states the obligation of praising Allah for the Prophet and the virtue of sending blessings. Also note the proof from authentic hadith.
The conditional argument 'If you know... then you know' is important.
3
Reflect on the practical implication
Consider how the author uses the hadith and the Sufi saying to encourage frequent salawat. Ask yourself how this applies to your own spiritual practice.
The saying about those without teachers is especially striking.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حمد الله تعالى على نعمة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام من أوجب الواجبات، والتوسل به من أعلى الوسائل للفوز بعلي الدرجات. وإذا عرفت أن منزلة سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم عند مولانا جل وعلا بهذه المثابة.. عرفت أن حمده تعالى وشكره على إنعامه به على الخلق من أوجب الواجبات، وأن التوسل إليه تعالى بحب هذا السيد، والتعظيم له، وكثرة الصلاة والتسليم عليه.. من أعلى الوسائل للأمن من المخوفات، والفوز بعلي الدرجات. ولو لم يكن للصلاة عليه من الفضل العظيم إلا ما ورد في الصحاح: أن من صلى على سيدنا ومولانا محمد عليه الصلاة والسلام مرة صلى الله عليه بها عشراً.. لكان كافياً، كيف وقد ورد في فضلها العظيم ما ألف أئمتنا فيه على الانفراد تأليف عديدة؟! وقد رأيت لبعض أئمة التصرف: أن من فقد شيوخ التربية.. فليكثر من الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم؛ فإنه يصل به إلى مقصده، ولعله أخذ ذلك من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لأبي هريرة رضي الله عنه عندما التزم أن يجعل جميع صلاته للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: (إذا تُكفى همك، ويغفر ذنبك).
Praising Allah Almighty for the blessing of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, is one of the most obligatory duties, and seeking intercession through him is among the highest means for attaining lofty degrees. And if you know that the station of our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, is of such magnitude... then you know that praising and thanking Him for His bestowal of him upon creation is one of the most obligatory duties, and that seeking intercession to Him through love of this master, veneration of him, and frequent prayer and salutation upon him... are among the highest means for safety from fears and for attaining lofty degrees. And if there were no great virtue for prayer upon him except what has been related in the authentic collections: that whoever prays upon our master and lord Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, once, Allah prays upon him ten times by it... that would be sufficient. How so, when there has been related concerning its great virtue what our imams have authored individually in numerous works?! And I have seen from some of the masters of spiritual discipline: that whoever lacks the teachers of spiritual training... then let him increase prayer upon the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him; for it will bring him to his goal. And perhaps he took that from his saying, peace and blessings be upon him, to Abu Hurairah, may Allah be pleased with him, when he committed to making all his prayers upon the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him: (Then your concern will be taken care of, and your sin will be forgiven).
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a devotional exhortation and proof of the high station of the Prophet Muhammad (saw). The author begins by stating that praising Allah for the blessing of the Prophet is one of the most obligatory duties, and that seeking intercession (tawassul) through him is among the highest means to attain lofty degrees in the Hereafter. He then draws a conditional argument: if you truly understand the immense rank of the Prophet with Allah, then you will recognize the obligation of thanking Allah for sending him, and that the means to divine protection and high ranks are through love, veneration, and frequent prayers and greetings upon him. The author supports this with a hadith from the authentic collections: whoever sends blessings upon the Prophet once, Allah sends ten blessings upon him. Even this alone would be sufficient incentive. But further, the author notes that the scholars have written many works on the great virtue of salawat, implying even more merit. He then quotes a saying from some Sufi masters: if a person lacks a spiritual teacher (shaykh), they should increase salawat, for it will lead them to their goal. He suggests this is derived from the hadith where the Prophet told Abu Hurairah that if he makes all his prayer salawat upon the Prophet, his worldly concerns will be removed and his sins forgiven. Thus, the passage emphasizes the centrality of gratitude and devotion to the Prophet as a means to Allah's favor.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي
التوسل
حمد الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that tawassul (seeking intercession) is limited to asking directly, excluding love and veneration.
Correction: The passage includes love, veneration, and frequent salawat as part of tawassul, which are among the highest means.

Checkpoint

A) Fasting in Ramadan
B) Praising Allah for the blessing of the Prophet

Key Takeaway
