The Relationship Between Truthfulness, Trustworthiness, and Delivery
Sanusi enumerates how each prophetic duty exceeds the others in scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each prophetic duty (truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivery) has a unique prohibitive scope that exceeds the others.

Core Idea
Each prophetic duty forbids something the others do not.

This passage from Sanusi's work on prophethood clarifies the precise relationship between the three essential prophetic duties. While they are all required, each duty carries prohibitions that go beyond the others. The author uses a comparative method to show how each duty 'surpasses' the others in specific aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the heading and identify the three duties.
The title mentions 'generalities and specificities' among truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery. Write down these three duties.
These are the three essential prophetic duties.
2
Notice the pattern of 'surpassing'.
Each duty is said to 'surpass' another in a specific prohibition. Look for the Arabic phrase 'يزيد على' (surpasses) and note the pattern.
There are six comparisons total.
3
List the six comparisons.
Go through each sentence and identify which duty surpasses which other duty and in what way. For example: truthfulness surpasses trustworthiness by forbidding forgetful lying.
You can create a table to organize the comparisons.
4
Reflect on the significance for prophethood.
Why does it matter that each duty has a unique scope? This ensures that the prophets are fully trustworthy in all aspects of their mission.
5
Test your understanding with the checkpoint.
Answer the multiple-choice question to see if you can identify how delivery surpasses truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عمومات وخصوصات وجهية بين الصدق والأمانة والتبليغ ]
فالواجبُ الأَوَّلُ يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً ، ويزيدُ على التبليغ بمنع الزيادة على ما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً، وتزيدُ الأمانة على الصدق بمنع وقوع المخالفة في غير كذب اللسانِ ، وعلى التبليغ بمنعِ المخالفة في غيرِ التبليغ ويزيد التبليغ على الصدق بمنع ترك شيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً ، مع لزومِ الصدق فيما بلغوا مِنْ ذلكَ(٢) ويزيد على الأمانة بمنع ترك شيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه نسياناً
Generalities and specificities between truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery: The first duty surpasses trustworthiness by forbidding lying even forgetfully, and surpasses delivery by forbidding adding to what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully. Trustworthiness surpasses truthfulness by forbidding the occurrence of contradiction in other than lying of the tongue, and surpasses delivery by forbidding contradiction in other than delivery. Delivery surpasses truthfulness by forbidding leaving out anything of what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully, with the necessity of truthfulness in what they delivered from that, and surpasses trustworthiness by forbidding leaving out anything of what they were commanded to deliver forgetfully.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a classification and comparison of the three essential prophetic duties: truthfulness (الصدق), trustworthiness (الأمانة), and delivery (التبليغ). The heading indicates that these duties have 'generalities and specificities' (عمومات وخصوصات) in relation to each other. The author then enumerates six comparisons: (1) Truthfulness surpasses trustworthiness by forbidding forgetful lying. (2) Truthfulness surpasses delivery by forbidding adding to the message. (3) Trustworthiness surpasses truthfulness by forbidding any contradiction not limited to verbal lying (e.g., actions). (4) Trustworthiness surpasses delivery by forbidding contradiction in matters other than the specific duty of delivery. (5) Delivery surpasses truthfulness by forbidding omission of any part of the message (even forgetfully) while still requiring truthfulness. (6) Delivery surpasses trustworthiness by forbidding forgetful omission. This shows the unique prohibitive scope of each duty.

Key Terms
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ
الواجب الأول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery are identical in scope.
Correction: The passage shows that each duty has a unique prohibitive scope, forbidding something the others do not.

Checkpoint

B) By forbidding adding to the message

Key Takeaway
Each prophetic duty has a unique prohibitive scope that distinguishes it from the others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The duty of trustworthiness forbids contradiction outside of verbal lies. Look at your daily life: where do your actions contradict what you claim to believe? What one step can you take to align your behavior with your faith?

The Unique Relationships Among the Three Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi explains the unique relationships between sidq, amanah, and tabligh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the three obligatory prophetic attributes (sidq, amanah, tabligh) are distinct and not redundant, each covering a unique deficiency that the others do not address.

Core Idea
Each prophetic attribute forbids a specific deficiency that the others do not cover.

Sanusi begins by emphasizing that the three prophetic attributes—truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amanah), and delivery (tabligh)—are not merely redundant or synonymous. He explains that each attribute has a unique scope, and together they protect against all possible deficiencies in prophethood. This lesson unpacks his careful analysis of how each attribute adds something the others do not.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the full translation. Notice the technical terms sidq, amanah, tabligh and how they are compared.
Pay attention to the phrase 'عموم وخصوص من وجه' which is key to the argument.
2
Identify the three increases
Find where Sanusi states that each attribute 'increases' (يزيد) over the others. List each increase and what deficiency it forbids.
There are three main comparisons: sidq over amanah, sidq over tabligh, amanah over tabligh, and then another pair.
3
Understand the relationship type
Sanusi says the attributes are related by 'عموم وخصوص من وجه' (general and specific from one aspect). This means each attribute overlaps with the others but also has a unique part. Understand why this prevents redundancy.
Contrast this with absolute generality or equality.
4
Analyze the examples
Sanusi gives two examples: why unintentional lying is forbidden by sidq, not amanah, and why adding to the message is forbidden by sidq, not tabligh. Make sure you see the reasoning.
These examples illustrate the practical implication of the relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالواجبُ الأَوَّلُ يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً، ويزيدُ على التبليغ بمنع الزيادة على ما أمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً، وتزيدُ الأمانة على الصدق بمنع وقوع المخالفة في غير كذب اللسانِ، وعلى التبليغ بمنعِ المخالفة في غيرِ التبليغ ويزيد التبليغ على الصدق بمنع ترك شيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً، مع لزومِ الصدق فيما بلغوا مِنْ ذلكَ ويزيد على الأمانة بمنع ترك شيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه نسياناً. إنَّما تعرَّضنا في أصل العقيدة لِمَا بينَ هذهِ الواجباتِ الثلاثةِ مِنَ النَّسَبِ؛ لئلا يُتوهَّمَ أَنَّ فيها تكراراً، أو أن فيها ترادفاً أو تساوياً، أو عموماً وخصوصاً بإطلاق؛ بحيثُ يُستغنى بالأخص عن الأعم؛ فنبَّهنا على أن بينها عموماً وخصوصاً مِنْ وجه، فلا يمكن حينئذ الاستغناء ببعضها عن بعض؛ لأنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ يزيد على صاحبيهِ بزيادة لا تفهم إلا منه. وبيانُ ذلكَ: أنَّ الواجبَ الأول - وهو الصّدقُ - يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً؛ أي: هذهِ النقيصةُ إِنَّما يُفهَمُ امتناعها في حقٌّ الرسل عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنَ الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدقُ؛ لأنَّه عام في كل قول، ولا يُفهَمُ امتناعُها مِنَ الواجب الثاني الذي هو الأمانةُ؛ لأنَّها إِنَّما تَمنَعُ مِنْ وقوع المعصية والمكروه، والكذب سهواً ليس بحرام ولا مكروه، فلا منافاة بينه وبين الأمانة. ويزيدُ أيضاً الصدقُ على الواجب الثالث، الذي هو التبليغ العام، بمنع الزيادةِ على ما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً؛ أي: هذهِ النقيصة لا تُفهَمُ مِنَ الواجب الثالث؛ لأنَّها وقعَتْ بعد التبليغ العام.
The first obligation increases over trustworthiness by forbidding lying unintentionally, and increases over delivery by forbidding addition to what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully. And trustworthiness increases over truthfulness by forbidding occurrence of opposition in other than lying of the tongue, and over delivery by forbidding opposition in other than delivery. And delivery increases over truthfulness by forbidding leaving anything of what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully, along with the necessity of truthfulness in what they delivered of that, and increases over trustworthiness by forbidding leaving anything of what they were commanded to deliver forgetfully. We only addressed in the essence of the creed the relationship between these three obligations, lest it be imagined that there is repetition in them, or that there is synonymity or equality, or absolute generality and specificity, such that the specific suffices over the general. So we pointed out that between them there is generality and specificity from one aspect, so it is not possible then to suffice with some over others, because each one increases over its two companions by an increase not understood except from it. And the explanation of that is: the first obligation – and it is truthfulness – increases over trustworthiness by forbidding lying unintentionally; i.e., this deficiency, its prohibition is understood in the right of the messengers, peace be upon them, only from the first obligation which is truthfulness, because it is general in every speech, and its prohibition is not understood from the second obligation which is trustworthiness, because it only forbids occurrence of disobedience and detestable acts, and unintentional lying is not forbidden nor detestable, so there is no conflict between it and trustworthiness. And truthfulness also increases over the third obligation, which is general delivery, by forbidding addition to what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully; i.e., this deficiency is not understood from the third obligation, because it occurred after the general delivery.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is an analytical exposition of the relationship between the three obligatory prophetic attributes: sidq (truthfulness), amanah (trustworthiness), and tabligh (delivery of the message). The author first enumerates how each attribute uniquely adds to the others. Then he explains why he discussed this relationship: to prevent misunderstandings that these attributes are redundant, synonymous, equivalent, or related by absolute generality and specificity. Instead, they share a relationship of 'general and specific from one aspect' (umum wa khusus min wajh), meaning each attribute has a scope that overlaps with others but also has a unique extension. He then illustrates this with two examples: first, how sidq forbids unintentional lying, which amanah does not forbid because amanah only forbids sin and detestable acts, and unintentional lying is neither sin nor detestable. Second, how sidq forbids adding to the message intentionally or forgetfully, which tabligh does not forbid because that addition occurs after the delivery itself. Thus, each attribute contributes a distinct protection.

Key Terms
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ
العموم والخصوص من وجه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the three prophetic attributes (sidq, amanah, tabligh) are redundant or synonymous, i.e., they all essentially mean the same thing.
Correction: Sanusi shows that each attribute forbids a deficiency that the others do not. For example, unintentional lying is only forbidden by sidq, not by amanah. Thus, they are distinct and all necessary.

Checkpoint

D) Committing a sin

Key Takeaway
The three prophetic attributes are not redundant; each protects against a specific type of deficiency and together they ensure the integrity of prophethood.

The lesson shows that each attribute guards a unique form of deficiency. Why the Three Prophetic Duties Are Not Redundant
Sanusi explains the non-redundancy of the three prophetic duties by analyzing their unique scopes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi demonstrates that the three prophetic duties are not redundant by showing that truthfulness uniquely prohibits unintentional lying and adding to the message.

Core Idea
The three duties are not synonyms; each blocks a different fault.

Sanusi anticipated a possible confusion: if the duties overlap, maybe one suffices. He clarifies that they have a relationship of 'generality and specificity from one perspective', meaning each has its own unique coverage. Let's follow his reasoning to see why all three are necessary.

Guided Path
1
Recognize Sanusi's motivation
Notice that Sanusi begins by stating why he discussed the relationships among the three duties: to prevent the misunderstanding that they are repetitive or that one could substitute for another.
This shows the author is proactively addressing a potential objection.
2
Understand the logical relationship
Sanusi says the duties have 'generality and specificity from one perspective' (عموم وخصوص من وجه). This means each duty has a unique scope not covered by the other two, so none can replace another.
This is the key concept that resolves the apparent redundancy.
3
Examine truthfulness vs. trustworthiness
See how truthfulness adds to trustworthiness by prohibiting unintentional lying. Trustworthiness only forbids intentional disobedience, but lying unintentionally is neither forbidden nor disliked by trustworthiness—so truthfulness is needed.
Unintentional lying is not a sin, yet it is a defect of truthfulness.
4
Examine truthfulness vs. general delivery
Truthfulness also adds to general delivery by prohibiting adding to the message intentionally or forgetfully. General delivery only requires conveying the message; it doesn't forbid adding something extra, but truthfulness does because addition is a lie.
The addition occurs after delivery, so general delivery doesn't cover it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّما تعرَّضنا في أصل العقيدة لِمَا بينَ هذهِ الواجباتِ الثلاثةِ مِنَ النَّسَبِ؛ لئلا يُتوهَّمَ أَنَّ فيها تكراراً، أو أن فيها ترادفاً أو تساويا، أو عموماً وخصوصاً بإطلاق؛ بحيثُ يُستغنى بالأخص عن الأعم؛ فنبَّهنا على أن بينها عموماً وخصوصاً مِنْ وجه، فلا يمكن حينئذ الاستغناء ببعضها عن بعض؛ لأنَّ كلَّ واحدٍ يزيد على صاحبيهِ بزيادة لا تفهم إلا منه. وبيانُ ذلكَ: أنَّ الواجبَ الأول - وهو الصّدقُ - يزيدُ على الأمانة بمنع الكذب سهواً؛ أي: هذهِ النقيصةُ إِنَّما يُفهَمُ امتناعها في حقِّ الرسل عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنَ الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدقُ؛ لأنَّه عام في كل قول، ولا يُفهَمُ امتناعُها مِنَ الواجب الثاني الذي هو الأمانةُ؛ لأنَّها إِنَّما تَمنَعُ مِنْ وقوع المعصية والمكروه، والكذب سهواً ليس بحرام ولا مكروه، فلا منافاة بينه وبين الأمانة. ويزيدُ أيضاً الصدقُ على الواجب الثالث، الذي هو التبليغ العام، بمنع الزيادةِ على ما أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو نسياناً؛ أي: هذهِ النقيصة لا تُفهَمُ مِنَ الواجب الثالث؛ لأنَّها وقعَتْ بعد التبليغ العام، فلا تنافيه، وتُفهَمُ مِنَ الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدقُ؛ لأنَّ هذهِ الزيادةَ كذبٌ، ووجوب الصدقِ العام يدفعُهُ.
We only addressed in the foundation of doctrine the relationships among these three duties, lest it be imagined that there is repetition in them, or that there is synonymy or equivalence, or absolute generality and specificity, such that the more specific could suffice for the more general. So we alerted that between them there is generality and specificity from one perspective, and thus it is impossible to do without some in place of others, because each one adds to its two companions an increase that is not understood except from it. The explanation of that is: The first duty—which is truthfulness—adds to trustworthiness by preventing lying unintentionally, i.e., this deficiency is only understood to be prohibited in the case of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, from the first duty which is truthfulness, because it is general in every statement, and its prohibition is not understood from the second duty which is trustworthiness, because it only prevents the occurrence of disobedience and the disliked, and lying unintentionally is neither forbidden nor disliked, so there is no contradiction between it and trustworthiness. And truthfulness also adds to the third duty, which is general delivery, by preventing addition to what they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully; i.e., this deficiency is not understood from the third duty, because it occurred after the general delivery, so it does not contradict it, and it is understood from the first duty which is truthfulness, because this addition is a lie, and the obligation of general truthfulness repels it.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of why the three prophetic duties (truthfulness, trustworthiness, and general delivery of the message) are not redundant or overlapping in such a way that one could substitute for another. The author begins by stating that in the original discussion of divine matters ('aqida), he addressed the relational aspects among these three obligations. The purpose is to prevent misunderstanding: one might think the duties are merely repetitive, synonymous, equivalent, or related as absolute generality and specificity where the more specific could replace the more general. To counter this, he emphasizes that there is a relationship of 'generality and specificity from one perspective' (عموم وخصوص من وجه), which means each duty has a unique aspect that the others do not cover. Therefore, none can be omitted in favor of another, because each one adds something that is not understood from the others. Then he proceeds to demonstrate this. The first duty (truthfulness) is shown to add to the second duty (trustworthiness) by prohibiting unintentional lying. Trustworthiness only prohibits intentional disobedience or disliked acts; since unintentional lying is neither forbidden nor disliked, it is not covered by trustworthiness. Hence truthfulness uniquely fills this gap. Similarly, truthfulness adds to the third duty (general delivery) by prohibiting adding to the message intentionally or forgetfully. General delivery only covers the act of conveying; it does not address adding something extra, because that addition occurs after delivery. But that addition is a lie, so truthfulness prohibits it. Thus truthfulness is necessary beyond the other two.

العموم والخصوص من وجه

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The three prophetic duties are essentially the same obligation, so one could substitute for another.
Correction: Sanusi shows that each duty has a unique scope: truthfulness covers unintentional lies and additions to the message, which trustworthiness and general delivery do not cover. Thus, all three are necessary.

Checkpoint

B) Because truthfulness is the most important duty.
C) Because unintentional lying is not a sin, but it still violates trustworthiness.
D) Because the duty of trustworthiness is specifically about the act of conveying the message.

Key Takeaway
The three prophetic duties are not redundant; each has a unique scope, and truthfulness in particular covers unintentional lies and additions to the message that the other duties do not address.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If even an unintentional lie disqualifies a messenger from prophethood, what does this demand of you regarding your own casual, careless words? How many 'small' or 'accidental' untruths have you let slide this week, and what would it cost you to root them out?
?
The lesson shows that covering one duty (like being trustworthy in actions) does not exempt you from another (truthfulness in speech). In your life, where are you leaning on one good quality to avoid a more uncomfortable one? Will you examine today where you are 'trustworthy' yet still dishonest?
?
Prophets were never permitted to add their own words to God's message. When you speak about Islam, do you distinguish between what Allah revealed and what you have inferred or felt? Are you willing to be held accountable for every 'extra' you present as if it were from the Book?

How Trustworthiness and General Delivery Add to Truthfulness
Sanusi enumerates how the second and third duties add unique prohibitions beyond truthfulness and each other.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the duties of trustworthiness and general delivery each prohibit deficiencies that truthfulness alone does not cover, and how they interrelate.

Core Idea
Each prophetic duty covers what the others miss, ensuring complete protection from sin and omission.

Sanusi continues his analysis of the three essential duties of messengers. Having established truthfulness as the first duty, he now shows that trustworthiness and general delivery each add specific protections. Truthfulness alone cannot prevent non-linguistic sins or omission of the message; these require the additional duties. This passage clarifies the unique scope of each duty and how they complement one another.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three duties
Recall the three duties: truthfulness (ṣidq), trustworthiness (amāna), and general delivery (tablīgh ʿāmm). This passage compares the second and third with the first and with each other.
The passage assumes you already know what each duty entails.
2
Understand how trustworthiness adds to truthfulness
Sanusi explains that trustworthiness prohibits acts of disobedience or disliked actions that are not lies of the tongue, such as backbiting or illicit gazing. Truthfulness alone does not forbid these because they are not speech-acts.
3
See how trustworthiness adds to general delivery
Trustworthiness also prohibits disobedience unrelated to the act of conveying, like theft or deception. General delivery only covers the transmission of the message, so trustworthiness fills the gap.
4
Learn how general delivery adds to truthfulness
General delivery prohibits omitting any part of the message, intentionally or forgetfully. Truthfulness only ensures that what is said is true, but does not compel conveying everything; delivery ensures completeness.
Omission is not a lie because no false statement is made about the omitted part.

And as for the second duty—which is trustworthiness—it adds to the first duty—which is truthfulness—by preventing the occurrence of disobedience or the disliked in matters other than the lies of the tongue, such as backbiting, for example, and deliberate looking at a non-mahram woman without necessity. So this deficiency is only understood to be prohibited from the second duty, which is trustworthiness, because of its contradiction to disobedience and the disliked, and its prohibition is not understood from the obligation of truthfulness, because it is not a lie such that truthfulness would repel it. And trustworthiness also adds to the third duty—which is general delivery—by preventing disobedience that is not related to delivery, such as theft, for example, and deception and the like, and that is apparent. And as for the third duty—which is general delivery—it adds to the first duty—which is truthfulness—by preventing the omission of anything that they were commanded to deliver, intentionally or forgetfully, while they adhere to truthfulness in what they delivered of that. That is: this deficiency is also only understood to be prohibited in the case of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, from the third duty, which is general delivery, because omission intentionally or forgetfully contradicts the obligation of general delivery, and does not contradict the obligation of truthfulness, because he may be truthful in what he delivered and leave out something else extraneous to it, so his omission of delivering it is not a lie in itself, since he did not report anything about it nor in what he delivered, because of his truthfulness in it. And the obligation of general delivery also adds to the second duty, which is...

Commentary
This passage continues the demonstration of unique aspects of each duty, focusing on the second duty (trustworthiness) and the third duty (general delivery). Sanusi explains that trustworthiness adds to truthfulness by prohibiting acts that are disobedient or disliked but are not lies of the tongue—like backbiting or gazing at a non-mahram woman without necessity. Truthfulness alone does not cover these because they are not speech-acts. Trustworthiness also adds to general delivery by prohibiting disobedience unrelated to the act of conveying, such as theft or deception, which are not addressed by the delivery duty. Then Sanusi explains how general delivery adds to truthfulness: it prohibits omission of any part of the message, whether intentional or forgetful, even if the messenger is truthful in what he does deliver. Omission is not a lie because he has not spoken falsely about the omitted part—he simply did not transmit it. Truthfulness alone does not compel conveying everything; delivery ensures the message is fully transmitted. The text ends mid-sentence while beginning to explain how delivery adds to trustworthiness. This completion likely covers acts that are not disobedient but still violate delivery.

The Unique Contributions of Truthfulness, Trustworthiness, and Preaching
Sanusi enumerates how each prophetic obligation uniquely excludes imperfections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how each of the three prophetic obligations—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and general preaching—uniquely excludes specific imperfections that the other obligations cannot address.

Core Idea
No single prophetic attribute covers all imperfections; each has a distinct role.

In this passage, Sanusi systematically compares the three obligatory attributes of prophets: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and general preaching. He shows that while they overlap, each covers a specific type of imperfection that the others cannot prevent. Let us see how trustworthiness adds to truthfulness by preventing sins not involving lies, and how general preaching adds to both by preventing omissions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the additions of trustworthiness
Read the segment where Sanusi explains how trustworthiness adds to truthfulness by preventing sins like backbiting and unlawful looks. Note that truthfulness only prevents lies.
This shows the need for multiple attributes.
2
Read how trustworthiness adds to general preaching
Next, notice that trustworthiness also covers sins unrelated to preaching, such as theft and deceit, which general preaching does not address.
3
Read how general preaching adds to truthfulness
Now read how the obligation of general preaching prevents omission of the divine message, whether intentional or forgetful. Truthfulness only ensures truth in what is preached, not that everything is preached.
Forgetful omission is not a lie, so truthfulness cannot prevent it.
4
Read how general preaching adds to trustworthiness
Finally, see how general preaching prevents forgetful omission, which trustworthiness cannot because forgetful acts are neither sinful nor disliked.
This completes the comparative analysis.

[What is shared among these attributes with each other] And it is not hidden from you after this what the three share and what two of them share without the third, and what each one adds beyond the sum of the other two. Commentary
This passage is a comparative analysis of the three obligatory attributes of prophets: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and general preaching (tablīgh 'āmm). The author first explains how the second obligation (trustworthiness) adds to the first (truthfulness) by preventing sins and disliked actions that are not lies, such as backbiting and looking at a non-mahram woman. Truthfulness alone cannot prevent these because they are not false statements. Then the author shows that trustworthiness also adds to the third obligation (general preaching) by preventing sins unrelated to preaching, like theft. Next, the third obligation (general preaching) adds to the first by preventing omissions—both intentional and forgetful—from the message. Truthfulness only ensures that what is preached is true, but it does not require universal coverage; omitting part of the message is not a lie, so only the obligation of general preaching prevents it. Finally, general preaching also adds to trustworthiness by preventing forgetful omissions. Trustworthiness only prohibits deliberate sins and disliked acts, but forgetfulness is neither sinful nor disliked, so it cannot prevent forgetful omission; therefore, the third obligation is needed. The passage concludes by introducing a summary of what the three obligations share, what two share exclusively, and what each adds uniquely. However, the actual enumeration is cut off at the page break, so we only have the introductory statement and the first of the three demands: identifying the imperfection all three negate.

Misconception: One might think that truthfulness (sidq) alone suffices to prevent all imperfections in prophets.
Correction: This passage shows that trustworthiness and general preaching are necessary to cover sins and omissions that truthfulness cannot address.

Key Takeaway
The three prophetic obligations complement each other, each covering imperfections that the others cannot address, ensuring the prophets are free from all types of deficiency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Deficiency All Prophetic Attributes Negate
Sanusi defines the common deficiency and shows how each attribute rejects it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific deficiency that all three prophetic attributes—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery—jointly negate, and why each attribute individually forbids it.

Core Idea
All three prophetic attributes prevent intentional alteration of the divine message.

Sanusi begins by identifying the one deficiency that all three necessary prophetic attributes—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and general delivery—unanimously negate. Understanding this common ground helps us see how these attributes work together to safeguard the integrity of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the common deficiency
Read the Arabic passage about the deficiency all three attributes negate. Focus on the definition of that deficiency.
The deficiency is 'changing or altering something of what God commanded to convey intentionally'.
2
Note how each attribute negates it
Identify how truthfulness negates it (it is lying), how trustworthiness negates it (it is disobedience), and how delivery negates it (it is concealment).
3
Reflect on the necessity of all three
Ask: Why would one attribute not suffice? Consider that each addresses a different aspect of the same deficiency.
This highlights the comprehensive protection of prophethood.

ولا يخفى عليك بعد هذا ما تشترك فيه الثلاثة وما يشترك فيه اثنان منها، دون الثالث، وما يزيد به كل واحد منها على مجموع الباقيين. يعني: أنك إذا حققت معاني الواجبات الثلاثة، وعرفت ما يزيد كل واحد منها على صاحبيه.. سهل عليك فهم هذه المطالب الثلاثة فيها: أحدها: معرفة النقيصة التي تشترك الواجبات الثلاثة في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ وهي تبديل شيء مما أمر الله تعالى بتبليغه، أو تغيير معناه عمدا؛ لأنه كذب؛ فوجوب الصدق للرسل ينفيه، وهو أيضا معصية، فوجوب الأمانة أيضا يدفعه، وهو أيضا كتمان لما أمر المولى العظيم بتبليغه، فوجوب تبليغ الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام لكل ما أمرهم الله تعالى بتبليغه يدفع أيضا هذه النقيصة عنهم. فهذه نقيصة تشترك الواجبات الثلاثة في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام. الثاني من المطالب الثلاثة الباقية: النقيصة التي يشترك في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام اثنان من الواجبات الثلاثة، ويزيدان به على الواجب الثالث؛ فيشترك الواجب الأول والثاني - وهما الصدق والأمانة - في منع الكذب عمدا في الزائد على المأمور بتبليغه، ولا يمنعه الواجب الثالث الذي هو التبليغ العام؛ لأن هذه النقيصة إنما وقعت بعد التبليغ العام. ويشترك الواجب الأول والثالث - وهما الصدق والتبليغ العام - في منع التبديل نسيانا لبعض المأمور بتبليغه؛ فإنه مناف للصدق؛ لأنه كذب، ومناف لتبليغ المأمور بتبليغه، ولا يمنع هذه النقيصة وجوب الأمانة؛ لأنها إنما تمنع المعصية والمكروه، والتبديل نسيانا ليس معصية ولا مكروها.
And it is not hidden from you after this: what the three share, and what two of them share without the third, and what each one adds beyond the sum of the remaining two. Meaning: when you realize the meanings of the three obligations, and know what each one adds beyond its companions, it becomes easy for you to understand these three matters concerning them: The first: knowing the deficiency that the three obligations share in negating from the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them; and it is changing something of what God Almighty commanded to convey, or altering its meaning intentionally; because it is lying; so the obligation of truthfulness for the messengers negates it, and it is also disobedience, so the obligation of trustworthiness also repels it, and it is also concealment of what the Great Master commanded to convey, so the obligation of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, to convey everything that God Almighty commanded them to convey also repels this deficiency from them. So this is a deficiency that the three obligations share in negating from the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. The second of the remaining three matters: the deficiency that two of the three obligations share in negating from the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and they add through it over the third obligation; so the first and second obligations – which are truthfulness and trustworthiness – share in preventing intentional lying concerning what is beyond what is commanded to convey, and the third obligation, which is general delivery, does not prevent it; because this deficiency only occurred after the general delivery. And the first and third obligations – which are truthfulness and general delivery – share in preventing forgetful alteration of part of what is commanded to convey; for it is contrary to truthfulness because it is lying, and contrary to conveying what is commanded to convey, and the obligation of trustworthiness does not prevent this deficiency; because it only prevents disobedience and the disliked, and forgetful alteration is neither disobedience nor disliked.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the interrelations among the three necessary prophetic attributes: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amanah), and general delivery (tabligh 'amm). The author, Sanusi, first announces that after understanding the previous discussion, the student will easily grasp three matters: (1) what deficiency all three attributes share in negating, (2) what deficiency two of them share without the third, and (3) what each attribute uniquely adds beyond the other two. Only the first two matters are explained here. The first matter: the deficiency common to all three is intentional substitution or alteration of any part of the divine message. This is lying (denied by truthfulness), disobedience (denied by trustworthiness), and concealment (denied by general delivery). Thus all three attributes jointly negate this deficiency. The second matter: two pairs of attributes share in negating specific deficiencies. First, truthfulness and trustworthiness together prevent intentional lying about matters beyond the commanded message, but general delivery does not prevent this because such lying occurs after delivery. Second, truthfulness and general delivery together prevent forgetful alteration of part of the message, because forgetful alteration is a form of lying (since it misrepresents the message) and fails to convey as commanded. Trustworthiness does not prevent this because forgetfulness is not a sin or disliked act; trustworthiness only prevents sinful or disliked actions. Thus the author carefully maps the scope of each attribute.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a single attribute (e.g., truthfulness) is enough to guarantee the integrity of the message.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the same deficiency is also a form of disobedience and concealment, requiring trustworthiness and delivery to address those aspects.

Checkpoint
What is the common deficiency that all three prophetic attributes negate?
A) Forgetting part of the message.
B) Intentional alteration of the divine message.
C) Adding something to the message.
D) Preaching without authorization.

Key Takeaway
All three prophetic attributes—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivery—unite to negate intentional alteration of the revealed message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you convey Islamic knowledge to others, have you ever altered the wording or meaning to make it more acceptable? Sanusi identifies this as a deficiency that all three prophetic attributes negate. How will you ensure you convey the message exactly as it is, without addition or omission?
?
You may think that being truthful is enough, but this lesson shows that trustworthiness and full delivery are also required. In your daily interactions, do you sometimes conceal parts of the truth to avoid difficulty? What specific step will you take this week to practice complete honesty and transparency?
?
The deficiency is not just lying but also disobedience and concealment. Reflect on a time you deliberately withheld a difficult teaching because you feared the reaction. How does this passage hold you accountable to deliver the full message, and what will you do to repent and change?

Deficiencies Negated by Pairs of Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi enumerates two pairs of attributes and their shared negations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two specific deficiencies that are negated by pairs of prophetic attributes—truthfulness with trustworthiness, and truthfulness with delivery—and why the third attribute does not apply.

Core Idea
Two pairs of attributes each block a distinct deficiency that the third attribute does not cover.

After covering the deficiency common to all three attributes, Sanusi turns to deficiencies that only two of them share. This shows the precise scope and boundaries of each prophetic attribute, deepening our understanding of how they complement one another.

Guided Path
1
Read about the first pair
Read the part describing what truthfulness and trustworthiness share: preventing intentional lying about matters beyond the commanded message.
Note that general delivery does not prevent this because the deficiency occurs after delivery.
2
Read about the second pair
Read the part about truthfulness and general delivery sharing prevention of forgetful alteration of the message.
Note that trustworthiness does not prevent this because it only applies to intentional sins.
3
Compare the two cases
Contrast why the third attribute is excluded in each case. This clarifies the domain of each attribute.

Checkpoint
Why does general delivery not prevent intentional lying about matters beyond the commanded message?
A) Because it is not a deficiency.
B) Because the lying occurs after delivery.
C) Because truthfulness already prevents it.
D) Because general delivery only applies to the message itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson shows that even unintentional forgetfulness in conveying truth is considered a deficiency in a prophet. When you share religious knowledge with others, how often do you double-check your accuracy? Will you commit to verifying your facts before speaking from now on?
?
The attribute of trustworthiness only guards against intentional sin, not forgetfulness. Are there areas in your life where you excuse your own negligence because it is 'unintentional'? What would change if you held yourself to a higher standard, even for unintentional mistakes?
?
Truthfulness and trustworthiness together prevent adding to the message. Have you ever added your own opinions to religious teachings, thinking they were harmless? How can you ensure that you convey only what has been revealed, without embellishment?

The Three Duties and the Deficiency They All Negate
Sanusi defines the deficiency all three duties negate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three duties of truthfulness, trustworthiness, and public delivery collectively negate the deficiency of intentional alteration or change of meaning in prophetic delivery.

Core Idea
All three duties together prevent any intentional tampering with God's message.

Sanusi begins his classification by first identifying a deficiency that is so serious that all three necessary duties of the prophets work together to negate it. This deficiency is the intentional alteration or change of meaning of what God commanded to be delivered. By seeing how each duty applies, we understand the comprehensive protection of prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the first paragraph
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام' until 'عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام'. This defines one specific deficiency and shows how each of the three duties negates it.
Notice that the same act is a lie, a sin, and concealment—hence all three duties apply.
2
Identify the three duties
List the three duties: truthfulness (al-sidq), trustworthiness (al-amanah), and public delivery (al-tabligh al-'amm). See how each one independently negates the deficiency.
Truthfulness negates lying, trustworthiness negates sin, public delivery negates concealment.
3
Understand why all three are needed
Reflect on why a single duty is insufficient. The deficiency has multiple aspects, each addressed by a different duty.
This shows the multi-faceted protection of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ وهي تبديل شيء مما أمر الله تعالى بتبليغه (۱) ، أو تغيير معناه عمداً (۲) ؛ لأنه كذب ؛ فوجوب الصدق للرسل ينفيه ، وهو أيضاً معصيةٌ ، فوجوب الأمانة أيضاً يدفعه ، وهو أيضاً كتمان لما أمر المولى العظيم بتبليغه ، فوجوب تبليغ الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام لكل ما أمرهم الله تعالى بتبليغه يدفع أيضاً هذه النقيصة عنهم فهذه نقيصة تشترك الواجبات الثلاثة في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام .
الثاني من المطالب الثلاثة الباقية : النقيصة التي يشترك في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام اثنان من الواجبات الثلاثة ، ويزيدان به على الواجب الثالث ؛ فيشترك الواجب الأول والثاني - وهما الصدق والأمانة - في منع الكذب عمداً في الزائد على المأمور بتبليغه ، ولا يمنعه الواجب الثالث الذي هو التبليغ العام ؛ لأن هذه النقيصة إنما وقعت بعد التبليغ العام .
ويشترك الواجب الأول والثالث - وهما الصدق والتبليغ العام - في منع التبديل نسياناً لبعض المأمور بتبليغه ؛ فإنه مناف للصدق ؛ لأنه كذب ، ومناف لتبليغ المأمور بتبليغه ، ولا يمنع هذه النقيصة وجوب الأمانة ؛ لأنها إنما تمنع المعصية والمكروة ، والتبديل نسياناً لا تكليف فيه ، فليس بمعصية ولا مكروه .
وتشترك الأمانة والتبليغ العام في منع نقص شيء من المأمور بتبليغه عمداً ؛ فإنه معصية وترك للتبليغ العام ؛ فكل واحد من هذين الواجبين ينفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا ينفيه الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق ؛ لأن الترك من غير تبديل ليس بكذب .
الثالث من المطالب الثلاثة : ما يزيده كل واحد من الواجبات الثلاثة على مجموع الواجبين الباقيين ؛ فالواجب الأول - وهو الصدق - يزيد على مجموع الأمانة والتبليغ العام ؛ بمنع الكذب نسياناً في غير المأمور بتبليغه لأنه مناف للصدق ، وليس منافياً للأمانة ولا للتبليغ العام ، فلا يفهم نفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام إلا من الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق .
ويزيد الواجب الثاني - وهو الأمانة - على مجموع الصدق والتبليغ العام ؛ بمنع المعصية في غير الكذب وبعد التبليغ العام ؛ كالسرقة مثلاً .
ويزيد التبليغ العام على مجموع الواجبين الأولين - وهما الصدق والأمانة - بمنع نقص شيء من المأمور بتبليغه نسياناً من غير تبديل ولا إخلال فيما بلغ (۲) ؛ فإنه مناف للتبليغ العام ، فيفهم نفيه منه .
The messengers, peace be upon them: and it is the alteration of something of what God Almighty commanded to be delivered, or changing its meaning intentionally, because it is a lie; so the obligation of truthfulness for the messengers negates it, and it is also a sin, so the obligation of trustworthiness also repels it, and it is also concealment of what the Great Lord commanded to be delivered, so the obligation of the messengers' delivery, peace be upon them, of all that God Almighty commanded them to deliver also repels this deficiency from them. So this is a deficiency in which the three duties share in negating it from the messengers, peace be upon them.
The second of the three remaining demands: the deficiency in which two of the three duties share in negating it from the messengers, peace be upon them, and they thereby exceed the third duty. So the first and second duties - namely truthfulness and trustworthiness - share in preventing intentional lying in what is beyond what was commanded to be delivered, and the third duty, which is public delivery, does not prevent it, because this deficiency occurred after public delivery.
And the first and third duties - namely truthfulness and public delivery - share in preventing alteration due to forgetfulness of some of what was commanded to be delivered; for it is contrary to truthfulness because it is a lie, and contrary to delivering what was commanded to be delivered, and the obligation of trustworthiness does not prevent this deficiency because it only prevents sin and the disliked, and alteration due to forgetfulness involves no obligation, so it is not a sin nor disliked.
And trustworthiness and public delivery share in preventing the intentional omission of something from what was commanded to be delivered; for it is a sin and an abandonment of public delivery; so each of these two duties negates it from the messengers, peace be upon them, and the first duty, which is truthfulness, does not negate it, because omission without alteration is not a lie.
The third of the three demands: what each of the three duties adds beyond the sum of the other two duties. So the first duty - namely truthfulness - adds to the sum of trustworthiness and public delivery by preventing lying due to forgetfulness in what is not commanded to be delivered, because it is contrary to truthfulness, and it is not contrary to trustworthiness nor to public delivery, so its negation from the messengers, peace be upon them, is understood only from the first duty, which is truthfulness.
And the second duty - namely trustworthiness - adds to the sum of truthfulness and public delivery by preventing sin in other than lying and after public delivery, such as theft.
And public delivery adds to the sum of the first two duties - namely truthfulness and trustworthiness - by preventing the omission of something from what was commanded to be delivered due to forgetfulness without alteration or deficiency in what was delivered; for it is contrary to public delivery, so its negation is understood from it.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the deficiencies (naqa'is) that are negated from the prophets (al-rusul) by the three necessary duties (al-wajibat al-thalath): truthfulness (al-sidq), trustworthiness (al-amanah), and public delivery (al-tabligh al-'amm). The author, Sanusi, systematically shows how these duties cooperate to protect the prophets from various types of shortcomings.

The passage begins by defining a deficiency that all three duties collectively negate. This deficiency is the intentional alteration or change of meaning of what God commanded to be delivered. It is a lie (kadhib), so truthfulness negates it. It is a sin (ma'siyah), so trustworthiness negates it. It is concealment (kitman) of what was commanded, so public delivery negates it. Thus, all three duties together prevent this deficiency.

Next, Sanusi discusses the deficiencies that are prevented by exactly two of the three duties, and not by the third. He lists three subcases:
1. Truthfulness and trustworthiness together prevent intentional lying about matters beyond what was commanded to be delivered (al-za'id 'ala al-ma'mur bi-tablighihi). Public delivery does not prevent this because it occurs after the delivery of the commanded message, so it is outside the scope of the delivery duty.
2. Truthfulness and public delivery together prevent alteration due to forgetfulness of something commanded to be delivered. This is a lie (so truthfulness negates it) and a failure to deliver (so public delivery negates it). Trustworthiness does not prevent it because forgetfulness involves no intentional sin, and trustworthiness only prevents sins and disliked acts.
3. Trustworthiness and public delivery together prevent intentional omission of something commanded to be delivered. This is a sin (so trustworthiness negates it) and an abandonment of delivery (so public delivery negates it). Truthfulness does not prevent it because omission without lying (like simply not saying something) is not a lie.

Finally, Sanusi identifies what each duty uniquely adds beyond the other two, i.e., deficiencies that only that duty can negate:
1. Truthfulness alone prevents lying due to forgetfulness in matters that are not part of the commanded delivery. The other duties do not cover this because it is not a failure of trustworthiness (no sin) nor of public delivery (it's outside the delivery scope).
2. Trustworthiness alone prevents sin other than lying after public delivery has occurred. Examples are theft or similar sins after the prophetic message has been delivered. Truthfulness and public delivery do not cover this because it is not a lie and does not affect the delivery itself.
3. Public delivery alone prevents the omission of something from the commanded delivery due to forgetfulness, where there is no alteration or deficiency in what was actually delivered. This is a failure to deliver fully, so only the duty of public delivery negates it.

This classification shows the precision of kalam in protecting the doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ismah).

النقيصة
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ العام

الكتمان

Checkpoint
What three aspects of intentional alteration make all three duties negate it?
A) Lie, sin, concealment
B) Lie, forgetfulness, omission
C) Sin, error, negligence
D) Lie, theft, change

Key Takeaway
Intentional alteration of God's message is a lie, a sin, and concealment, so all three prophetic duties negate it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you share religious knowledge, do you ever subtly adjust words or meanings to make them more palatable? This passage shows that even changing the meaning intentionally is a lie, a sin, and concealment. How will you commit to conveying God's message exactly as it is, even when it is hard?
?
Think of a situation where you knew the truth but altered it to avoid conflict or gain acceptance. The prophets are protected from such tampering. How does this lesson expose the state of your own heart regarding honesty? What will you change today?
?
The three duties—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and full delivery—together guard against any tampering. Which of these do you find yourself most compromising on, and what concrete step can you take before tonight to strengthen it?

Deficiencies Negated by Exactly Two Duties
Sanusi lists three deficiencies each negated by two duties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three types of deficiencies that are negated by exactly two of the three duties, and why the third duty does not apply.

Core Idea
Not all deficiencies require all three duties; some are negated by just two.

After establishing the deficiency that all three duties negate, Sanusi now examines deficiencies that are prevented by only two duties. These cases show the precise boundary of each duty. By studying these, we see how the duties complement each other without overlap.

Guided Path
1
Read the three subcases
Read the passage from 'الثاني من المطالب الثلاثة الباقية' until 'الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق'. There are three distinct subcases, each with a pairing of duties.
Pay attention to which duty is excluded in each case.
2
Case 1: Truthfulness + Trustworthiness
These two prevent intentional lying beyond the commanded message. Public delivery does not apply because it occurs after delivery.
This shows the scope of tabligh: only what is commanded to be delivered.
3
Case 2: Truthfulness + Public Delivery
These two prevent forgetful alteration of the commanded message. Trustworthiness does not apply because forgetfulness is not a sin.
Amanah only covers intentional sins and disliked acts.
4
Case 3: Trustworthiness + Public Delivery
These two prevent intentional omission of the commanded message. Truthfulness does not apply because omission without lying is not a lie.
Sidq only covers speech, not actions like omission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ وهي تبديل شيء مما أمر الله تعالى بتبليغه (۱) ، أو تغيير معناه عمداً (۲) ؛ لأنه كذب ؛ فوجوب الصدق للرسل ينفيه ، وهو أيضاً معصيةٌ ، فوجوب الأمانة أيضاً يدفعه ، وهو أيضاً كتمان لما أمر المولى العظيم بتبليغه ، فوجوب تبليغ الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام لكل ما أمرهم الله تعالى بتبليغه يدفع أيضاً هذه النقيصة عنهم فهذه نقيصة تشترك الواجبات الثلاثة في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام .
الثاني من المطالب الثلاثة الباقية : النقيصة التي يشترك في نفيها عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام اثنان من الواجبات الثلاثة ، ويزيدان به على الواجب الثالث ؛ فيشترك الواجب الأول والثاني - وهما الصدق والأمانة - في منع الكذب عمداً في الزائد على المأمور بتبليغه ، ولا يمنعه الواجب الثالث الذي هو التبليغ العام ؛ لأن هذه النقيصة إنما وقعت بعد التبليغ العام .
ويشترك الواجب الأول والثالث - وهما الصدق والتبليغ العام - في منع التبديل نسياناً لبعض المأمور بتبليغه ؛ فإنه مناف للصدق ؛ لأنه كذب ، ومناف لتبليغ المأمور بتبليغه ، ولا يمنع هذه النقيصة وجوب الأمانة ؛ لأنها إنما تمنع المعصية والمكروة ، والتبديل نسياناً لا تكليف فيه ، فليس بمعصية ولا مكروه .
وتشترك الأمانة والتبليغ العام في منع نقص شيء من المأمور بتبليغه عمداً ؛ فإنه معصية وترك للتبليغ العام ؛ فكل واحد من هذين الواجبين ينفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا ينفيه الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق ؛ لأن الترك من غير تبديل ليس بكذب .
الثالث من المطالب الثلاثة : ما يزيده كل واحد من الواجبات الثلاثة على مجموع الواجبين الباقيين ؛ فالواجب الأول - وهو الصدق - يزيد على مجموع الأمانة والتبليغ العام ؛ بمنع الكذب نسياناً في غير المأمور بتبليغه لأنه مناف للصدق ، وليس منافياً للأمانة ولا للتبليغ العام ، فلا يفهم نفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام إلا من الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق .
ويزيد الواجب الثاني - وهو الأمانة - على مجموع الصدق والتبليغ العام ؛ بمنع المعصية في غير الكذب وبعد التبليغ العام ؛ كالسرقة مثلاً .
ويزيد التبليغ العام على مجموع الواجبين الأولين - وهما الصدق والأمانة - بمنع نقص شيء من المأمور بتبليغه نسياناً من غير تبديل ولا إخلال فيما بلغ (۲) ؛ فإنه مناف للتبليغ العام ، فيفهم نفيه منه .
The messengers, peace be upon them: and it is the alteration of something of what God Almighty commanded to be delivered, or changing its meaning intentionally, because it is a lie; so the obligation of truthfulness for the messengers negates it, and it is also a sin, so the obligation of trustworthiness also repels it, and it is also concealment of what the Great Lord commanded to be delivered, so the obligation of the messengers' delivery, peace be upon them, of all that God Almighty commanded them to deliver also repels this deficiency from them. So this is a deficiency in which the three duties share in negating it from the messengers, peace be upon them.
The second of the three remaining demands: the deficiency in which two of the three duties share in negating it from the messengers, peace be upon them, and they thereby exceed the third duty. So the first and second duties - namely truthfulness and trustworthiness - share in preventing intentional lying in what is beyond what was commanded to be delivered, and the third duty, which is public delivery, does not prevent it, because this deficiency occurred after public delivery.
And the first and third duties - namely truthfulness and public delivery - share in preventing alteration due to forgetfulness of some of what was commanded to be delivered; for it is contrary to truthfulness because it is a lie, and contrary to delivering what was commanded to be delivered, and the obligation of trustworthiness does not prevent this deficiency because it only prevents sin and the disliked, and alteration due to forgetfulness involves no obligation, so it is not a sin nor disliked.
And trustworthiness and public delivery share in preventing the intentional omission of something from what was commanded to be delivered; for it is a sin and an abandonment of public delivery; so each of these two duties negates it from the messengers, peace be upon them, and the first duty, which is truthfulness, does not negate it, because omission without alteration is not a lie.
The third of the three demands: what each of the three duties adds beyond the sum of the other two duties. So the first duty - namely truthfulness - adds to the sum of trustworthiness and public delivery by preventing lying due to forgetfulness in what is not commanded to be delivered, because it is contrary to truthfulness, and it is not contrary to trustworthiness nor to public delivery, so its negation from the messengers, peace be upon them, is understood only from the first duty, which is truthfulness.
And the second duty - namely trustworthiness - adds to the sum of truthfulness and public delivery by preventing sin in other than lying and after public delivery, such as theft.
And public delivery adds to the sum of the first two duties - namely truthfulness and trustworthiness - by preventing the omission of something from what was commanded to be delivered due to forgetfulness without alteration or deficiency in what was delivered; for it is contrary to public delivery, so its negation is understood from it.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the deficiencies (naqa'is) that are negated from the prophets (al-rusul) by the three necessary duties (al-wajibat al-thalath): truthfulness (al-sidq), trustworthiness (al-amanah), and public delivery (al-tabligh al-'amm). The author, Sanusi, systematically shows how these duties cooperate to protect the prophets from various types of shortcomings.

The passage begins by defining a deficiency that all three duties collectively negate. This deficiency is the intentional alteration or change of meaning of what God commanded to be delivered. It is a lie (kadhib), so truthfulness negates it. It is a sin (ma'siyah), so trustworthiness negates it. It is concealment (kitman) of what was commanded, so public delivery negates it. Thus, all three duties together prevent this deficiency.

Next, Sanusi discusses the deficiencies that are prevented by exactly two of the three duties, and not by the third. He lists three subcases:
1. Truthfulness and trustworthiness together prevent intentional lying about matters beyond what was commanded to be delivered (al-za'id 'ala al-ma'mur bi-tablighihi). Public delivery does not prevent this because it occurs after the delivery of the commanded message, so it is outside the scope of the delivery duty.
2. Truthfulness and public delivery together prevent alteration due to forgetfulness of something commanded to be delivered. This is a lie (so truthfulness negates it) and a failure to deliver (so public delivery negates it). Trustworthiness does not prevent it because forgetfulness involves no intentional sin, and trustworthiness only prevents sins and disliked acts.
3. Trustworthiness and public delivery together prevent intentional omission of something commanded to be delivered. This is a sin (so trustworthiness negates it) and an abandonment of delivery (so public delivery negates it). Truthfulness does not prevent it because omission without lying (like simply not saying something) is not a lie.

Finally, Sanusi identifies what each duty uniquely adds beyond the other two, i.e., deficiencies that only that duty can negate:
1. Truthfulness alone prevents lying due to forgetfulness in matters that are not part of the commanded delivery. The other duties do not cover this because it is not a failure of trustworthiness (no sin) nor of public delivery (it's outside the delivery scope).
2. Trustworthiness alone prevents sin other than lying after public delivery has occurred. Examples are theft or similar sins after the prophetic message has been delivered. Truthfulness and public delivery do not cover this because it is not a lie and does not affect the delivery itself.
3. Public delivery alone prevents the omission of something from the commanded delivery due to forgetfulness, where there is no alteration or deficiency in what was actually delivered. This is a failure to deliver fully, so only the duty of public delivery negates it.

This classification shows the precision of kalam in protecting the doctrine of prophetic infallibility (ismah).

Key Terms
الصدق
الأمانة
التبليغ العام
الكذب عمداً
التبديل نسياناً
نقص الشيء عمداً

Checkpoint
Which two duties prevent intentional omission of the commanded message?
A) Truthfulness and trustworthiness
B) Truthfulness and public delivery
C) Trustworthiness and public delivery
D) All three

Key Takeaway
Three deficiencies are negated by exactly two duties, each exclusion based on the precise scope of the duties.

What Each Duty Uniquely Adds
Sanusi enumerates what each duty uniquely adds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the unique deficiency that each duty alone negates, beyond the combined scope of the other two.

Core Idea
Each duty has a unique area where it alone protects the prophets.

Sanusi completes his classification by identifying what each duty uniquely contributes. These are deficiencies that only one duty can negate, because the other two do not cover them. This final part shows the indispensable role of each duty in safeguarding prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the third section
Read from 'الثالث من المطالب الثلاثة' to the end. This covers three subcases, each showing a deficiency unique to one duty.
Notice how each deficiency is outside the scope of the other two duties.
2
Truthfulness alone: forgetful lying outside commanded delivery
This is a lie from forgetfulness about matters not commanded to be delivered. The other duties do not apply because it is not a sin (forgetful) and not related to delivery.
Only truthfulness covers lying regardless of intentionality and context.
3
Trustworthiness alone: sin other than lying after delivery
Example: theft after the prophetic message has been delivered. This is a sin but not a lie and does not affect delivery.
Trustworthiness covers all sins, not just those involving speech.
4
Public delivery alone: forgetful omission without alteration
Forgetting to deliver part of the commanded message, but not adding any falsehood. This is a failure of delivery but not a sin (forgetful) and not a lie.
Public delivery ensures complete delivery, even if unintentional.

Which duty alone prevents forgetting to deliver part of the message without any alteration?
A) Truthfulness

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The duty of trustworthiness prevents sin even after the message is delivered. After you fulfill a responsibility—like teaching, advising, or completing a task—do you still guard against small sins that others might overlook? Is there any area where you let your guard down because you think the 'main duty' is done?
?
Public delivery requires that nothing be omitted, even unintentionally. When you share knowledge of Islam—whether formally or informally—do you ever hold back parts that are difficult or uncomfortable? How can you train yourself to be faithful in conveying the whole truth, even when forgetfulness or fear tempts you to omit?
?
Truthfulness prevents lying even in trivial matters not commanded to be delivered. In your daily conversations, are you truthful in every word, even when a small 'forgetful' lie would go unnoticed? What would it cost you to be scrupulously truthful about things that seem unimportant?

The Five Demands of the Three Obligatory Attributes of Prophets
Sanusi enumerates the unique contributions of each prophetic attribute and totals the demands.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the three obligatory attributes of prophets—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and public delivery—interrelate and yield five distinct theological demands.

Core Idea
Three prophetic attributes combine to produce five demands: shared duties plus unique additions.

Sanusi now deepens our understanding of the three obligatory attributes of prophets—truthfulness, trustworthiness, and public delivery. He shows how they overlap in forbidding certain omissions and, more importantly, what each attribute uniquely forbids beyond the others. This analysis yields five total demands: the two preliminary demands (knowing the meanings and knowing what each adds to each other) plus three additional demands derived from the unique contributions of each attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage aloud once
Read the complete Arabic text to get a feel for Sanusi's precise and technical style. Focus on the flow from shared prohibitions to unique additions.
The passage uses repetition to distinguish each attribute's scope.
2
Identify the shared prohibition
Notice that trustworthiness (amana) and public delivery (tabligh al-'amm) both forbid intentionally omitting any part of the message. Truthfulness does not forbid this because omission without lying is not a lie.
This shows the partial overlap between the attributes.
3
Analyze the unique addition of each attribute
For truthfulness: it forbids forgetful lying about matters not commanded to be delivered. For trustworthiness: it forbids any sin other than lying after delivery. For public delivery: it forbids forgetful omission of anything commanded.
Each attribute adds a prohibition not covered by the other two.
4
Count the total demands
Sanusi sums up: the three unique additions plus the two earlier demands (knowing the meanings and knowing what each adds to each other) make five demands.
This is the conclusion that ties the passage together.

لا تكليف فيهِ، فليس بمعصية ولا مكروه. وتشترك الأمانة والتبليغ العام في منع نقص شيءٍ من المأمور بتبليغه عمداً؛ فإنه معصية وترك للتبليغ العام؛ فكل واحد من هذين الواجبين ينفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ولا ينفيه الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق؛ لأن الترك من غير تبديل ليس بكذب. الثالث من المطالب الثلاثة: ما يزيده كل واحد من الواجبات الثلاثة على مجموع الواجبين الباقيين؛ فالواجب الأول - وهو الصدق - يزيد على مجموع الأمانة والتبليغ العام؛ بمنع الكذب نسياناً في غير المأمور بتبليغه لأنه منافٍ للصدق، وليس منافياً للأمانة (1) ولا للتبليغ العام، فلا يفهم نفيه عن الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام إلا من الواجب الأول الذي هو الصدق. ويزيد الواجب الثاني - وهو الأمانة - على مجموع الصدق والتبليغ العام بمنع المعصية في غير الكذب وبعد التبليغ العام؛ كالسرقة مثلاً. ويزيد التبليغ العام على مجموع الواجبين الأولين - وهما الصدق والأمانة - بمنع نقص شيء من المأمور بتبليغه نسياناً من غير تبديل ولا إخلال فيما بلغ (2)؛ فإنه منافٍ للتبليغ العام، فيفهم نفيه منه. ومثاله: نسيان صلاة من الصلوات الخمس. فمجموع المطالب في هذه الواجبات الثلاثة: خمسة؛ هذه المطالب الثلاثة التي ذكرنا هنا، والمطلبان السابقان؛ وهما معرفة معاني الواجبات الثلاثة، ومعرفة ما يزيده كل واحد منها على كل واحد من صاحبيه. وبالله تعالى التوفيق.
(1) عُلِّق في (د): (كالخبر عن الصحيح بأنه أعمى).
(2) عُلِّق في (د): على كلمة (إخلال): (ترادف) يعني: مع التبديل هنا.
There is no obligation in it, so it is not a sin nor disliked. Trustworthiness and public delivery share in preventing a deficiency of anything from what is commanded to be delivered intentionally; for it is a sin and abandonment of public delivery. So each of these two obligations negates it from the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them), and the first obligation—which is truthfulness—does not negate it; because abandonment without alteration is not lying. The third of the three demands: what each of the three obligations adds over the sum of the remaining two obligations. So the first obligation—truthfulness—adds over the sum of trustworthiness and public delivery the prevention of forgetful lying in matters not commanded to be delivered, because it contradicts truthfulness, and it does not contradict trustworthiness (1) nor public delivery, so its negation from the messengers is understood only from the first obligation, which is truthfulness. The second obligation—trustworthiness—adds over the sum of truthfulness and public delivery the prevention of sin other than lying and after public delivery, such as theft. Public delivery adds over the sum of the first two obligations—truthfulness and trustworthiness—the prevention of a deficiency of anything from what is commanded to be delivered forgetfully without alteration or disruption in what he has delivered (2); for it contradicts public delivery, so its negation is understood from it. Its example: forgetting one of the five prayers. So the sum of the demands concerning these three obligations is five: these three demands that we have mentioned here, and the two previous demands: knowing the meanings of the three obligations, and knowing what each of them adds over each of the two companions. And with Allah Almighty is success. (1) Marginal note in (D): (like reporting about the sighted that he is blind). (2) Marginal note in (D): on the word (disruption): (synonymous) meaning: with alteration here.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage explains the mutual relationships between the three obligatory attributes of prophets (truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivering the message). It first notes that trustworthiness and delivering the message both forbid deliberately omitting any part of the command—that would be a sin. Truthfulness does not forbid that because omission without lying is not a lie. Then Sanusi defines the third of the three 'demands' (matalib): what each obligation adds uniquely over the other two. For truthfulness: it forbids forgetful lying about matters not commanded to be delivered (since intentional lying is already covered). For trustworthiness: it forbids any sin other than lying, even after delivery (e.g., theft). For delivering the message: it forbids even forgetful omission of anything commanded, even if the delivered message is otherwise correct (e.g., forgetting a prayer). He then sums up: there are five demands total—these three plus the two earlier demands: knowing the meanings of the three obligations and knowing what each adds to each of the others. The passage ends with a prayer for success. Marginal notes add an example and a lexical clarification.

المعصية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that forgetful omission of part of the message is excused or only forbidden by truthfulness.
Correction: The passage clarifies that forgetful omission is specifically forbidden by public delivery, not by truthfulness or trustworthiness. Truthfulness only forbids forgetful lying in non-commanded matters; forgetful omission of commanded matters is a violation of public delivery.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which attribute uniquely forbids forgetful omission of anything from what is commanded to be delivered?
A) Truthfulness
B) Trustworthiness
C) Public delivery
D) All three together

Key Takeaway
The three prophetic attributes yield five demands: two general (meanings and mutual additions) and three specific unique prohibitions, ensuring no form of omission or sin escapes their scope.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that a prophet cannot forget to deliver even a single prayer. Yet you, in your daily life, often neglect or forget commands of Allah. If a mere human is held to such perfect standard of delivery, how will you answer for your carelessness? What specific act of worship or dawah have you been putting off, and when will you start it?
?
Sanusi's analysis shows that truthfulness even covers forgetful lies about non-religious matters. Have you excused yourself by saying 'I didn't mean to lie' when you misspoke? How does this passage call you to greater vigilance over your speech, even in casual conversation?
?
The five demands are not abstract theology—they reveal the meticulous care Allah took in choosing His messengers. How does this precision contrast with your own attitude toward religious knowledge? Are you satisfied with a vague, general faith, or will you pursue the detailed understanding exemplified by scholars like Sanusi? Write one concrete step you will take this week to deepen your knowledge.

Impossible Attributes of Prophets as Opposites
Sanusi states that impossible attributes are opposites and deduces them from obligations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the impossible attributes of prophets are logically deduced from their obligatory attributes as their opposites.

Core Idea
The impossible for prophets is simply the opposite of the obligatory.

Sanusi now turns to the attributes that are impossible for prophets. He shows that these are not arbitrary; they follow directly from the obligatory attributes. By understanding the three obligations, we automatically know their opposites, which are impossible. This logical connection is the key to this short but important passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical principle stated in the first sentence.
2
Identify the three obligatory attributes
The passage mentions three obligations of prophets: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and public delivery. Find them in the text.
These are the foundation for the impossibilities.
3
Understand the logical principle
Sanusi says that knowing the obligation leads to knowing the impossibility. The marginal note explains: existence of a thing necessitates negation of its opposite.
This principle is key to kalam reasoning.
4
Match each obligation to its opposite
For each obligation, Sanusi gives the corresponding impossible attribute: lying (opposite of truthfulness), betrayal (opposite of trustworthiness), failure to deliver (opposite of delivery).
Notice that betrayal includes both prohibited and disliked actions.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Sanusi says 'that is apparent'—meaning the logical connection is clear once the obligations are known.
This demonstrates the rational basis for prophetic attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المستحيلات في حق الرسل الكرام عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وأما المستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام فأضداد هذه الثلاثة. لا خفاء أنه إذا علم ما يجب في حق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام علم منه ما يستحيل في حقهم (1)؛ فلما علم وجوب الصدق في حقهم علم منه استحالة الكذب عليهم؛ وهو الإخبار بما لا يطابق ما في نفس الأمر، ولما علم وجوب الأمانة لهم علم منه استحالة الخيانة عليهم؛ وهو التلبس بمنهي عنه نهي تحريم أو كراهة، ولما علم وجوب التبليغ العام لهم علم منه استحالة عدم التبليغ لشيء مما أمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو سهواً، وذلك ظاهر. وبالله تعالى التوفيق.
(1) عُلِّق في (د): (لأن وجود الشيء يستلزم نفي ضدّه).
The impossible things concerning the noble messengers (peace and blessings be upon them). As for what is impossible concerning them (peace and blessings be upon them), it is the opposites of these three. There is no hiding that when one knows what is obligatory concerning the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them), one knows from it what is impossible concerning them (1); so when the obligation of truthfulness concerning them is known, from it is known the impossibility of lying for them; it is reporting what does not correspond to what is in actual reality. And when the obligation of trustworthiness for them is known, from it is known the impossibility of betrayal for them; it is engaging in what is forbidden by a prohibition of prohibition or dislike. And when the obligation of public delivery for them is known, from it is known the impossibility of not delivering anything that they were commanded to deliver intentionally or forgetfully. And that is apparent. And with Allah Almighty is success. (1) Marginal note in (D): (because the existence of a thing necessitates the negation of its opposite).
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage discusses the impossible attributes (mustahilat) of the messengers. It begins by stating that the impossible attributes are simply the opposites of the three obligatory ones (truthfulness, trustworthiness, delivering the message). Sanusi then articulates a logical principle: knowing what is obligatory directly implies knowing what is impossible, because existence of a thing negates its opposite. He applies this: from the obligation of truthfulness, we infer the impossibility of lying (reporting something contrary to reality). From the obligation of trustworthiness, we infer the impossibility of betrayal (engaging in what is prohibited or disliked—whether haram or makruh). From the obligation of public delivery, we infer the impossibility of failing to deliver anything commanded, whether intentionally or forgetfully. The passage concludes that this is apparent and seeks divine success.

الرسل

الأمانة

الخيانة
النهي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the impossibility of lying etc. for prophets is known only from explicit revelation, not from rational deduction.
Correction: Sanusi shows that once we know truthfulness is obligatory, its opposite (lying) is rationally impossible. The existence of a thing negates its opposite.

Checkpoint
How do we know that lying is impossible for prophets according to Sanusi?
A) It is stated explicitly in revelation
B) It is the opposite of truthfulness, and once truthfulness is known to be obligatory, its opposite is impossible
C) It is a major sin and prophets are sinless
