Key Takeaway
The impossible attributes of prophets are logically deduced from their obligatory attributes as their opposites.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that truthfulness is obligatory for prophets and lying is impossible for them. Now ask yourself: in your daily speech, how often do you allow your tongue to deviate from reality—even in small 'white lies'? If the most honorable of creation were utterly incapable of falsehood, what does your own comfort with dishonesty say about your spiritual state? Will you commit to a single day of complete honesty, watching every word, and feel the weight of this standard?
?
Trustworthiness (al-amāna) means avoiding even disliked actions. Consider the last time you cut a corner, cheated on a task, or took something that wasn't fully yours (time, credit, goods). Did you excuse it as 'minor'? If the prophets cannot betray even a disliked act, how can you accept such betrayals in your own life? What is one concrete betrayal you will repent from today and never repeat?
?
Public delivery (al-tablīgh) means the prophets must convey every message they were commanded to deliver without omission. Think of the truth you know from this lesson—the reality that prophets are infallible in these three ways. Are you delivering this truth to those around you, or are you silently withholding it out of shyness, fear, or laziness? If the prophets could not fail to deliver, how can you justify failing to share the truth you now know? Will you speak to one person about this lesson before the day ends?

Deriving the Impossible Attributes of the Messengers
Sanusi derives three impossible attributes from obligatory ones via opposition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the impossible attributes of the messengers are logically derived from their obligatory attributes through the principle of opposition.

Core Idea
The impossible is the opposite of the obligatory.

Sanusi establishes a simple but powerful logical principle: if an attribute is obligatory for a messenger, its opposite is impossible. This lesson traces this derivation for the three key pairs: truthfulness vs. lying, trustworthiness vs. treachery, and delivery vs. failure to deliver.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi moves from the obligatory to the impossible.
The footnote illustrates the underlying logical principle: existence of a thing necessitates negation of its opposite.
2
Identify the three pairs
The passage presents three pairs: obligatory truthfulness → impossible lying; obligatory trustworthiness → impossible treachery; obligatory delivery → impossible non-delivery. Find each pair in the text.
3
Reflect on the logical principle
Ask yourself why Sanusi states that knowing the obligatory automatically gives knowledge of the impossible. The commentary explains the principle of opposition.
This principle is foundational in Islamic theology for deriving negative attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا ينافي الواجبين الأولين ; إذ ليس بكذب ولا خيانة . فمجموع المطالبِ في هذه الواجبات الثلاثةِ : خمسة ؛ هذهِ المطالب الثلاثةُ التي ذكرنا هنا ، والمطلبان السابقان ; وهما معرفةً معاني الواجبات الثلاثة ، ومعرفة ما يزيدُهُ كلُّ واحدٍ منها على كلِّ واحدٍ مِنْ صاحبيه ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق . التحميلات في حق الرسل الكرام عليهم الصلاة والسلام حق الرسل اله . وأما المستحيل في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام فأضداد هذه الثلاثة . لا خفاءَ أَنَّهُ إذا عُلِمَ ما يجب في حق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام .. عُلِمَ منه ما يستحيلُ في حقهم (۱) ; فلمَّا عُلِمَ وجوب الصدق في حقهم .. عُلِمَ منه استحالةُ الكذب عليهم ; وهو الإخبار بما لا يطابق ما في نفس الأمرِ ، ولمَّا عُلِمَ وجوبُ الأمانةِ لهم .. عُلِمَ منهُ استحالة الخيانة عليهم ; وهو التلبس بمنهي عنه نهي تحريم أو كراهة ، ولمَّا عُلِمَ وجوبُ التبليغ العام لهم .. عُلِمَ منه استحالة عدم التبليغ لشيء ممَّا أُمروا بتبليغه عمداً أو سهواً ، وذلكَ ظاهرُ ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق . (۱) عُلَّقَ في (د) : ( لأنَّ وجود الشيء يستلزم نفي ضدّه ) .
And it does not contradict the first two obligations, because it is neither lying nor treachery. So the total of the demands in these three obligations is five: these three demands that we mentioned here, and the two previous demands: knowing the meanings of the three obligations, and knowing what each of them adds over each of its companions. And with Allah Almighty is success. The impossibilities regarding the noble messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. As for the impossible regarding them, peace and blessings be upon them, they are the opposites of these three. There is no concealment that when what is obligatory regarding the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, is known, what is impossible regarding them is known from it. For when the obligation of truthfulness regarding them is known, the impossibility of lying upon them is known from it; and it is reporting what does not correspond to what is in reality. And when the obligation of trustworthiness for them is known, the impossibility of treachery upon them is known from it; and it is engaging in what is forbidden by a prohibition of prohibition or dislike. And when the obligation of general delivery for them is known, the impossibility of non-delivery of anything that they were commanded to deliver, intentionally or forgetfully, is known from it; and that is apparent. And with Allah Almighty is success. (1) Annotated in (D): (Because the existence of a thing necessitates the negation of its opposite).
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage derives the impossible attributes of the messengers from their obligatory attributes. It begins by noting that the third obligation (delivery) does not conflict with the first two (truthfulness and trustworthiness), as it is not lying nor treachery. Then the author states that the total required topics concerning these three obligations are five: the three obligations themselves plus two prior topics: knowing their meanings and knowing what each adds over the others. Then the author turns to the impossibilities: the impossible attributes of messengers are the opposites of the three obligations. The proof is that if you know the obligatory, you know its opposite is impossible. Specifically: because truthfulness is obligatory, lying (reporting contrary to reality) is impossible; because trustworthiness is obligatory, treachery (committing what is forbidden or disliked) is impossible; because general delivery is obligatory, failure to deliver anything commanded (intentionally or forgetfully) is impossible. The footnote explains the logical principle: existence of a thing necessitates negation of its opposite.

Correction: The text shows they are derived by logical necessity from the obligatory attributes: knowing the obligatory entails knowing its opposite is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The impossible attributes of messengers are simply the opposites of the obligatory ones, known by logical necessity.

?
The impossibility of non-delivery means you have received the complete message. Do you treat the Sunnah as a complete source of guidance, or do you selectively ignore parts that are inconvenient? Confess this to yourself and decide to change.

Definition and Examples of Possible Attributes
Definition and listing of possible human attributes for messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what attributes are possible for the messengers and how they are distinguished by being free from anything that contradicts their exalted rank.

Core Idea
The messengers' possible attributes are human accidents that never compromise their lofty rank.

Sanusi now turns from attributes of Allah to attributes of His messengers. He explains that some human experiences, like illness and hunger, are possible for prophets because observing them in their lives confirms it. This lesson examines the definition and examples of these possible attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic definition of possible attributes (الجائزات) and note the condition: they must not contradict the messengers' high rank.
The proof is direct observation (مشاهدة).
2
Identify the examples given
Find the list of human accidents: illness, hunger, poverty, eating, drinking, marriage, forgetfulness, and sleep. Notice the exception for sleep: eyes sleep but hearts do not.
These are all common human experiences.
3
Reflect on the proof and benefit
Sanusi states that these have been observed in messengers and that there are benefits to these attributes. Ask yourself what purpose they might serve.
The benefits will be explained in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجائزات في حق الرسل الكرام عليه الصلاة والسلام . وأما الجائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فالأعراض البشرية التي لا تنافي عُلَوَّ رُتبتهم . كالمرض ونحوه ، بدليل مشاهدة ذلك فيهم ، وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا تخفى . مراده بنحو المرض : الجوع ، والفقرُ مِنَ الأعراض الدنيوية معَ الغنى عنها بالله تعالى ، والأكل والشرب ، والنكاح ، والنسيان بعد التبليغ ، أو فيما لم يُؤمَرُوا بتبليغه ، والنوم ; إلا أنّهم تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم ، ولا شكّ أنَّه قد شُوهِدَ جميع ذلك فيهم . وقوله : ( وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا تخفى ) يعني : ليس نزولُ هذه الأعراض بهم كنزولها بغيرهم في إمكان عدم اقترانها بالفوائد التي تُصيرُها قُرباً وعبادات ، بل لا تنزل بهم إلا عارية عن حظ النفس ودواعي (۱) وبهذا القيد السلبي تثبت لهم صفة الفطانة ; وهي حدة العقل وكماله ; إذ البَلَهُ والبلادة نقص كبير ينافي علوّ رُتَبِهم ، وهذه الصفة يذكرها المتأخرون في الواجبات ، وكأنها ثبتت بالاستقراء ، أو بالوجوب العقلي بملاحظة نفي ضدها ، وممَّا يذكره المتأخرون من الصفات الواجبة والقيد هنا يفيد وجوبها أيضاً : الذكورة ، والحرية ، وتمام العقل ويرجع للفطانة ، والسلامة من المنفرات ، وشرف الآباء والأمهات ، واللين لتنتفي صفة الغلظة ، والمروءة لتنتفي خوارمها ، وكونه من أهل الحضر لا الوبر . ۲۰۱
The possible attributes regarding the noble messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. As for the possible regarding them, peace and blessings be upon them: it is the human accidents that do not contradict the loftiness of their rank. Like illness and the like, by the evidence of observing that in them, and in their being characterized by them there are benefits that are not hidden. He intends by 'the like of illness': hunger, and poverty from worldly accidents along with being independent of them by Allah Almighty, and eating and drinking, and marriage, and forgetfulness after delivery, or regarding what they were not commanded to deliver, and sleep; except that their eyes sleep but their hearts do not sleep, and there is no doubt that all of that has been observed in them. And his statement: 'And in their being characterized by them there are benefits that are not hidden' means: the descent of these accidents upon them is not like their descent upon others in the possibility of their being devoid of the benefits that make them acts of closeness and worship; rather they do not descend upon them except free from self-interest and motives. And by this negative condition the attribute of intelligence is established for them; and it is sharpness of intellect and its perfection; for stupidity and dullness are a great deficiency contradicting the loftiness of their ranks. And this attribute is mentioned by later scholars among the obligatory attributes, and it seems it was established by induction, or by rational obligation by considering the negation of its opposite. And among what later scholars mention of the obligatory attributes—and the condition here also indicates their obligation—are: masculinity, freedom, completeness of intellect (which reverts to intelligence), safety from repulsive things, nobility of fathers and mothers, gentleness to negate harshness, chivalry to negate its violations, and being from the people of settled areas not the desert.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the possible attributes (الجائزات) of the messengers. The author states that what is possible for them are human accidents (الأعراض البشرية) that do not contradict their exalted rank, such as illness and similar things. The proof is that these are observed in them. Their being characterized by these has hidden benefits. 'The like of illness' includes hunger, poverty (while being independent of them through Allah), eating, drinking, marriage, forgetfulness after delivery or concerning what they were not commanded to deliver, and sleep—but their hearts do not sleep, only their eyes. These are all witnessed. The benefit is that these accidents do not happen to them as they happen to others, devoid of benefit; rather, they are free from selfish motives and become acts of worship. Then the author notes that from this negative condition (i.e., that these accidents are not accompanied by lowly motives) the attribute of intelligence (الفطانة) is established, which is sharpness and perfection of intellect, because stupidity would contradict their rank. Later scholars include this among obligatory attributes. The author lists additional obligatory attributes mentioned by later scholars: masculinity, freedom, completeness of intellect (which reverts to intelligence), safety from repulsive things, noble lineage, gentleness, chivalry, and being from settled areas instead of the desert.

Key Terms

Misconception: Some think that human accidents like illness and forgetfulness imply imperfection in prophets.
Correction: These attributes are possible and carry spiritual benefits; they do not contradict their exalted rank.

Possible attributes of messengers are human accidents that do not contradict their exalted rank, proven by observation.

Benefits and Derived Obligatory Attributes
Explanation of benefits and derivation of obligatory attributes from the possible attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose behind the messengers' human experiences and how they imply obligatory attributes like intelligence and nobility.

Core Idea
Every human accident of a messenger is a means of closeness to Allah, not a flaw.

Having listed the possible attributes, Sanusi now explains their deeper significance. The very condition that these attributes are free from selfish motives establishes the messengers' perfect intelligence. Later scholars derived additional obligatory attributes from this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of benefits
Sanusi clarifies that these accidents descend upon messengers free from self-interest, turning them into acts of worship.
This distinguishes them from similar accidents in ordinary people.
2
Understand the establishment of intelligence
From the negative condition (absence of selfish motives), the attribute of intelligence (الفطانة) is derived. Stupidity would contradict their rank.
Later scholars consider intelligence obligatory by induction or rational necessity.
3
Review the list of additional obligatory attributes
Sanusi lists: masculinity, freedom, completeness of intellect, safety from repulsive things, noble lineage, gentleness, chivalry, and being from settled areas.
These are mentioned by later scholars, and the condition of the possible attributes implies them.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجائزات في حق الرسل الكرام عليه الصلاة والسلام . وأما الجائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فالأعراض البشرية التي لا تنافي عُلَوَّ رُتبتهم . كالمرض ونحوه ، بدليل مشاهدة ذلك فيهم ، وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا تخفى . مراده بنحو المرض : الجوع ، والفقرُ مِنَ الأعراض الدنيوية معَ الغنى عنها بالله تعالى ، والأكل والشرب ، والنكاح ، والنسيان بعد التبليغ ، أو فيما لم يُؤمَرُوا بتبليغه ، والنوم ; إلا أنّهم تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم ، ولا شكّ أنَّه قد شُوهِدَ جميع ذلك فيهم . وقوله : ( وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا تخفى ) يعني : ليس نزولُ هذه الأعراض بهم كنزولها بغيرهم في إمكان عدم اقترانها بالفوائد التي تُصيرُها قُرباً وعبادات ، بل لا تنزل بهم إلا عارية عن حظ النفس ودواعي (۱) وبهذا القيد السلبي تثبت لهم صفة الفطانة ; وهي حدة العقل وكماله ; إذ البَلَهُ والبلادة نقص كبير ينافي علوّ رُتَبِهم ، وهذه الصفة يذكرها المتأخرون في الواجبات ، وكأنها ثبتت بالاستقراء ، أو بالوجوب العقلي بملاحظة نفي ضدها ، وممَّا يذكره المتأخرون من الصفات الواجبة والقيد هنا يفيد وجوبها أيضاً : الذكورة ، والحرية ، وتمام العقل ويرجع للفطانة ، والسلامة من المنفرات ، وشرف الآباء والأمهات ، واللين لتنتفي صفة الغلظة ، والمروءة لتنتفي خوارمها ، وكونه من أهل الحضر لا الوبر . ۲۰۱
The possible attributes regarding the noble messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. As for the possible regarding them, peace and blessings be upon them: it is the human accidents that do not contradict the loftiness of their rank. Like illness and the like, by the evidence of observing that in them, and in their being characterized by them there are benefits that are not hidden. He intends by 'the like of illness': hunger, and poverty from worldly accidents along with being independent of them by Allah Almighty, and eating and drinking, and marriage, and forgetfulness after delivery, or regarding what they were not commanded to deliver, and sleep; except that their eyes sleep but their hearts do not sleep, and there is no doubt that all of that has been observed in them. And his statement: 'And in their being characterized by them there are benefits that are not hidden' means: the descent of these accidents upon them is not like their descent upon others in the possibility of their being devoid of the benefits that make them acts of closeness and worship; rather they do not descend upon them except free from self-interest and motives. And by this negative condition the attribute of intelligence is established for them; and it is sharpness of intellect and its perfection; for stupidity and dullness are a great deficiency contradicting the loftiness of their ranks. And this attribute is mentioned by later scholars among the obligatory attributes, and it seems it was established by induction, or by rational obligation by considering the negation of its opposite. And among what later scholars mention of the obligatory attributes—and the condition here also indicates their obligation—are: masculinity, freedom, completeness of intellect (which reverts to intelligence), safety from repulsive things, nobility of fathers and mothers, gentleness to negate harshness, chivalry to negate its violations, and being from the people of settled areas not the desert.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the possible attributes (الجائزات) of the messengers. The author states that what is possible for them are human accidents (الأعراض البشرية) that do not contradict their exalted rank, such as illness and similar things. The proof is that these are observed in them. Their being characterized by these has hidden benefits. 'The like of illness' includes hunger, poverty (while being independent of them through Allah), eating, drinking, marriage, forgetfulness after delivery or concerning what they were not commanded to deliver, and sleep—but their hearts do not sleep, only their eyes. These are all witnessed. The benefit is that these accidents do not happen to them as they happen to others, devoid of benefit; rather, they are free from selfish motives and become acts of worship. Then the author notes that from this negative condition (i.e., that these accidents are not accompanied by lowly motives) the attribute of intelligence (الفطانة) is established, which is sharpness and perfection of intellect, because stupidity would contradict their rank. Later scholars include this among obligatory attributes. The author lists additional obligatory attributes mentioned by later scholars: masculinity, freedom, completeness of intellect (which reverts to intelligence), safety from repulsive things, noble lineage, gentleness, chivalry, and being from settled areas instead of the desert.

بله
بلادة

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Permissible Attributes of Messengers and Their Benefits
Sanusi defines permissible attributes of messengers and explains their benefits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what constitutes a permissible attribute for messengers, the proof for these attributes, and the profound spiritual benefits they carry.

Core Idea
Prophets' human experiences are not mundane; they are acts of worship with profound benefits.

This lesson explores the category of permissible (ja'iz) attributes for messengers. While prophets are sinless and exalted, they experience human needs and limitations. Sanusi explains what these attributes are, how we know them, and why they are spiritually significant, turning ordinary acts into worship.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Read the opening lines where Sanusi defines permissible attributes as human accidents that do not contradict the prophets' lofty rank. Note the proof: empirical observation (mushahadah).
The term 'human accidents' refers to physical and psychological states like illness, hunger, etc.
2
Identify the list and the negative condition
Go through the list of examples: hunger, poverty, eating, drinking, marriage, forgetfulness, and sleep (with the exception that their hearts remain awake). Notice the negative condition: these are free from self-interest and base desires, which establishes their intelligence (fatanah).
The negative condition (al-qayd al-salbi) is key to distinguishing prophets' experiences from ordinary ones.
3
Explore the benefits
Read the section on benefits: these accidents become acts of worship, teach patience and altruism, and legislate practices for the community. The passage concludes that asceticism (zuhd) is the comprehensive good, as shown by the prophets' shunning worldly excess.
The benefits are both for the prophets themselves and for their followers.

الجائزات في حق الرسل الكرام عليه الصلاة والسلام وأما الجائز في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : فالأعراض البشرية التي لا تنافي عُلَوَّ رُتبتهم؛ كالمرض ونحوه، بدليل مشاهدة ذلك فيهم، وفي اتصافهم بها فوائد لا في عَرَضِ الأكل والشرب بما ندبَ إليهِ مِنْ آدابهما، والصبر والرضا عن الله تعالى عند فقدهما، وإيثار ذوي الفاقة مع شدَّةِ الاحتياج إليهما، وتشريع جميعِ ذلك للمؤمنين بهم التابعين لهم وهكذا حكم مرضهم The permissible things (al-ja'izat) regarding the noble messengers, peace and blessings be upon them. As for the permissible (al-ja'iz) in their right, peace and blessings be upon them: it is the human accidents (al-a'rad al-bashariyya) that do not contradict the loftiness of their rank, such as illness and the like, by evidence of observing that in them, and in their being described with them are benefits that are not hidden. He intends by 'like illness': hunger, and poverty from worldly accidents despite being free of need for them by Allah, and eating and drinking, and marriage, and forgetfulness after conveying (the message), or regarding what they were not commanded to convey, and sleep; except that their eyes sleep while their hearts do not sleep, and there is no doubt that all of that has been observed in them. And his saying: 'And in their being described with them are benefits that are not hidden' means: the descending of these accidents upon them is not like their descending upon others in the possibility of their not being accompanied by benefits that make them nearness (to Allah) and acts of worship; rather, they do not descend upon them except free from self-interest and the impulses of desire (1). And by this negative condition, the attribute of intelligence (al-fatanah) is established for them; it is sharpness of intellect and its perfection; for stupidity and dullness are a great deficiency that contradict the loftiness of their ranks, and this attribute is mentioned by the later scholars among the necessary attributes (al-wajibat), and it seems that it is established by induction, or by rational obligation considering the negation of its opposite. And among what the later scholars mention of the necessary attributes, and the condition here also indicates their obligation: masculinity, freedom, complete intellect which reduces to intelligence, safety from repulsive things, nobility of fathers and mothers, gentleness to negate harshness, chivalry (al-muru'a) to negate its breaches, and his being from the people of settled lands not the desert. Then the desire (al-hawa) [continues the main sentence], surrounded by gnostic benefits and noble luminous nearnesses; such as their worshipping Allah through the occurrence of eating and drinking with what He prescribed of their etiquettes, and patience and contentment with Allah when they are lacking, and preferring the needy despite severe need for them, and legislating all of that for the believers who follow them; and similarly the ruling of their illness and hunger, with the additional benefit of obtaining consolation from the world for the community, and their alerting to the lowness of its worth with Allah (1); for if it had any status with Allah, He would have given it to these masters who are the most noble of creation with Allah, and they would have been eager, upon them peace, to collect and enjoy it more than others; but when we saw them averse to its excesses and discouraging from it extremely, we knew that there is no good in its excesses, and that asceticism (al-zuhd) in it is the truth that encompasses every good. And it is not hidden from the intelligent person the derivation of many benefits from their states, upon them peace; because Allah has protected them, and cared for the perfection of their guidance, and made them models for creation in their words, actions, and silences; so all of them occur in the most perfect attributes, the noblest intentions, and the highest traits. And all that the scholars have derived of benefits from their words and actions, and authored and multiplied, is a drop from a boundless sea. We ask Allah to increase them in honor, then honor, without end, and that (1) in (B, W) 'and their alerting' instead of 'and their alerting'.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage defines the category of permissible (ja'iz) attributes for messengers and elaborates on their spiritual and legal benefits. The author begins by stating that the permissible things for messengers are the human accidents (al-a'rad al-bashariyya) that do not contradict the loftiness of their rank, such as illness. The proof is empirical observation (mushahadah) that these things occurred in them. He then clarifies that 'like illness' includes hunger, poverty, eating, drinking, marriage, forgetfulness regarding what they were not commanded to convey, and sleep—except that their eyes sleep while their hearts do not, as reported in hadith. The key point is that these are not mere mundane occurrences; they are accompanied by benefits that make them acts of worship and nearness to Allah. The author then inserts a long parenthetical note (footnote 1) that explains how the absence of personal desire and impulse establishes the necessary attribute of intelligence (fatanah) for prophets. This negative condition (al-qayd al-salbi) shows that they are free from the lowly motives that would detract from their rank. The note lists other necessary attributes mentioned by later scholars: masculinity, freedom, complete intellect (which reduces to intelligence), safety from repulsive things, noble lineage, gentleness, chivalry, and being from settled lands rather than desert dwellers. Returning to the main argument, the author details the benefits: prophets worship Allah through the very acts of eating and drinking by observing prescribed etiquettes, they demonstrate patience and contentment when deprived, they prefer others despite their own need, and they legislate these practices for their followers. Their illness and hunger serve to console the community about worldly matters and alert them to the low value of this world, for if the world had value with Allah, He would have given it to the prophets, who are the most noble of creation. The fact that prophets shunned worldly excess and discouraged others from it proves that asceticism is the comprehensive good. The passage concludes by emphasizing that all states of prophets—words, actions, silences—are perfect and contain immense benefits, and that the scholars' derivations of these benefits are but a drop from an endless ocean. The closing prayer asks for increase in honor for the prophets.

Key Terms
الجائز (al-ja'iz)
الأعراض البشرية (al-a'rad al-bashariyya)
الفطانة (al-fatanah)
الواجبات (al-wajibat)
مشاهدة (mushahadah)
القيد السلبي (al-qayd al-salbi)
الزهد (al-zuhd)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets' human experiences are merely mundane and devoid of spiritual meaning.
Correction: This passage shows that these experiences are laden with benefits, transforming them into acts of worship and legal precedents, and they are free from self-interest.

Checkpoint

A) Human accidents that do not contradict their high rank, such as illness.

Key Takeaway
The permissible attributes of messengers are human accidents that, through divine grace, become means of nearness to Allah and legal precedents for the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sit down to eat your next meal, will you simply consume for pleasure, or will you intentionally turn it into an act of worship by following the prophetic etiquettes and remembering the higher purpose?
?
If you were to face poverty or illness tomorrow, would your heart instinctively complain and despair, or would you strive to embody the patience, contentment, and altruism that the prophets modeled for us?
?
The prophets were averse to worldly excess and their example proves that asceticism is the comprehensive good. Are you clinging to any attachment to this world that you know deep down is an excess? What would it cost you to let it go and embrace the freedom of zuhd?

The Spiritual Benefits of the Prophets' Human Conditions
Sanusi explains the spiritual benefits of the prophets' actions and states, and their perfection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophets' human actions (like eating, drinking, illness, and hunger) serve as spiritual lessons and proofs for the value of asceticism and the perfection of their example.

Core Idea
The prophets' worldly renunciation proves the low value of this world and the comprehensive good of asceticism.

Sanusi presents a profound reflection on the seemingly mundane human experiences of the prophets. He shows that their eating, drinking, illness, and even hunger are not merely natural occurrences but are imbued with divine wisdom and spiritual benefits for their followers. Through these states, they teach us about patience, altruism, and the ultimate worthlessness of worldly excess, establishing asceticism as the path to all good.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the flow from specific benefits to the broader conclusion about asceticism.
The passage contains a footnote marker (1) which refers to an omitted editorial note.
2
Identify the listed benefits
Look for the explicit benefits Sanusi mentions: worship in eating/drinking, patience when lacking, preferring the needy, and the additional benefits of illness and hunger.
These are practical lessons for believers to emulate.
3
Analyze the proof from worldly aversion
Focus on the argument: if this world had value, God would have given it to the prophets. Since they avoided excess, we know there is no good in it, and asceticism (zuhd) is the comprehensive truth.
This is a key rational proof in the passage.
4
Reflect on prophets as perfect exemplars
Sanusi asserts that prophets are infallible (ma'sum) and their words, actions, and silences are perfect. Consider why this is essential for them to be role models.
This reinforces the reliability of their example.
5
Consider the limitless wisdom
The passage ends with the statement that scholars' derivations are but a drop from an ocean. Contemplate the vastness of prophetic knowledge and the humility required.
This encourages continued study and reliance on God's mercy.

الهوى، محفوفةً بالفوائدِ العِرفانيَّةِ ، والقُرب الشريفة النورانية ؛ كتعبدهم الله تعالى في عَرَضِ الأكل والشرب بما ندبَ إليهِ مِنْ آدابهما ، والصبر والرضا عن الله تعالى عند فقدهما ، وإيثار ذوي الفاقة مع شدَّةِ الاحتياج إليهما ، وتشريع جميعِ ذلك للمؤمنين بهم التابعين لهم وهكذا حكم مرضهم وجوعِهم ، مع زيادة حصولِ التسلّي عن الدنيا للأمة ، وتنبههم لخِسَةِ قَدْرِها عندَ اللهِ تعالى (۱) ؛ إذ لو كانَ لها موقع عند الله تعالى .. لأعطاها لهؤلاء الساداتِ الذين هم الخلقِ عندَ الله تبارك وتعالى ، ولَحرَصوا عليهم الصلاة والسلام على أشرفُ جمعها والتمتُّع بها أكثرَ مِنْ غيرِهم ، فلما رأيناهم نافرين عن فضولها منفّرينَ عنها في غايةٍ .. علمنا أنَّهُ لا خير في فضولها ، وأنَّ الزهد فيها هو الحق الجامع لكلِّ خيرٍ ولا يخفى على العاقل استنباط الفوائد الكثيرةِ مِنْ أحوالهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؛ لأنَّ الله تعالى قد عصمهم ، واعتنى بكمال هدايتهم ، وجعلَهم قُدوةً للخلْقِ في أقوالهم وأفعالهم وسكوتهم ، فهي كلُّها واقعة على أكمل الصفاتِ ، وأشرف المقاصدِ ، وأعلـى السَّماتِ ، وكلُّ ما استنبط العلماءُ مِنْ فوائدِ أقوالهم وأفعالهم وألَّفوا وأكثروا . . نُقطةٌ مِنْ بحرٍ لا ساحلَ لهُ نسأل الله تعالى أن يزيدهم شرفاً ثم شرفاً إلى ما لا نهاية له ، وأن يُدخِلَ جميعنا بلا مِحْنةٍ في شفاعةِ سيّدِ الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى ؛ سيدنا ونبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ وعلى آلِهِ
...the inclination, surrounded by gnostic benefits and noble luminous proximities; such as their worship of Allah the Exalted in the context of eating and drinking by following the etiquette He prescribed, and patience and contentment with Allah the Exalted when lacking them, and preferring the needy while in severe need of them, and legislating all of that for the believers who follow them. Similarly, the ruling of their illness and hunger, with the additional benefit of consoling the community regarding the world and alerting them to the lowliness of its value in the sight of Allah the Exalted (1); for if it had any standing with Allah the Exalted, He would have given it to these masters who are the most honored of creation with Allah the Blessed and Exalted, and they would have been keen—peace and blessings be upon them—on collecting it and enjoying it more than others. So when we see them averse to its excess and strongly discouraging from it, we know that there is no good in its excess, and that asceticism (zuhd) in it is the comprehensive truth comprising all good. It is not hidden from the intelligent person the derivation of many benefits from their states—peace and blessings be upon them—because Allah the Exalted has protected them (ʿiṣma), attended to the perfection of their guidance, and made them exemplars for creation in their words, actions, and silences. All of them occur upon the most perfect attributes, the noblest intentions, and the highest qualities. Everything that the scholars have derived from the benefits of their words and actions, and compiled and expanded upon, is but a point from an endless ocean. We ask Allah the Exalted to increase them in honor, then honor, without end, and to admit all of us without trial into the intercession of the Master of creation and the most generous to Allah the Exalted—our Master, our Prophet, and our Mawlā Muḥammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and upon his family.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage expounds on the benefits derived from the prophets' human conditions. The author begins by noting that even mundane actions like eating and drinking are acts of worship when done with prescribed etiquette. He then discusses the virtues of patience and altruism, especially in hardship. The prophets' illnesses and hunger serve to console the community by revealing the low value of this world. A proof is given: if this world were valuable to Allah, He would have given it to the prophets, but they avoided it—thus asceticism is the comprehensive good. The author then emphasizes the prophets' infallibility and perfection; their states are exemplary. All scholarly derivations from their lives are but a drop from an ocean. The passage concludes with a supplication for increased honor for the prophets and for the community to receive their intercession.

Key Terms
الفوائد العرفانيّة (gnostic benefits)
الزهد (asceticism)
العصمة (infallibility)
القدوة (exemplar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude from the prophets' aversion to worldly excess?
A) That the world is entirely evil and to be completely abandoned.
B) That there is no good in worldly excess and asceticism is the comprehensive truth.
C) That the prophets were not truly human.
D) That the world is of great value to Allah.

Key Takeaway
The prophets' human conditions teach us that worldly excess holds no good, and asceticism is the comprehensive good; their actions are perfect exemplars for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hunger, illness, or deprivation, do you see it as an opportunity for gnostic benefit and closeness to Allah, or merely as a trial? How can you consciously follow the prophets' example of patience and contentment in your next difficulty?
?
The prophets preferred the needy even while they themselves were in need. Examine your last week—where did you prioritize your own comfort over giving to someone who needed more? What is one concrete change you will make today to embody this prophetic trait?
?
You learned that scholars' knowledge of the prophets' benefits is just a drop from an endless ocean. How much time have you spent studying the lives of the prophets? What is one specific step you will take this week to dive deeper into their example?

Three Reservations Regarding Permissible Attributes of Prophets
Sanusi explains three reservations and three categories of people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three reservations that protect against false beliefs about the prophets and the three categories of people regarding their veneration.

Core Idea
Three reservations guard against extremes in understanding prophets.

This lesson unpacks Sanusi's careful wording that prevents misunderstandings about the prophets' humanity and their high rank. We'll see how each part of the phrase 'the human attributes that do not contradict the highness of their rank' guards against specific heresies. Then we'll learn about the three attitudes people take toward prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to understand the overall meaning.
Notice the three reservations are introduced by 'our statement: ... is a reservation against...'
2
Identify the three reservations
Find each reservation and note which group or belief it guards against: (1) 'the attributes' against Christians, (2) 'the human' against ignorant, (3) 'that do not contradict...' against Jews and ignorant historians.
3
Understand the three categories of people
The passage divides people into exaggerator, neglecter (both ruined), and the moderate (saved). Reflect on how the reservations protect against the first two extremes.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: Why is it important to define prophets' attributes so precisely? How do these reservations help maintain correct belief?
This connects to the broader goal of protecting tawḥīd and respect for prophets.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ احترازات مفادةٌ مِنْ قولِهِ : ( الأعراض البشريَّةُ التي لا تنافي عُلُو رتبتهم ) ] فقولنا : ( الأعراض ( احتراز مِنْ مذهب النصارى في وصفهم عيسى عليه السلام بالصفة القديمة وقولُنا · ( البشرية ( احتراز من اعتقادِ الجاهليةِ أنَّ البشرية تنافي الرسالة وقولنا ) : ( التي لا تنافي علوّ رُتبتهم ( احترازُ مِن اعتقادِ اليهودِ وكثيرِ مِنْ جهلةِ المؤرّخين والمفسرين اتصاف الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام بنقيصة المعصية والمكروه ونحوهما لا شك أن الناس باعتبار تعظيمهم الرُّسُلَ عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ثلاثة أقسام : مُفرِطٌ ، ومُفرَّطٌ ؛ وهمـا هـالكـان ، ومتوسط ؛ وهو الناجي بفضل الله تعالى ، وعن القسمين الأولين احترزنا بالقيود التي ذكرناها في تفسير الجائز على الرسل صلواتُ اللهِ وسلامه عليهم فاحترزنا بالأعراض - وهي الصفاتُ الحادثة المتجددة - مِنَ
[Useful reservations from his statement: 'The human attributes that do not contradict the highness of their rank.'] For our statement: 'the attributes' is a reservation against the doctrine of the Christians in their description of Jesus, peace be upon him, with the eternal attribute. And our statement: 'the human' is a reservation against the belief of the ignorant that humanity contradicts the message. And our statement: 'that do not contradict the highness of their rank' is a reservation against the belief of the Jews and many ignorant historians and exegetes that the prophets—peace and blessings be upon them—are described with the shortcoming of sin, the disliked, and the like. There is no doubt that people, with regard to their veneration of the messengers—peace and blessings be upon them—are three categories: an exaggerator, a negligent person—both are ruined—and a moderate person; he is the saved by the grace of Allah the Exalted. And from the first two categories we guarded ourselves by the restrictions we mentioned in the interpretation of what is permissible for the messengers—peace and blessings be upon them. So we guarded ourselves by 'attributes'—which are the temporally originated qualities—from...
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage provides three crucial reservations (iḥtirāzāt) clarifying the phrase 'the human attributes that do not contradict the highness of their rank.' Each reservation guards against a specific heresy: (1) The word 'attributes' refutes the Christian claim that Jesus had an eternal attribute (i.e., divinity). (2) The word 'human' repudiates the ignorant belief that being human precludes prophethood. (3) The clause 'that do not contradict the highness of their rank' counters the Jewish belief and ignorant historians who attribute sin and disliked things to prophets. The author then categorizes people regarding veneration of messengers into three groups: the exaggerator (muftiṭ), the negligent (mufarriṭ), both ruined, and the moderate (mutawassiṭ), who is saved. The reservations protect against the first two extremes. The text ends mid-sentence about guarding by 'attributes' from something, likely continuing on the next page.

Key Terms
الأعراض (attributes)
البشرية (humanity)
علو الرتبة (highness of rank)
المفرط (exaggerator)
المفرط (neglecter)
المتوسط (moderate)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that prophets' human attributes imply imperfection or contradiction to their high rank.
Correction: The reservations clarify that prophets' human attributes do not contradict their high rank; they are permissible and not indicative of imperfection.

Checkpoint
Which reservation guards against the Christian belief that Jesus had an eternal attribute?
A) The reservation by 'the human' (al-bashariyya)
B) The reservation by 'the attributes' (al-aʿrāḍ)
C) The reservation by 'that do not contradict the highness of their rank'
D) The reservation by 'the moderate' (al-mutawassiṭ)

Key Takeaway
The three reservations protect against extremism in veneration of prophets, and the moderate path is the saved one by Allah's grace.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your own relationship with the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), do you tend toward exaggeration (ascribing more than human) or negligence (not giving him due respect)? What is one concrete way you can move toward the moderate path today?
?
The lesson warns against attributing eternal qualities to a prophet, as Christians did with Jesus. Are there people today whom you unconsciously elevate to a near-divine status? How can you guard your heart against this subtle shirk?
?
If you were to ask yourself honestly, do you sometimes fall into the trap of thinking that being human makes the prophets less worthy of reverence? What specific thought or action can you change this week to better honor their rank while acknowledging their humanity?

Three Precautions in Defining What Is Permissible for Prophets
Explains three precautionary qualifications in defining permissible prophetic traits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three precautionary qualifications in the definition of what is permissible for prophets and how they guard against extremism and neglect.

Core Idea
The definition of permissible prophetic traits is a middle path between two extremes.

In defining what traits are permissible for prophets, scholars use precise language to avoid both over-glorification and under-appreciation. This lesson examines a key text from Sanusi that explains three critical qualifications in the definition, each aimed at correcting a specific doctrinal error.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the concise style of the author.
2
Identify the three qualifications
Find the three parts of the definition: 'accidents', 'human', and 'that do not contradict their high rank'. Understand what each excludes.
Each precaution guards against a different extreme group.
3
Understand the targets of each precaution
See that 'accidents' rejects the Christian deification of Jesus, 'human' rejects the Jahiliyyah denial of prophethood for humans, and 'not contradicting rank' rejects the Jewish attribution of sin to prophets.
4
Study the three categories of people
The author divides people into extremist, neglecter, and moderate. The definition protects against the first two.
Both extremes are destroyed; only the moderate is saved.
5
Reflect on the wisdom of the definition
Consider why these qualifications are necessary for a correct understanding of prophethood. Note the concluding remark that human traits in prophets are perfections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احترازات مفادةٌ مِنْ قولِهِ : ( الأعراض البشريَّةُ التي لا تنافي عُلُو رتبتهم ) فقولنا : ( الأعراض ( احتراز مِنْ مذهب النصارى في وصفهم عيسى عليه السلام بالصفة القديمة وقولنا : ( البشرية ( احتراز من اعتقادِ الجاهليةِ أنَّ البشرية تنافي الرسالة وقولنا ) : ( التي لا تنافي علوّ رُتبتهم ( احترازُ مِن اعتقادِ اليهودِ وكثيرِ مِنْ جهلةِ المؤرّخين والمفسرين اتصاف الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام بنقيصة المعصية والمكروه ونحوهما لا شك أن الناس باعتبار تعظيمهم الرُّسُلَ عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ثلاثة أقسام : مُفرِطٌ ، ومُفرَّطٌ ؛ وهمـا هـالكـان ، ومتوسط ؛ وهو الناجي بفضل الله تعالى ، وعن القسمين الأولين احترزنا بالقيود التي ذكرناها في تفسير الجائز على الرسل صلواتُ اللهِ وسلامه عليهم فاحترزنا بالأعراض - وهي الصفاتُ الحادثة المتجددة - مِنَ الصفات القديمة التي هي صفات الإله جلَّ وعلا ، فلا يصح أن يتّصفَ بها غيرُ مولانا جل وعلا • وقد كفرَتِ النصارى بمخالفتهم هذا القيد ، وإفراطهم في حقّ عيسى عليه الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ فجعلوا صفة العلم القديم قائمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام ، وجعلوه لذلكَ إلهاً على خَبْط لهم شديدٍ ، وتخليط عظيم لا يفوهُ بهِ عاقل ، تعالى الله عن قولهم واحترزنا بقيدِ البشرية - كالأكل والشرب والمرض ونحوها ـ مِنْ صفات الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وهي غناهم عن هذهِ الأعراض التي وضعها الله تعالى في البشرِ ، فليسَ يُشترَطُ ذلكَ في الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ لعدم توقف الرسالة عليها ، وليس غنى الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام عنها لذواتهم ، بل بجعل الله تعالى لهم ذلكَ وقد كفرَتِ الجاهليَّةُ بمخالفتهم هذا القيد ، وإفراطهم أيضاً بزعمهم أنَّ هذهِ الصفاتِ البشريَّةَ نقيصةٌ لا تليق بمرتبة الرسالة ، وإنَّما يليقُ بها صفاتُ الملائكة ، فكفروا ، وكَذَّبوا بسبب ذلكَ الرُّسُلَ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ، وقالوا ما أخبر الله تعالى عنهم : أَبشَرُ يَهْدُونَنَا [التغابن : ٦] ، وَ إِنْ أَنتُمْ إِلَّا بَشَرٌ مِثْلُنَا ﴾ [إبراهيم : ١٠]، ﴿ مَالِ هَذَا الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ ﴾ [الفرقان : 7] ، ولو انكشف الحجاب عن قلوبهم .. تعرفوا أنَّ في وقوع هذه الأعراض البشرية بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ كمالاتٍ لهم في أنفسهم ، وتكميلاتٍ متكاثرةً
Beneficial precautions from his statement: (human accidents that do not contradict their high rank). So our statement: (the accidents) is a precaution from the doctrine of the Christians in their describing Jesus, peace be upon him, with the eternal attribute. And our statement: (the human) is a precaution from the belief of the Jahiliyyah that humanity contradicts messengership. And our statement: (that do not contradict their high rank) is a precaution from the belief of the Jews and many of the ignorant historians and exegetes that the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, are described with the defect of sin, the disliked, and similar. There is no doubt that people, with regard to their veneration of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, are three categories: an extremist, and a neglecter – both are destroyed – and a moderate; he is the saved by the grace of Allah Almighty. And from the first two categories we took precaution with the restrictions that we mentioned in the interpretation of what is permissible for the messengers, may the blessings and peace of Allah be upon them. So we took precaution with (accidents) – which are the temporal, renewed attributes – from the eternal attributes which are the attributes of the Divine, Mighty and Majestic. So it is not valid that any other than our Master, Mighty and Majestic, be described with them. And the Christians have disbelieved by violating this restriction and by their extremism regarding Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him; they made the attribute of eternal knowledge subsist in the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, and thus they made him a god, in a severe confusion and a great mixing that no intelligent person utters. Exalted is Allah above their statement. And we took precaution with the restriction of humanity – such as eating, drinking, illness, and the like – from the attributes of the angels, peace and blessings be upon them, which is their independence from these accidents that Allah Almighty placed in humans. So that is not required in the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, because messengership does not depend on it. And the angels' independence from them, peace and blessings be upon them, is not by their essences, but by Allah Almighty making that for them. And the Jahiliyyah have disbelieved by violating this restriction and by their extremism as well, claiming that these human attributes are a defect not befitting the rank of messengership, and that only the attributes of the angels are befitting it. So they disbelieved and denied the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, because of that, and said what Allah Almighty informed about them: 'Shall human beings guide us?' [Taghabun, 6], and 'You are only human like us' [Ibrahim, 10], and 'What is this messenger who eats food and walks in the markets?' [Furqan, 7]. And if the veil were lifted from their hearts, they would know that in the occurrence of these human accidents in the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, there are perfections for them in themselves and multiplying completions.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage explains the three precautionary qualifications in the definition of what is permissible for prophets. It begins by stating the definition: 'human accidents that do not contradict their high rank.' Then it breaks down each component: (1) The term 'accidents' (أعراض) excludes eternal attributes, guarding against the Christian error of attributing eternal knowledge to Jesus, which led to their disbelief and claim of divinity for him. (2) The term 'human' (بشرية) excludes angelic attributes, guarding against the pre-Islamic Arab (Jahiliyyah) error of denying prophethood to humans because they considered human traits like eating and drinking a defect, while angels are free from such accidents. The author notes that angels' freedom from these needs is not intrinsic but by God's making, so it is not required for prophets. (3) The phrase 'that do not contradict their high rank' excludes sin and disliked acts, guarding against the Jewish and ignorant historians' claim that prophets could commit sins. The author then categorizes people into three types regarding reverence for prophets: extremists (like Christians who deify), neglecters (like those who deny their high status), and the moderate (the saved). The two extremes are destroyed. The restrictions in the definition are precisely to avoid the errors of the two extreme groups. The passage concludes by observing that if the disbelievers understood, they would see that human accidents in prophets are actually perfections that enhance their mission.

Key Terms
الأعراض البشرية
الجائز على الرسل
الصفات القديمة
الصفات الحادثة
النصارى
الجاهلية
اليهود
المفرط
المفرط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that any human attributes are permissible for prophets.
Correction: The definition specifies only those human accidents that do not contradict their high rank and are not defects like sin.

Checkpoint
Which group falsely attributed eternal attributes to a prophet?
A) The Jews
B) The Christians
C) The Jahiliyyah (pre-Islamic Arabs)
D) The moderate Muslims

Key Takeaway
The permissible traits for prophets are specifically defined to avoid both deification and denial of their humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt uncomfortable with the full humanity of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) — his eating, his sleeping, his walking in the markets — and wished he were more 'angelic'? What does that discomfort reveal about your own heart's proximity to the Jahiliyyah mindset, and what will you do today to embrace his humanity as a perfection?
?

?
The Christians and the Jahiliyyah both fell into disbelief because of their extremes about the prophets. Where in your own life do you see a subtle tendency toward either exaggeration or neglect in how you honor Allah's messengers? Write down one specific change you will make today to align your heart with the saved middle.

Human Attributes of Prophets: Condition and Refutation
Sanusi defends human attributes and refutes Jahiliyya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that human attributes in prophets are a wise condition, not a deficiency, and why the Jahiliyya's rejection amounts to disbelief.

Core Idea
Human attributes in prophets are a mercy, not a flaw.

Sanusi begins by clarifying a key restriction in his creed: prophets have human attributes like eating and drinking, but these are not obligatory for prophethood. He then confronts the Jahiliyya who considered such attributes a deficiency and thus rejected the messengers. This lesson explores the condition itself and the error of those who see it as a flaw.

Guided Path
1
Understand the restriction
Read the first part where Sanusi explains why human attributes are specified ('احترزنا بقيد البشرية') and why they are not required for messengers.
Angels are free from these accidents by God's grant, not inherently.
2
Learn the Jahiliyya's mistake
See how the Jahiliyya violated this restriction and fell into extremism by deeming human attributes as a deficiency.
They rejected the prophets because they expected messengers to be angelic.
3
Reflect on the Qur'anic verses
Three verses are quoted showing their rejection. Notice the common thread: they could not accept a human messenger.
4
See the deeper irony
Sanusi hints that such attributes actually bring perfections for the prophets and completions for nations. This sets up the next lesson.
This prepares us for the wisdom behind the human condition.

واحترزنا بقيدِ البشرية - كالأكل والشرب والمرض ونحوها ـ مِنْ صفات الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، وهي غناهم عن هذهِ الأعراض التي وضعها الله تعالى في البشرِ ، فليسَ يُشترَطُ ذلكَ في الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ؛ لعدم توقف الرسالة عليها ، وليس غنى الملائكةِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام عنها لذواتهم ، بل بجعل الله تعالى لهم ذلكَ • وقد كفرَتِ الجاهليَّةُ بمخالفتهم هذا القيد ، وإفراطهم أيضاً بزعمهم أنَّ هذهِ الصفاتِ البشريَّةَ نقيصةٌ لا تليق بمرتبة الرسالة ، وإنَّما يليقُ بها صفاتُ الملائكة ، فكفروا ، وكَذَّبوا بسبب ذلكَ الرُّسُلَ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ، وقالوا ما أخبر الله تعالى عنهم : أَبشَرُ يَهْدُونَنَا [التغابن : ٦] ، وَ إِنْ أَنتُمْ إِلَّا بَشَرٌ مِثْلُنَا ﴾ [إبراهيم : ١٠]، ﴿ مَالِ هَذَا الرَّسُولِ يَأْكُلُ الطَّعَامَ وَيَمْشِي فِي الْأَسْوَاقِ ﴾ [الفرقان : 7] ، ولو انكشف الحجاب عن قلوبهم .. تعرفوا أنَّ في وقوع هذه الأعراض البشرية بالرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ كمالاتٍ لهم في أنفسهم ، وتكميلاتٍ متكاثرةً لأُممهم؛ بحيثُ يَغتبط بها الملائكةُ الكرام ، ويتمنون وجود مثلها لهم؛ لما فيها مِنَ الآدابِ الرفيقةِ (١) ، والعبادات الدقيقة التي لم يجدوا مثلها في عباداتهم، هذا معَ ما فيها مِنْ تأنيس الأمم، ودفع الوَحشةِ عنهم بمخالطةِ مَنْ هو مِنْ جنسِهم، ومتَّصف بحسَبِ الظاهرِ بصفاتهم، وأمكنهم لأجل الجنسيَّةِ والمخالطة أن يعرفوا أمانته وصدقَهُ ونصيحته والتلقي منه، ولو كان مَلَكاً .. لَتَعذَّرَ ذلكَ كلُّهُ؛ قالَ اللهُ تعالى: ﴿ وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَاهُ مَلَكَا لَّجَعَلْنَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ [الأنعام : ٩] س فاعتبر سبحانَهُ الخلق بمقتضى الفضل العظيم ، والرحمة واللطفِ؛ بأن بعثَ إليهم رُسُلاً مِنْ أنفسهم، ظاهرهم بشريٌّ مِنْ جنسِ المبعوث إليهم، وباطنُهم مَلَكي، بل أعلى؛ ولهذا اتَّسَعَتْ قلوبهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ لمخالطة الفريقين، ومراعاة الجانبين
And we guarded ourselves by the restriction of human attributes — such as eating, drinking, illness, and the like — from the attributes of the angels, peace be upon them, which is their being free from these accidents that God the Exalted placed in humans. So that (i.e., having human attributes) is not required of the messengers, peace be upon them, because the message does not depend on it. The angels' freedom from them is not due to their own essences, but by God the Exalted granting them that. • And the Jahiliyya disbelieved by violating this restriction and by their extremism as well, claiming that these human attributes are a deficiency unworthy of the rank of prophethood, and that only the attributes of angels are worthy of it. So they disbelieved and rejected the messengers, peace be upon them, because of that, and they said what God the Exalted informed about them: 'Will a human guide us?' [Al-Taghabun: 6], and 'You are nothing but humans like us' [Ibrahim: 10], and 'What is this messenger that he eats food and walks in the markets?' [Al-Furqan: 7]. And if the veil were lifted from their hearts, they would come to know that in the occurrence of these human accidents upon the messengers, peace be upon them, there are perfections for themselves and numerous completions for their nations, such that the noble angels would envy them and wish to have similar things for themselves, because of the refined etiquettes and subtle acts of worship that they do not find in their own worship. This, along with what it contains of familiarizing the nations and removing alienation from them through mixing with someone who is of their own kind and outwardly described with their attributes, so that because of that common kind and mixing they can know his trustworthiness, truthfulness, sincerity, and receive knowledge from him. And if he were an angel, all of that would be impossible. God the Exalted said: 'And if We had made him an angel, We would surely have made him a man and would have confused for them what they are confusing' [Al-An'am: 9]. So He, Exalted, treated the creation according to great bounty, mercy, and kindness by sending to them messengers from among themselves, their outward is human of the same kind as those sent to, and their inward is angelic, even higher; and therefore their hearts, peace be upon them, expanded to mix with both groups and observe both aspects.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage both defends a condition and refutes a misguided group. It first clarifies that human attributes (like eating and drinking) are not obligatory for messengers; angels lack them but by God's grant, not inherently. Then it refutes the Jahiliyya (pre-Islamic Arabs) who considered these human attributes a deficiency and thus rejected the prophets. The author quotes three Qur'anic verses expressing their rejection. The core of the passage explains the profound wisdom behind human messengers: their human qualities allow them to connect with people, serve as role models, and facilitate teaching. The angels themselves would envy these human experiences. If a messenger were an angel, this connection would be impossible, as the Qur'an states. The passage concludes by summarizing God's mercy in sending outwardly human but inwardly angelic messengers.

قيد البشرية
الجاهلية
نقيصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human attributes in prophets are a sign of low status or deficiency.
Correction: Sanusi shows these attributes are not required for prophethood, and they are actually a mercy and perfection.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did the Jahiliyya become disbelievers?
A) Because they claimed prophets were angels.
B) Because they considered human attributes a deficiency and rejected the prophets.
C) Because they denied the existence of God.
D) Because they refused to accept the Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The human attributes of prophets are a wise divine choice, not a flaw, and rejecting them leads to disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jahiliyya disbelieved because they considered human qualities a deficiency. Have you ever felt that your own humanity — your mistakes, your needs, your emotions — makes you unworthy of drawing close to God? What in this lesson says otherwise, and will you let that change how you see yourself?
?
If the prophets were free of all human limitations, they would not be relatable to you. In what area of your life do you most need a prophet who understands your struggles? How does knowing that they ate, walked, and felt illness affect your trust in their guidance today?
?
You are surrounded by people who may mock religious leaders for being 'too human'. The Jahiliyya rejected because of this. Will you be among those who recognize that God chose humans as messengers as a mercy? Make a specific intention to defend the humanity of the prophets when you hear it criticized.

The Wisdom Behind Human Messengers
Sanusi explains wisdom of human messengers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the profound wisdom behind God sending human messengers, including perfections for themselves and their nations, and the angels' envy.

Core Idea
Human prophets reach higher than angels through human humility.

After refuting the Jahiliyya's error, Sanusi unveils the deeper wisdom: the human attributes of prophets are actually perfections for themselves and completions for their nations. The noble angels would envy these prophets for their refined etiquettes and subtle acts of worship. Moreover, human messengers allow intimacy and remove alienation, making it possible for people to learn from them and trust them. This lesson explores these profound benefits.

Guided Path
1
Envision the lifted veil
Read the conditional statement: if the veil were lifted, the Jahiliyya would see the perfections. Notice the contrast.
The perfections are in the very attributes they rejected.
2
Identify the two types of benefit
Sanusi mentions 'كمالات' (perfections for themselves) and 'تكميلات' (completions for nations). See how these differ.
The prophets gain personal perfection; the nations gain guidance.
3
Appreciate the angels' envy
The angels would wish for similar experiences because of the refined etiquettes and subtle acts of worship humans can perform.
This refutes any idea that human attributes are inferior.
4
Understand the function of familiarity
Sanusi explains that human messengers remove alienation and enable teaching through shared nature.
The Qur'anic verse about making an angel as a man confirms this.
5
Final summary of mercy
God's mercy sent outwardly human but inwardly angelic messengers, allowing them to mix with both groups.
This shows the comprehensive wisdom.

The Condition of Not Contradicting Prophets' High Rank
Sanusi explains the condition that human attributes must not contradict the high rank of prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the purpose of the condition that prophets' human attributes must not contradict their high rank, and why this condition guards against diminishing their status.

Core Idea
Prophets' human attributes do not diminish their exalted rank.

Sanusi explains a key condition in defining the attributes of prophets. While prophets possess human traits, these must never lead us to forget their lofty station. This passage clarifies that the condition 'which do not contradict their lofty rank' serves as a safeguard against two related dangers: heedlessness and failure to appreciate God's special care for them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi explains the condition and what it guards against.
The passage is a single sentence but packs a lot of meaning.
2
Identify the two dangers
The passage mentions two dangers: heedlessness (الغفلة) of the prophets' exalted station due to their human appearances, and failure to observe (التفريط) their high worth and God's care for them. Find these in the text.
These dangers are the reason for the condition.
3
Connect to the bigger picture
Understand how this condition maintains proper reverence for prophets. It ensures that despite their human attributes, believers do not lower their respect or forget their special rank.
This condition is part of a larger definition of prophets' attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولنا : ( التي لا تنافي عُلُو رتبتهم ) فاحترزنا بهِ مِنَ الغفلة عن جنابهم الرفيع ، والتفريط بسبب مشاهدة ظواهرهم البشريَّةِ ؛ في مراعاة قدرِهم العليّ، وملاحظةِ اعتناء المولى العظيم بهم، ورفع مَقامِهِمُ الأكمل فوق جميع الخلق .
And as for our saying: 'which do not contradict their lofty rank,' we guard thereby against heedlessness of their exalted station and failure to observe their high worth due to seeing their human appearances, and (we guard) against not observing the care of the Great Master for them and the raising of their most perfect station above all creation.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of a specific condition in the definition of prophets' attributes. The author states that the condition "which do not contradict their lofty rank" serves to prevent two dangers: (1) neglect of the prophets' high status due to focusing on their human outward appearances, and (2) failure to appreciate the special care God has for them and their elevated rank above all creatures. The condition ensures that believers maintain proper reverence despite the human traits of the prophets.

الغفلة
التفريط
العناية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because prophets have human attributes like eating and sleeping, they are not special or can be treated like ordinary people.
Correction: The condition clarifies that these human attributes do not diminish their rank; rather, we must always remember their high status and God's care for them.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the condition 'which do not contradict their lofty rank'?
A) To ensure that prophets have no human attributes.
B) To guard against neglecting the prophets' high status due to their human appearance.
C) To prove that prophets are angels.
D) To deny that prophets eat or drink.

Key Takeaway
The condition that prophets' human attributes do not contradict their high rank ensures that believers do not lose reverence for them due to their physical human appearance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you imagine the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) eating, sleeping, or walking in the marketplace, does your heart still maintain the same awe and reverence for him as the beloved of Allah? Be honest: have you ever allowed his human traits to quietly diminish your sense of his exalted rank? What will you do today to restore that reverence?
?
The condition warns against 'heedlessness of their exalted station due to seeing their human appearances.' Reflect: do you treat the prophets—especially those who faced hardship—as if they were ordinary people who simply happened to be chosen? Or do you truly see them as beings lifted by Allah's care above all creation? If the former, what specific change in your daily thoughts about them will you make?
?
Think of a time when you spoke casually about a prophet without the proper respect—perhaps in a discussion or even in your private thoughts. This condition exposes that as a failure to observe their high worth. Will you repent from that and commit to learning more about their unmatched status so your heart aligns with the truth?

The Wisdom of Sending Human Messengers
Sanusi proves why prophets must be human, not angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets were sent as humans because it allows people to interact with them, recognize their trustworthiness, and learn from them, and this wisdom is supported by the Quran.

Core Idea
Human messengers make divine guidance relatable and verifiable.

Sanusi, in this passage, defends the necessity of human prophets by showing the profound wisdom behind their humanity. He argues that human messengers possess such noble character that even angels envy them, and that their human nature allows people to personally know and trust them. This lesson unpacks that argument and the Quranic support.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses a very compressed style here.
2
Identify the two main benefits
Find the two categories of benefits Sanusi mentions: (1) the spiritual virtues of human messengers that even angels envy, and (2) the practical benefit of relatability and personal verification.
3
Consider the counterfactual
Think about why an angel messenger would fail to achieve these benefits. Then see how the Quranic verse confirms the argument.
This connects to the misconception that angels would be better messengers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأُممهم ؛ بحيثُ يَغتبط بها الملائكةُ الكرام ، ويتمنون وجود مثلها لهم ؛ لما فيها مِنَ الآدابِ الرفيقةِ ، والعبادات الدقيقة التي لم يجدوا مثلها في عباداتهم ، هذا معَ ما فيها مِنْ تأنيس الأمم ، ودفع الوَحشةِ عنهم بمخالطةِ مَنْ هو مِنْ جنسِهم ، ومتَّصف بحَسَبِ الظاهرِ بصفاتهم ، وأمكنهم لأجل الجنسيَّةِ والمخالطة أن يعرفوا أمانته وصدقَهُ ونصيحته والتلقي منه ، ولو كان مَلَكاً .. لَتَعذَّرَ ذلكَ كلُّهُ ؛ قالَ اللهُ تعالى : ﴿ وَلَوْ جَعَلْنَاهُ مَلَكَا لَّجَعَلْنَهُ رَجُلًا وَلَلَبَسْنَا عَلَيْهِم مَّا يَلْبِسُونَ ﴾
to their nations; such that the noble angels envy them and wish for the existence of the like of them for themselves, because of the refined etiquettes and precise acts of worship contained therein, the like of which they have not found in their own acts of worship; this, along with what is in them of familiarizing the nations and repelling loneliness from them by mixing with one who is of their own kind and outwardly described with their attributes, and it was possible for them, due to commonality and mixing, to know his trustworthiness, truthfulness, advice, and learning from him. Had he been an angel, all of that would have been impossible. Allah the Exalted said: 'And if We had made him an angel, We would have made him a man, and We would have confused for them what they are confusing.'
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) for why messengers are human. Sanusi argues that human messengers possess refined manners and detailed worship that even angels envy. They also allow people to interact with someone of their own kind, removing loneliness, and enabling them to recognize his honesty and learn from him. If the messenger were an angel, these benefits would be impossible because angels are not physically relatable. The Quranic verse (6:9) is cited as evidence that if an angel were sent, he would have to appear as a man, creating confusion. The point is that God's wisdom necessitated human messengers.

Key Terms
الملائكة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Angels would make more effective messengers because they are sinless and powerful.
Correction: Sanusi argues the opposite: an angelic messenger would be impossible for humans to relate to and verify personally, and would cause confusion, as the Quran states.

Key Takeaway
God’s wisdom necessitated human messengers to facilitate relatability, verification, and learning.

The Dual Nature of Prophets: A Manifestation of Divine Mercy
Sanusi explains the dual nature of prophets as God's mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the dual nature of prophets—outwardly human, inwardly angelic—is a profound expression of Allah's mercy and enables their role as intermediaries.

Core Idea
Prophets are outwardly human but inwardly angelic – a mercy from Allah.

Sanusi teaches us that God's treatment of creation is rooted in His bounty and mercy. One profound expression of this mercy is the sending of prophets who are human like us, yet possess an inner angelic nature. This dual constitution allows them to mediate between humanity and the divine realm.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage silently. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's words. Notice the opening phrase about God's treatment of creation.
Pay attention to the key terms: الفضل العظيم, الرحمة واللطف.
2
Identify the dual nature
Focus on the description of prophets: 'their outward is human... and their inward is angelic, nay higher.' What does 'nay higher' imply about their inner rank?
The phrase 'بل أعلى' indicates a superiority even over angels.
3
Understand the purpose
Consider why this dual nature is necessary. Sanusi says it allowed their hearts to expand to mix with both groups (humans and angels) and observe both aspects. How does this help in their mission?
This dual access is essential for conveying revelation and guiding humanity.
4
Connect to divine mercy
Reflect on how this arrangement is a manifestation of God's great bounty and mercy. The entire act of sending prophets with this nature stems from mercy.
The passage begins with 'عالَمَ... بمقتضى الفضل العظيم' linking the dual nature directly to mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعامل سبحانَهُ الخلق بمقتضى الفضل العظيم ، والرحمة واللطفِ ؛ بأن بعثَ إليهم رُسُلاً مِنْ أنفسهم ، ظاهرهم بشريٌّ مِنْ جنسِ المبعوث إليهم ، وباطنُهم مَلَكي ، بل أعلى ؛ ولهذا اتَّسَعَتْ قلوبهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ لمخالطة الفريقين ، ومراعاة الجانبين
So He — glorified be He — treated creation according to great bounty, mercy, and kindness, by sending to them messengers from among themselves, whose outward is human, of the same kind as those they were sent to, and whose inward is angelic, nay higher; and because of this their hearts — peace and blessings be upon them — expanded to mix with both groups and to observe both aspects.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage explains God's gracious treatment: He sent messengers who are outwardly human but inwardly angelic (even higher). This dual nature allowed them to connect with both realms. Sanusi emphasizes that this is due to God's bounty and mercy.

Key Terms
الفضل العظيم
الرحمة واللطف
ظاهرهم بشري
باطنهم ملكي
مخالطة الفريقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are only human and have no angelic aspect.
Correction: Sanusi affirms that prophets have an inner angelic nature, even higher than angels, which complements their human outward.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the nature of prophets?
A) They are purely human
B) They are purely angelic
C) They are outwardly human and inwardly angelic
D) They are a different species

Key Takeaway
The prophets' unique combination of human outward and angelic inward enables them to bridge the gap between humanity and the divine, a gift of Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophets were sent from among yourselves, yet their inner reality is angelic. Do you truly recognize the mercy in having a guide who shares your human struggles? What one change will you make today to honor their example?
?
Your own heart is capable of expansion to connect with both worldly and spiritual realms. Which of these two do you prioritize in your daily actions? Commit to one small act this week that elevates your inward state.
