Ibn al-'Arabi on Adam's Intentional Act and Forgetfulness
Ibn al-'Arabi defends prophetic infallibility by analyzing Adam's sin as intentional but forgetful.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn al-'Arabi reconciles Adam's deliberate eating from the tree with his forgetfulness of the covenant, and why only Allah may use such language about prophets.

Core Idea
Adam's disobedience was intentional but his covenant was forgotten, allowing a unique divine reproach.

The great scholar Ibn al-'Arabi offers a subtle defense of prophetic infallibility by distinguishing between Adam's intentional act of eating and his forgetting of the divine command. He shows how the Qur'an itself uses both 'disobeyed' and 'forgot' to address these aspects, and then clarifies that humans must not repeat this language except in recitation. This passage deepens our understanding of how to speak about the prophets with proper reverence.

Guided Path
1
Read Ibn al-'Arabi's statement
Carefully read the Arabic quote from Ibn al-'Arabi and its translation. Notice how he begins by affirming the necessity of exalting prophets above accusations of ignorance.
The quote is within parentheses in the text.
2
Identify the two aspects of Adam's act
Ibn al-'Arabi explains that Adam was intentional in eating (the act itself was deliberate) but forgetful of the covenant (the prohibition). Find the Qur'anic verses he cites for each aspect.
The verse 'And Adam disobeyed' refers to the intentional act; 'but he forgot' refers to his excuse.
3
Understand the divine perspective
Reflect on Ibn al-'Arabi's point that Allah, as Lord, may say 'He disobeyed' as a reproach and 'he forgot' as a favor. This is permissible only for Allah, not for humans.
The term 'tathrib' means reproach, and 'taqrib' means approximation or drawing near.
4
Apply the lesson to our speech
Note the concluding rule: we may only mention such things about prophets when reciting the Qur'an or quoting the Prophet. This teaches us to guard our tongues regarding the status of prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويرحم الله تعالى الإمام العالم ابن العربي حيث قال: ( يجب تنزيه الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام عما نسب إليهم الجهال، ولكن البارئ سبحانه وتعالى بحكمه النافذ وقضائه السابق أسلم آدم إلى الأكل من الشجرة متعمداً للأكل ناسياً للعهد؛ فقال في تعمده: ﴿وَعَصَى آدَمُ﴾، وقال في بيان عذره: ﴿وَلَقَدْ عَهِدْنَا إِلَى آدَمَ مِن قَبْلُ فَنَسِيَ﴾، فمتعلق العمد غير متعلق النسيان، وجاز للمولى تبارك وتعالى أن يقول في عبده لحقه: «عصى» تثريباً، ويعود عليه بفضله فيقول: «نسي» تقريباً، ولا يجوز لأحد منا أن يطلق ذلك على آدم أو يذكره إلا في تلاوة القرآن، أو قول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم). وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا جَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ فِيمَا آتَاهُمَا﴾: فقال الواحدي في ( تفسيره ): ( إن إبليس أتى حواء في غير صورته التي عرفته، وقال لها: ما الذي في بطنك؟ قالت: ما أدري، قال: إني أخاف أن يكون بهيمة أو كلباً أو خنزيراً، وذكرت ذلك لآدم، فلم يزالا في هم من ذلك، ثم أتاها وقال: إن سألت الله تعالى أن يجعله بشراً سوياً مثلك... تسميه عبد الحارث؟ وكان اسم إبليس في الملائكة الحارث، فلم يزل بها حتى غرها، فلما ولدت ولداً سوياً... سمت عبد الحارث برضا آدم عليه السلام؛ وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا ولداً بشراً سوياً... وجَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ﴾ يعني: إبليس، فأوقع الجمع موقع الواحد فيما آتاهما من الولد.
And may Allah have mercy on the eminent scholar Ibn al-'Arabi when he said: 'It is obligatory to exalt the prophets, peace be upon them, above what the ignorant have attributed to them. However, the Creator, exalted be He, by His penetrating decree and prior determination, surrendered Adam to eat from the tree – intentionally for eating, forgetful of the covenant. So He said regarding his intention: {And Adam disobeyed}, and He said regarding the explanation of his excuse: {And We had already made a covenant with Adam before, but he forgot}. So the object of intention is different from the object of forgetfulness. And it is permissible for the Lord, blessed and exalted, to say regarding His servant, due to His right, 'He disobeyed' as a reproach, and He returns to him with His favor saying 'he forgot' as an approximation. And it is not permissible for any of us to say that about Adam or mention it except in recitation of the Qur'an or the saying of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' And as for His statement, the Exalted: {Then when He gave them a righteous [child], they ascribed to Him partners in that which He gave them}: al-Wahidi said in his Tafsir: 'Indeed, Iblis came to Eve in a form other than his known one and said to her: "What is in your belly?" She said: "I do not know." He said: "I fear it may be an animal, a dog, or a pig." She mentioned that to Adam, and they remained in worry about that. Then he came to her and said: "If you ask Allah to make him a sound human like you... will you name him 'Abd al-Harith?" And the name of Iblis among the angels was al-Harith. He kept at her until he deceived her. Then when she gave birth to a sound child... she named him 'Abd al-Harith with the approval of Adam, peace be upon him. That is the statement of the Exalted: {Then when He gave them a righteous [child], they ascribed to Him partners} meaning Iblis. So He used the plural in place of the singular concerning what He gave them of the child.'
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage contains two parts. First, the author cites Ibn al-'Arabi to further explain Adam's disobedience. Ibn al-'Arabi emphasizes that while Adam intentionally ate (the act was deliberate), he was forgetful of the covenant (the prohibition). Therefore, the Qur'an uses 'disobeyed' for the intentional act and 'forgot' as an excuse. This is permissible for Allah to say regarding His servant, but no human may use such language about Adam except when reciting the Qur'an or quoting the Prophet. Second, the author addresses the verse about Adam and Eve naming their child 'Abd al-Harith (servant of al-Harith). Al-Wahidi explains that Iblis deceived Eve into naming the child after him, under the pretense of gratitude. The verse uses the plural 'they ascribed partners' even though only Eve named the child, because Adam consented. This exonerates Adam and Eve from actual shirk, as the naming was done out of ignorance and deception.

Key Terms
ابن العربي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Adam's sin was purely accidental or that he did not sin at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Adam intentionally ate but forgot the covenant, so there was both intention and forgetfulness.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-'Arabi, why does the Qur'an use both 'disobeyed' and 'forgot' for Adam?
A) To show that Adam sinned and then repented.
B) To distinguish between the intentional eating and the forgotten covenant.
C) To indicate that Adam was forced to eat.
D) To demonstrate that Adam was not a prophet.

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-'Arabi defends prophetic infallibility by showing that Adam's disobedience was intentional but his forgetfulness was an excuse, and only Allah may combine reproach and favor in such speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin intentionally, do you truly believe that Allah can turn even your deliberate disobedience into an occasion for closeness—or do you assume your sin has permanently distanced you from Him? How will you act on that belief today?
?
Adam forgot the covenant; what covenant from Allah have you 'forgotten' that you now need to remember and honor, even if your past action was deliberate?
?
If only Allah has the right to combine reproach and favor in speaking of sin, what does that mean for how you speak about others' sins—especially those you consider intentional? Will you restrain your own tongue and leave judgment to Him?

The Naming of 'Abd al-Harith: Deception, Not Shirk
Al-Wahidi explains the verse about ascribing partners through the story of Iblis's deception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the story of Adam and Eve naming their child 'Abd al-Harith, and how this incident does not constitute shirk but was a result of Iblis's deception.

Core Idea
The naming was a deception by Iblis, not actual polytheism.

The passage presents al-Wahidi's commentary on the Qur'anic verse about Adam and Eve ascribing partners to Allah. Through a detailed narrative, al-Wahidi explains that Iblis deceived Eve into naming her child 'Abd al-Harith (servant of al-Harith, Iblis's angelic name), and Adam consented. This clarifies that the verse refers to a misguided action born of ignorance and deceit, not intentional shirk. This lesson helps us understand how the Qur'an can use strong language while still exonerating the prophets from actual sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and al-Wahidi's explanation
Begin by reading the Qur'anic verse and then al-Wahidi's account of the event. Note how Iblis disguises himself and sows doubt about the child's health.
The verse is: {Then when He gave them a righteous [child], they ascribed to Him partners in that which He gave them}.
2
Follow the narrative of deception
Trace the steps: Iblis comes to Eve in a different form, expresses fear about the child, then suggests that if she asks Allah for a sound child, she should name it 'Abd al-Harith. Iblis's angelic name was al-Harith, so this is a form of associating gratitude to Iblis.
The name 'Abd al-Harith means 'servant of al-Harith'.
3
Understand the plural 'they'
Al-Wahidi explains that the verse uses the plural 'they ascribed partners' even though only Eve named the child, because Adam consented. This implicates both, but the action was done under deception.
The Qur'an uses the plural to include Adam's approval.
4
Reflect on the exoneration
The passage shows that the naming was not done out of worship of Iblis but out of gratitude misdirected due to deception. This preserves the infallibility of Adam and Eve from actual shirk.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When faced with fear about something you don't yet have, how often do you turn to Allah with trust, versus letting that fear make you vulnerable to compromising your principles? What specific fear is currently tempting you to make a decision that might not be completely for Allah's sake?
?
Adam and Eve agreed to name their child after Iblis out of a misplaced sense of gratitude. In your own life, are there blessings you attribute partly to your own efforts or to others, forgetting that every good thing comes solely from Allah? How will you correct that today?
?
The deception began with a seemingly harmless suggestion from Iblis. Reflect on a time when a subtle whisper led you away from obedience. What safeguard will you put in place this week to catch such whispers before they lead to action?

Adam's Disobedience and Forgetfulness Reconciled
Sanusi distinguishes between Adam's intentional act and forgetfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi reconciles the verses about Adam's disobedience and forgetfulness to preserve prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
God can reproach and then cover with mercy; Adam's disobedience and forgetfulness refer to different aspects.

In this passage, Sanusi addresses a common objection: how can Adam be a prophet if he disobeyed God? He carefully distinguishes between the intentional act of eating and the forgetting of the covenant, showing that God's assessment allows for both reproach and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Sanusi's own argument come through.
Notice that Sanusi uses the Quranic verses as his primary evidence.
2
Identify the two Quranic verses
Find the references to Adam disobeying (from Ta-Ha 121) and Adam forgetting (from Ta-Ha 115). See how Sanusi uses them.
3
Understand the distinction
Sanusi says the object of intention is different from the object of forgetfulness. Make sure you see that one refers to the act of eating, the other to the covenant.
This distinction resolves the apparent contradiction.
4
Note the prohibition
Sanusi says we cannot call Adam disobedient except when reciting the Quran or quoting the Prophet. This is an important practical guideline.
This safeguards prophetic respect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام عما نسب إليهم الجُهَّالُ، ولكن الباري سبحانه وتعالى بحكمه النافذ وقضائه السابق أسلم آدم إلى الأكل من الشجرة متعمداً للأكل ناسياً للعهد؛ فقال في تعمده: وَعَصَى آدَمُ، وقال في بيان عذره: ﴿وَلَقَدْ عَهِدْنَا إِلَىٰ آدَمَ مِن قَبْلُ فَنَسِيَ﴾، فمُتعلَّقُ العمد غير متعلَّق النسيان، وجاز للمولى تبارك وتعالى أن يقول في عبده لحقه: «عصى» تثريباً(١)، ويعود عليه بفضله فيقول: «نَسِيَ» تقريباً، ولا يجوز لأحد منا أن يُطلق ذلك على آدم أو يذكره إلا في تلاوة القرآن، أو قول النبي ﷺ(٢). وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا جَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ فِيمَا آتَاهُمَا﴾ [الأعراف: ١٩٠]: فقال الواحدي في (تفسيره): (إن إبليس أتى حواء في غير صورته التي عرفته، وقال لها: ما الذي في بطنك؟ قالت: ما أدري، قال: إني أخاف أن يكون بهيمة أو كلباً أو خنزيراً، وذكرت ذلك لآدم، فلم يزالا في هم من ذلك، ثم أتاها وقال: إن سألت الله تعالى أن يجعله بشراً سوياً مثلك... تُسميه عبد الحارث؟ وكان اسم إبليس في الملائكة الحارث، فلم يزل بها حتى غرها، فلما ولدت ولداً سوياً... سمته عبد الحارث برضا آدم عليه السلام؛ وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا وَلَدًا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا... وَجَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ فِيمَا آتَاهُمَا﴾ إذ سَمَّياه عبد الحارث، ولا ينبغي أن يكون عبداً إلا الله، ولم تعرف حواء أنه إبليس، ولم يكن هذا شركاً بالله؛ لأنهما لم يذهبا إلى أن الحارث ربهما، لكنهما قصدا إلى أنه كان سبب نجاته، وتم الكلام عند قوله: ﴿آتَاهُمَا﴾ ثم ذكر كفار مكة فقال: ﴿فَتَعَالَى اللَّهُ عَمَّا يُشْرِكُونَ﴾ (انتهى)(١). قلت: قال ابن العربي في «الأحكام» في توهين هذا القول وتزييفه: (وهذا القول ونحوه مذكور في ضعيف الحديث في «الترمذي» وغيره، وفي الإسرائيليات التي ليس لها ثبات، ولا يُعوِّلُ عليها من له قلب، والقول الأشبه بالحق: أن المراد بهذا جنس الآدميين)(٢). وأما قول آدم عليه السلام: ﴿رَبَّنَا ظَلَمْنَا أَنفُسَنَا﴾ [الأعراف: ٢٣]: فقول صدر منه على سبيل الاستكانة والتعظيم لجناب أوامر المولى تبارك وتعالى ومناهيه؛ بحيث يَحِق على العبيد أن لو كان الأمر بأيديهم ألا بوجه من الوجوه، لا عمداً ولا نسياناً، ولا بانتهاك مخالفة تقع منهم ولا بتأويل، وأشار عليه السلام بذلك إلى أنه لا حجة للعبد على سيده، ولا يعتذر لنفسه فيما خالف من أمره تعالى ونهيه، ولا حق له.

(١) التثريب: اللوم.
(٢) انظر «أحكام القرآن» لابن العربي (٢٥٩/٣).
(١) انظر «الوجيز» (ص ٤٢٥).
(٢) انظر «أحكام القرآن» (٢/٣٥٥).
The prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, from what the ignorant have attributed to them. But the Creator, glorified and exalted, by His penetrating decree and prior judgment, delivered Adam to eating from the tree, intentionally eating, forgetting the covenant. So He said regarding his intention: 'And Adam disobeyed,' and He said regarding the clarification of his excuse: 'And We had already taken a covenant from Adam before, but he forgot.' So the object of intention is not the object of forgetfulness. It is permissible for the Master, blessed and exalted, to say concerning His servant of His right: 'He disobeyed' as a reproach, and He returns to him with His favor and says: 'He forgot' as an approximation. It is not permissible for any of us to say that about Adam or mention it except in reciting the Quran or the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him. And as for His saying, exalted: 'Then when He gave them a righteous [child], they made partners for Him in what He had given them' [al-A'raf: 190] - al-Wahidi said in his Tafsir: 'Indeed Iblis came to Eve in other than his form that she knew, and said to her: What is in your belly? She said: I do not know. He said: I fear it may be a beast, a dog, or a pig. She mentioned that to Adam, and they did not cease to be worried about that. Then he came to her and said: If you ask Allah, exalted, to make him a sound human like you... would you name him 'Abd al-Harith? And the name of Iblis among the angels was al-Harith. He did not cease with her until he deceived her. When she gave birth to a sound child... she named him 'Abd al-Harith with the consent of Adam, peace be upon him. That is His saying, exalted: 'Then when He gave them a righteous child, a sound human... they made partners for Him in what He had given them' because they named him 'Abd al-Harith. It is not fitting that any be a servant except Allah. Eve did not know that it was Iblis. This was not polytheism towards Allah because they did not intend that al-Harith is their lord, but they intended that he was the cause of his salvation. The speech is completed at His saying: 'He gave them,' then He mentioned the disbelievers of Mecca and said: 'Exalted is Allah above what they associate [with Him].' (End.) I say: Ibn al-'Arabi said in 'al-Ahkam' in weakening this saying and falsifying it: 'This saying and the like are mentioned in weak hadith in al-Tirmidhi and others, and in the Isra'iliyyat which have no stability, and one who has a heart does not rely on them. The saying more resembling the truth is that what is meant by this is the genus of human beings.' And as for the saying of Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' [al-A'raf: 23] - it is a saying issued from him in a manner of humility and magnification of the majesty of the commands and prohibitions of the Master, blessed and exalted, such that it is incumbent upon servants that if the matter were in their hands, they would not do anything at all: neither intentionally nor forgetfully, nor by committing a violation that occurs from them, nor by interpretation. He, peace be upon him, indicated by that that there is no argument for the servant against his master, and he does not excuse himself regarding what he has opposed of His command and prohibition, and he has no right.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the prophets (specifically Adam and Eve) against accusations of sin based on apparent meanings of Quranic verses. The author first addresses the verse about Adam's disobedience and forgetfulness (Ta-Ha 115 and 121). He explains that God's statement that Adam 'disobeyed' refers to the intentional act of eating, while 'he forgot' refers to the covenant; the two statements are not contradictory because they concern different aspects. God may reproach His servant for a right due to Him, yet also cover him with mercy by calling it forgetfulness. However, we as humans are not allowed to label Adam with 'disobedience' except when reciting the Quran or repeating the Prophet's words. Next, the author discusses the verse about Adam and Eve making partners for God (al-A'raf 190) by reporting al-Wahidi's interpretation: Iblis tricked Eve into naming their child 'Abd al-Harith (thinking he was a righteous angel), but they did not consider al-Harith a god; it was only a name signifying that he was a cause of the child's safety, not true polytheism. The author then quotes Ibn al-'Arabi who weakens this narrative as weak hadith and Isra'iliyyat, and states that the verse actually refers to the descendants of Adam in general (i.e., people who are given children and then commit shirk). Finally, the author interprets Adam's statement 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' as an expression of extreme humility and reverence for God's commands, not an admission of actual sin. Adam is showing that a servant has no excuse before his Master, even if the apparent action is not sinful. The overall point is that the prophets are innocent of the sins attributed to them by the ignorant.

Key Terms
عصيان
نسيان
تثريب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran contradicts itself by saying Adam both disobeyed and forgot.
Correction: The two statements refer to different objects (act vs. covenant), so there is no contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it not contradictory that God said both 'Adam disobeyed' and 'Adam forgot'?
A) Because one statement is abrogated by the other.
B) Because the object of intention is different from the object of forgetfulness.
C) Because the word 'disobeyed' refers to Eve, not Adam.
D) Because the verse is metaphorical and not to be taken literally.

Key Takeaway
Adam's actions are interpreted by God from two angles: intentional disobedience and excusable forgetfulness, preserving his prophetic status.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you used the excuse of forgetfulness to dismiss a deliberate sin? How does this passage challenge you to face your intentional disobedience without hiding behind excuses?
?
If God can reproach Adam for His right and then cover with mercy, what does that mean for the way you treat your own failures? Will you let God's mercy be greater than your guilt, or do you cling to self-condemnation?
?
This passage shows that a prophet can have a real, intentional sin that God still covers. How does that change your view of your own slip-ups? Are you willing to trust that God can use you despite your faults, as He did with Adam?

The 'Abd al-Harith Narrative and Its Refutation
Sanusi reports and then refutes a weak interpretation of al-A'raf 190.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the weak tradition about Adam and Eve naming their child 'Abd al-Harith and why scholars reject it.

Core Idea
The 'Abd al-Harith story is weak and based on Isra'iliyyat; the verse actually refers to idolaters among Adam's descendants.

Sanusi presents a controversial interpretation from al-Wahidi involving Iblis tricking Eve into naming their child 'Abd al-Harith. He then quotes Ibn al-'Arabi's decisive refutation, showing that such narratives are unreliable and that the true meaning of the verse is general.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative from al-Wahidi
Read the story of Iblis and Eve as reported by al-Wahidi. Notice the details: Iblis comes in disguise, suggests naming the child 'Abd al-Harith, and Adam consents.
This story is presented to explain the verse but is later criticized.
2
Identify the theological problem
The story implies that Adam and Eve named their child 'Abd al-Harith, which could be seen as associating a partner with God (shirk). Sanusi notes that they did not intend shirk, but Ibn al-'Arabi rejects the whole narrative.
3
Read Ibn al-'Arabi's critique
Ibn al-'Arabi says this story is found in weak hadith and Isra'iliyyat, which are unreliable. He gives the correct interpretation: the verse refers to the descendants of Adam (humanity) who commit shirk.
This is the scholarly consensus.
4
Understand the correct interpretation
The verse 'they make partners for Him' refers to later polytheists, not Adam and Eve. The prophets are innocent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام عما نسب إليهم الجُهَّالُ، ولكن الباري سبحانه وتعالى بحكمه النافذ وقضائه السابق أسلم آدم إلى الأكل من الشجرة متعمداً للأكل ناسياً للعهد؛ فقال في تعمده: وَعَصَى آدَمُ، وقال في بيان عذره: ﴿وَلَقَدْ عَهِدْنَا إِلَىٰ آدَمَ مِن قَبْلُ فَنَسِيَ﴾، فمُتعلَّقُ العمد غير متعلَّق النسيان، وجاز للمولى تبارك وتعالى أن يقول في عبده لحقه: «عصى» تثريباً(١)، ويعود عليه بفضله فيقول: «نَسِيَ» تقريباً، ولا يجوز لأحد منا أن يُطلق ذلك على آدم أو يذكره إلا في تلاوة القرآن، أو قول النبي ﷺ(٢). وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا جَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ فِيمَا آتَاهُمَا﴾ [الأعراف: ١٩٠]: فقال الواحدي في (تفسيره): (إن إبليس أتى حواء في غير صورته التي عرفته، وقال لها: ما الذي في بطنك؟ قالت: ما أدري، قال: إني أخاف أن يكون بهيمة أو كلباً أو خنزيراً، وذكرت ذلك لآدم، فلم يزالا في هم من ذلك، ثم أتاها وقال: إن سألت الله تعالى أن يجعله بشراً سوياً مثلك... تُسميه عبد الحارث؟ وكان اسم إبليس في الملائكة الحارث، فلم يزل بها حتى غرها، فلما ولدت ولداً سوياً... سمته عبد الحارث برضا آدم عليه السلام؛ وذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَمَّا آتَاهُمَا صَالِحًا وَلَدًا بَشَرًا سَوِيًّا... وَجَعَلَا لَهُ شُرَكَاءَ فِيمَا آتَاهُمَا﴾ إذ سَمَّياه عبد الحارث، ولا ينبغي أن يكون عبداً إلا الله، ولم تعرف حواء أنه إبليس، ولم يكن هذا شركاً بالله؛ لأنهما لم يذهبا إلى أن الحارث ربهما، لكنهما قصدا إلى أنه كان سبب نجاته، وتم الكلام عند قوله: ﴿آتَاهُمَا﴾ ثم ذكر كفار مكة فقال: ﴿فَتَعَالَى اللَّهُ عَمَّا يُشْرِكُونَ﴾ (انتهى)(١). قلت: قال ابن العربي في «الأحكام» في توهين هذا القول وتزييفه: (وهذا القول ونحوه مذكور في ضعيف الحديث في «الترمذي» وغيره، وفي الإسرائيليات التي ليس لها ثبات، ولا يُعوِّلُ عليها من له قلب، والقول الأشبه بالحق: أن المراد بهذا جنس الآدميين)(٢). وأما قول آدم عليه السلام: ﴿رَبَّنَا ظَلَمْنَا أَنفُسَنَا﴾ [الأعراف: ٢٣]: فقول صدر منه على سبيل الاستكانة والتعظيم لجناب أوامر المولى تبارك وتعالى ومناهيه؛ بحيث يَحِق على العبيد أن لو كان الأمر بأيديهم ألا بوجه من الوجوه، لا عمداً ولا نسياناً، ولا بانتهاك مخالفة تقع منهم ولا بتأويل، وأشار عليه السلام بذلك إلى أنه لا حجة للعبد على سيده، ولا يعتذر لنفسه فيما خالف من أمره تعالى ونهيه، ولا حق له.

(١) التثريب: اللوم.
(٢) انظر «أحكام القرآن» لابن العربي (٢٥٩/٣).
(١) انظر «الوجيز» (ص ٤٢٥).
(٢) انظر «أحكام القرآن» (٢/٣٥٥).
The prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, from what the ignorant have attributed to them. But the Creator, glorified and exalted, by His penetrating decree and prior judgment, delivered Adam to eating from the tree, intentionally eating, forgetting the covenant. So He said regarding his intention: 'And Adam disobeyed,' and He said regarding the clarification of his excuse: 'And We had already taken a covenant from Adam before, but he forgot.' So the object of intention is not the object of forgetfulness. It is permissible for the Master, blessed and exalted, to say concerning His servant of His right: 'He disobeyed' as a reproach, and He returns to him with His favor and says: 'He forgot' as an approximation. It is not permissible for any of us to say that about Adam or mention it except in reciting the Quran or the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him. And as for His saying, exalted: 'Then when He gave them a righteous [child], they made partners for Him in what He had given them' [al-A'raf: 190] - al-Wahidi said in his Tafsir: 'Indeed Iblis came to Eve in other than his form that she knew, and said to her: What is in your belly? She said: I do not know. He said: I fear it may be a beast, a dog, or a pig. She mentioned that to Adam, and they did not cease to be worried about that. Then he came to her and said: If you ask Allah, exalted, to make him a sound human like you... would you name him 'Abd al-Harith? And the name of Iblis among the angels was al-Harith. He did not cease with her until he deceived her. When she gave birth to a sound child... she named him 'Abd al-Harith with the consent of Adam, peace be upon him. That is His saying, exalted: 'Then when He gave them a righteous child, a sound human... they made partners for Him in what He had given them' because they named him 'Abd al-Harith. It is not fitting that any be a servant except Allah. Eve did not know that it was Iblis. This was not polytheism towards Allah because they did not intend that al-Harith is their lord, but they intended that he was the cause of his salvation. The speech is completed at His saying: 'He gave them,' then He mentioned the disbelievers of Mecca and said: 'Exalted is Allah above what they associate [with Him].' (End.) I say: Ibn al-'Arabi said in 'al-Ahkam' in weakening this saying and falsifying it: 'This saying and the like are mentioned in weak hadith in al-Tirmidhi and others, and in the Isra'iliyyat which have no stability, and one who has a heart does not rely on them. The saying more resembling the truth is that what is meant by this is the genus of human beings.' And as for the saying of Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' [al-A'raf: 23] - it is a saying issued from him in a manner of humility and magnification of the majesty of the commands and prohibitions of the Master, blessed and exalted, such that it is incumbent upon servants that if the matter were in their hands, they would not do anything at all: neither intentionally nor forgetfully, nor by committing a violation that occurs from them, nor by interpretation. He, peace be upon him, indicated by that that there is no argument for the servant against his master, and he does not excuse himself regarding what he has opposed of His command and prohibition, and he has no right.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the prophets (specifically Adam and Eve) against accusations of sin based on apparent meanings of Quranic verses. The author first addresses the verse about Adam's disobedience and forgetfulness (Ta-Ha 115 and 121). He explains that God's statement that Adam 'disobeyed' refers to the intentional act of eating, while 'he forgot' refers to the covenant; the two statements are not contradictory because they concern different aspects. God may reproach His servant for a right due to Him, yet also cover him with mercy by calling it forgetfulness. However, we as humans are not allowed to label Adam with 'disobedience' except when reciting the Quran or repeating the Prophet's words. Next, the author discusses the verse about Adam and Eve making partners for God (al-A'raf 190) by reporting al-Wahidi's interpretation: Iblis tricked Eve into naming their child 'Abd al-Harith (thinking he was a righteous angel), but they did not consider al-Harith a god; it was only a name signifying that he was a cause of the child's safety, not true polytheism. The author then quotes Ibn al-'Arabi who weakens this narrative as weak hadith and Isra'iliyyat, and states that the verse actually refers to the descendants of Adam in general (i.e., people who are given children and then commit shirk). Finally, the author interprets Adam's statement 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' as an expression of extreme humility and reverence for God's commands, not an admission of actual sin. Adam is showing that a servant has no excuse before his Master, even if the apparent action is not sinful. The overall point is that the prophets are innocent of the sins attributed to them by the ignorant.

إسرائيليات
ضعيف الحديث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adam and Eve committed shirk by naming their child 'Abd al-Harith.
Correction: The story is weak; the verse actually refers to later generations of idolaters.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-'Arabi, what is the most correct interpretation of the verse 'they made partners for Him'?
A) It refers to Adam and Eve naming their child 'Abd al-Harith.
B) It refers to polytheists among Adam's descendants.
C) It is unclear and cannot be interpreted.
D) It refers to angels being worshipped.

Key Takeaway
The weak 'Abd al-Harith narrative is rejected; the verse 'they made partners' refers to later idolaters, not Adam and Eve.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a religious story or teaching without verifying its source, simply because it was repeated often? What story comes to mind, and how can you check its authenticity from today onward?
?
If you learned that a common belief about a prophet (like this one about Adam and Eve) was based on weak evidence, how would you correct yourself and others without causing fitna? What specific words from this lesson would you use to do so?
?
The scholar Ibn al-Arabi said that one who has a heart does not rely on such weak reports. What does it mean to have a 'heart' in this context? Is your heart sensitive enough to reject falsehood even when it feels comforting or familiar? What will you do this week to strengthen that sensitivity?

Adam's Statement 'We Have Wronged Ourselves' as Humility
Sanusi interprets Adam's statement as humility and reverence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Adam's confession of wrongdoing is an expression of profound humility and reverence, not an admission of actual sin.

Core Idea
Adam's 'wronging ourselves' shows a servant's total submission, not an actual sin.

The final part of the passage addresses Adam's Quranic plea 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves.' Sanusi explains that this is not an admission of sin but a demonstration of the servant's complete humility before God's commands, indicating that even if there is no actual fault, the servant has no excuse.

Guided Path
1
Read Adam's statement and Sanusi's explanation
Read the passage where Sanusi interprets Adam's words 'We have wronged ourselves' (al-A'raf 23).
Pay attention to the terms 'استكانة' (humility) and 'تعظيم' (magnification).
2
Understand the context of humility
Sanusi says Adam spoke out of humility and reverence for God's commands. Even if an action is not sinful, a servant should show complete submission.
3
Realize the protection of Prophetic infallibility
Since prophets are sinless, Adam's words cannot be an admission of actual sin. They serve as a model of how a servant should address God.
4
Summarize the key point
Adam's statement is a rhetorical expression of humility, not a confession of guilt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Adam actually sinned by eating from the tree, and his confession 'we have wronged ourselves' proves it.
Correction: Adam's statement is an expression of humility and reverence, not an admission of actual sin, consistent with prophetic infallibility.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why did Adam say 'We have wronged ourselves'?
A) He actually committed a sin and was repenting.
B) To show humility and reverence for God's commands, despite being sinless.
C) He was quoting what Iblis told him to say.
D) He forgot that he was a prophet.

Key Takeaway
Adam's confession is a model of humility, not an admission of sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall short in obeying Allah, do you instinctively reach for excuses—'I forgot,' 'I didn't mean to,' 'I interpreted it differently'—rather than adopting Adam's posture of utter humility? How would your relationship with Allah change if you stopped arguing and simply said, 'I have no excuse before You'?
?
Consider a moment when you felt justified in a sin because you thought your intention was good or your circumstances were special. Does Adam's model—where he does not even claim a valid interpretation—expose a hidden pride in your heart? What would it cost you to drop every excuse and stand before Allah with nothing but humility?
?
Adam's statement magnifies the majesty of God's commands. The next time you are tempted to downplay a prohibition, will you remember that the Creator's command is so great that even an unintentional violation is not to be excused? Can you honestly say you tremble at every command, or have you become comfortable with selective obedience? What will you do to change that today?

Defending Adam and Hawwa from Shirk: The Naming of 'Abd al-Harith
Author defends Adam and Hawwa from shirk and cites Ibn al-Arabi's critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the act of Adam and Hawwa naming their son 'Abd al-Harith does not constitute shirk, according to the author's reasoning.

Core Idea
Intent determines shirk; means are not lords.

This passage addresses a potential misunderstanding about the prophetic couple Adam and Hawwa. Some might think that by naming their child 'Abd al-Harith (servant of the cultivator), they committed shirk. The author clarifies their true intention and defends them from this accusation, also citing Ibn al-Arabi's critique of weak narrations used to support such claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the source text carefully. Notice how the author directly addresses the naming incident and provides his reasoning.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لم يكن هذا شركا بالله'.
2
Understand the core argument against shirk
The author explains that Adam and Hawwa did not consider al-Harith as a lord, only as a cause of salvation. Reflect on why this distinction matters in defining shirk.
Shirk is about intent, not mere naming.
3
Examine Ibn al-Arabi's critique
Ibn al-Arabi dismisses the narration linking this event as weak hadith or Isra'iliyyat. Consider the methodological point: not all reports about prophets are reliable.
This reinforces the defense by questioning the source.
4
Apply the lesson
Think about how this reasoning protects prophets from false accusations and teaches us to evaluate reports critically.
The principle: means of salvation ≠ object of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذ سمَّياه عبد الحارثِ ، ولا ينبغي أن يكون عبداً إلا الله ، ولم تَعرِفْ حواء أنَّهُ إبليس ، ولم يكن هذا شِرْكاً باللهِ ؛ لأنَّهُما لم يذهبا إلى أنَّ الحارث ربُّهما ، لكنَّهما قصدا إلى أنَّهُ كانَ سبب نجاتِهِ ، وتم الكلامُ عند قوله : واتَنهُمَا ﴾ ، ثمَّ ذكرَ كُفَّارَ مكَّةَ فقالَ : فَتَعَلَى اللَّهُ عَمَّا يُشْرِكُونَ ( انتهى ! (۱) قلتُ : قالَ ابنُ العربي في الأحكام » في توهين هذا القول وتزييفه : ( وهذا القولُ ونحوه مذكور في ضعيف الحديث في الترمذي » وغيرِه ، وفي الإسرائيليات التي ليس لها ثبات ، ولا يُعوِّلُ عليها مَنْ له قلب ، والقولُ الأشبه بالحقِّ : أنَّ المراد بهذا جنس الآدميين ((٢) . وأما قولُ آدم عليهِ السلامُ : رَبَّنَا ظَلَمْنَا أَنفُسَنَا [الأعراف : ٢٣] : فقول ﴾ صدرَ منه على سبيل الاستكانة والتعظيم لجنابِ أوامر المولى تبارك وتعالى ومناهيهِ ؛ بحيثُ يَحِقُ على العبيدِ أنْ لو كان الأمر بأيديهم ألا بوجهِ مِنَ الوجوه ، لا عمداً ولا نسياناً ، ولا بانتهاك مخالفة تقع منهم ولا بتأويل ، وأشار عليهِ السلامُ بذلكَ إلى أنَّهُ لا حُجَّةَ للعبدِ على سيّدِهِ ، ولا يَعتذِرُ لنفسِهِ فيما خالفَ مِنْ أمرِهِ تعالى ونهيه ، ولا حق لهُ على المولى العظيم أن يَعذِرَهُ بنسيان أو تأويل ، بلِ الحُجَّةُ للمولى تبارك وتعالى على كلِّ حالٍ ، وحكمه على عبدِهِ بأَنَّهُ معذور في بعض الأحوال.. محض فضل منه جلَّ وعلا ، ولهُ أنْ يُعذِّبَ مَنْ يَشَاءُ ويرحم مَنْ يَشَاءُ ، وهو المحمودُ المُنزَّهُ عَنِ النقص والظُّلْمِ على كلِّ حالٍ
When they named him 'Abd al-Harith, while it is not befitting that anyone be a servant except Allah, and Hawwa did not know that it was Iblis, and this was not shirk with Allah because they did not intend that al-Harith was their lord, but they intended that he was the cause of their salvation. And the speech is completed at His saying 'and He gave them both [the tree]' then He mentioned the disbelievers of Mecca and said 'Exalted is Allah above what they associate [with Him]' (end). I said: Ibn al-Arabi said in al-Ahkam regarding weakening this statement and refuting it: 'This statement and the like are mentioned in weak hadith in al-Tirmidhi and others, and in Isra'iliyyat that have no stability, and one who has a heart does not rely on them. The statement most resembling the truth is that what is meant by this is the generality of Adam's children.' And as for the saying of Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' [al-A'raf 23] – it is a saying that issued from him by way of humility and veneration of the commands of the Sovereign, Blessed and Exalted, and His prohibitions; such that it becomes incumbent upon the servants that if the matter were in their hands, they would not do it in any way, neither intentionally nor forgetfully, nor by violating a prohibition occurring from them nor by interpretation. And he, peace be upon him, indicated by that that there is no proof for the servant against his Master, and he does not excuse himself in what he has contravened of His command and prohibition, and he has no right upon the Great Master to excuse him by forgetfulness or interpretation. Rather, the proof belongs to the Sovereign, Blessed and Exalted, in every case, and His judgment upon His servant that he is excused in some circumstances is pure grace from Him, Glorious and Exalted, and He has the right to punish whom He wills and have mercy on whom He wills, and He is Praiseworthy, Transcendent above deficiency and injustice in every case.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the prophets Adam and Hawwa from accusations of shirk and sin, and an interpretation of Adam's statement in the Quran. The author begins by refuting the claim that naming their child 'Abd al-Harith constituted shirk, explaining that they only considered al-Harith a means of salvation, not a lord. He then references a tafsir that connects this to the disbelievers of Mecca. Following this, the author mentions Ibn al-Arabi's critique of such narrations as weak or based on Isra'iliyyat. The core of the passage is the explanation of Adam's verse 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves.' The author argues that this is not an admission of sin but an expression of profound humility and recognition of God's sovereignty. He explains that Adam's words emphasize that the servant has no claim against his Master, and any excuse for failing to obey perfectly is purely by God's grace. The passage concludes by affirming God's absolute freedom to punish or forgive, and His transcendence above any deficiency or injustice.

Key Terms
عبد الحارث
شرك
إسرائيليات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Adam and Hawwa committed shirk by naming their child 'Abd al-Harith.
Correction: The author argues they did not intend shirk, seeing al-Harith only as a means, not a deity; furthermore, the narrations are weak.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why was naming their child 'Abd al-Harith not shirk?
A) Because Hawwa did not know it was Iblis
B) Because they considered al-Harith a cause, not a lord
C) Because the Quran explicitly permits it
D) Because Ibn al-Arabi said so

Key Takeaway
Adam and Hawwa's naming of 'Abd al-Harith was not shirk because they saw al-Harith as a means, not a deity, and the narrations implying otherwise are unreliable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's action as shirk without knowing their true intention? How does the example of Adam and Hawwa challenge your quick judgments? What would it take for you to give others the same benefit of the doubt in matters of faith?
?
Do you have any habits where you rely on 'causes' (like people or material means) almost as if they have independent power? How does this lesson's distinction between cause and Lord force you to re-examine where your trust truly lies?

Interpreting Adam's Confession: Humility, Not Admission of Sin
Author explains Adam's Quranic confession as humility and veneration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's interpretation of Adam's Quranic statement 'Rabbana zalamna anfusana' as an expression of humility and divine sovereignty, not an admission of sin.

Core Idea
Adam's confession is humility, not sin.

Adam's words in the Quran, 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves,' might seem like an admission of sin. The author explains that this saying was an act of profound humility and reverence for God's commands, emphasizing that the servant has no standing before the Master. This interpretation protects the prophetic status of Adam while affirming God's absolute sovereignty and grace.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the source text. Notice how the author describes the manner in which Adam's statement was made.
Key phrase: 'على سبيل الاستكانة والتعظيم'
2
Understand the concept of 'istikanah'
The author says the statement was 'by way of humility and veneration.' Reflect on how this differs from admitting a sinful act.
Humility acknowledges God's greatness, not necessarily wrongdoing.
3
Recognize the implication about divine sovereignty
Adam's words show that the servant has no claim against God; any excuse (forgetfulness, interpretation) is not a right but pure grace. Consider how this relates to God's absolute authority.
The lesson: God is justified in all His judgments.
4
Connect to the broader theological point
The author concludes that God is free to punish or forgive, and is beyond deficiency. See how this interpretation safeguards God's justice and mercy.
This passage ties into predestination and divine justice.

?

?

?
If you truly believed you have no right to be excused by forgetfulness or interpretation, how would your prayer of repentance change tonight? Would it become more desperate, more humble, more reliant on God's mercy alone?

The Educational Discipline of Prophet Yunus
The author defends Yunus and explains the discipline as educational.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the story of Prophet Yunus contains no sin but rather an educational discipline from Allah, demonstrating the special status and higher standard required of prophets.

Core Idea
Allah’s discipline of Yunus was teaching, not punishment.

The story of Prophet Yunus is sometimes misunderstood as implying sin. However, the author clarifies that the Quranic account does not mention any sin, and the disciplinary event was a means of training for the future. This lesson unpacks that argument and reveals how prophets are held to a unique standard.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the full argument. Note the key terms 'abaqa' (fled) and 'mughadiban' (in anger).
These terms are central to the author's claim that no sin is implied.
2
Identify the general vs. specific ruling
The author notes that avoiding disbelievers is normally among the greatest acts of obedience. But for Yunus, due to his special role, a different standard applies.
This contrast highlights the prophetic rank.
3
Understand the purpose of the discipline
The discipline is explicitly called 'teaching and training for the future,' not punishment. See the phrase 'تأديب تعليم وترييض للمستقبل'.
This is the core doctrinal point.
4
Reflect on the inward meaning
The author says the discipline showed Allah's great care and honor for Yunus, as He personally undertook his upbringing.
This refutes the idea of punishment or anger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا قصَّةُ يونس عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : فليس فيها نص على ذنبٍ وإنَّما فيها : أبق وذهب مغاضباً ، وهما راجعان إلى قومه ؛ أي هرب منهم وذهب مغاضباً لهم لكفرهم ، ومجانبة أهل الكفرِ وهِجْرانُ أوطانهم مِنْ أكبر الطاعاتِ لو صدرا مِنْ غيرِهِ ، إِلا أَنَّ الله سبحانَهُ نَبَّهَ يونس عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ بذلك التأديب . . أنَّه ليس كغيره في هذا ؛ لأَنَّهُ مِنْ خواص حضرتِهِ ، المبعوث لهداية الخلْقِ مِنْ عندِهِ ، ولا يحصل المقصودُ مِنْ هدايتهم على التمام إلا بصبره على جفائهم ومشاهدة ضلالهم ، فلا يتصرَّفُ هو إذاً إلا بالإذنِ الخاص ، لا بالإذنِ العام كغيره فذلك التأديب تعليم وترييض للمستقبل ، لا عقوبة عن ذَنْبٍ كما يعتقدُهُ مَنْ جَهِلَ وباطنُ ذلك التأديب يدلُّ على الاعتناء العظيم بيونس عليهِ السلام ، والتشريف له بتولّي المولى العظيم لتربيته وترييضه بلطيف تدبيره ، ولم يكلْهُ في ذلك لنفسِهِ ، ولا لأحدٍ مِنْ عبيدِهِ وأما قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا أَنتَ سُبْحَنَكَ إِنِّي كُنتُ مِنَ الظَّالِمِينَ [الأنبياء : ۸۷] : فالجواب عنه ما سبق في قولِ آدمَ عليهِ السلامُ : رَبَّنَا ظَلَمْنَا أَنفُسَنَا ﴾ [الأعراف : ٢٣] .
As for the story of Yunus, peace be upon him: there is no text in it about a sin. Rather, in it [there is] 'he ran away' and 'he went in anger,' both referring to his people: i.e., he fled from them and went in anger with them due to their disbelief. Avoiding people of disbelief and abandoning one's homeland are among the greatest acts of obedience if done by other than him, except that Allah, Glorified, admonished Yunus, peace be upon him, with that discipline... that he is not like others in this; because he is among the special ones of His presence, sent for guidance of creation from Him, and the purpose of guiding them is not fully achieved except by his patience with their harshness and witnessing their misguidance. Therefore, he does not act except by special permission, not by general permission like others. So that discipline is teaching and training for the future, not punishment for a sin as someone ignorant thinks. The inward of that discipline indicates great care for Yunus, peace be upon him, and honor for him by the Great Master undertaking his upbringing and training with His gentle planning, and He did not entrust that to himself nor to any of His servants. And as for his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is no god but You, exalted are You, indeed I have been of the wrongdoers' [al-Anbiya 87] – the answer to it is what preceded in the saying of Adam, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' [al-A'raf 23].
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Prophet Yunus from the accusation that he sinned by leaving his people. The author argues that the Quranic text contains no explicit mention of a sin; rather, the terms used indicate that Yunus fled from his people in anger due to their disbelief. The author notes that avoiding disbelievers and leaving one's homeland are normally among the greatest acts of obedience. However, because Yunus is a special prophet chosen for guidance, God disciplined him to teach him that he must act only by special permission and must be patient with his people. This discipline is described as teaching and training for the future, not punishment for a sin. The inward meaning of this discipline is one of honor, as God Himself undertook his upbringing. Finally, the author connects Yunus's supplication 'La ilaha illa anta...' to the same explanation given for Adam's confession, reinforcing that it is an expression of humility, not an admission of sin.

Key Terms
تأديب
خواص الحضرة
إذن خاص
تعليم وترييض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophet Yunus committed a sin by leaving his people in anger.
Correction: The passage clarifies that his actions were not sinful; they were normally acts of obedience. The discipline was educational training, not punishment, and the inward meaning was honor.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the purpose of the discipline given to Yunus?
A) Punishment for his sin
B) Teaching and training for the future
C) To make him an example for others
D) To show God's anger

Key Takeaway
The discipline of Prophet Yunus was an act of honor and training, not punishment, because of his special prophetic rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficulty or setback in life, do you immediately assume it is punishment for a past mistake, or could it be that Allah is training you for a greater purpose you do not yet see? How would your heart respond today if you believed that every trial is a sign of Allah's care for you personally?
?
Prophet Yunus was so honored that Allah personally undertook his upbringing and training. Do you feel that sense of honor when Allah disciplines you, or do you feel abandoned and resentful? What would change in your life if you truly believed that His discipline is education, not punishment?
?
The ordinary believer is allowed to avoid harsh people, but the prophet must stay and be patient. Are there people in your life whom you avoid because they are difficult? Could it be that Allah wants you to remain patient with them for a purpose, and that leaving them might be a missed opportunity for growth? What would it cost you to stay?

The Story of Yunus: No Sin, Only Divine Discipline
Sanusi explains that Yunus's actions were not sinful but a form of dutiful piety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Prophet Yunus's action of leaving his people was not a sin but a disciplined teaching from Allah due to his special prophetic rank.

Core Idea
Prophetic actions are judged by special permission, not general standards.

The story of Prophet Yunus is often misunderstood as implying sin. Sanusi clarifies that the Qur'an does not mention a sin; rather, Yunus's flight was a great act of obedience for an ordinary person. But because he is a prophet with a unique mission, Allah disciplined him to train him for future patience. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the full argument from Sanusi. Notice his opening statement that there is no text indicating a sin.
The passage uses technical terms like 'special permission' (الإذن الخاص).
2
Identify the key claims
Sanusi makes two main points: (1) Yunus's actions (fleeing, going angrily) are normally great acts of obedience, but (2) for him they required special permission because of his prophetic role. Find these in the text.
3
Understand the discipline’s purpose
Sanusi explains that the discipline was teaching and training for the future, not punishment. Reflect on how this differs from common assumptions.
4
Grasp the inner meaning
The discipline actually indicates Allah's great care and honor for Yunus. Consider how this reframes the entire event.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا قصَّةُ يونس عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : فليس فيها نص على ذنبٍ وإنَّما فيها : أبق وذهب مغاضباً ، وهما راجعان إلى قومه ؛ أي هرب منهم وذهب مغاضباً لهم لكفرهم ، ومجانبة أهل الكفرِ وهِجْرانُ أوطانهم مِنْ أكبر الطاعاتِ لو صدرا مِنْ غيرِهِ ، إِلا أَنَّ الله سبحانَهُ نَبَّهَ يونس عليه الصلاةُ والسلامُ بذلك التأديب . . أنَّه ليس كغيره في هذا ؛ لأَنَّهُ مِنْ خواص حضرتِهِ ، المبعوث لهداية الخلْقِ مِنْ عندِهِ ، ولا يحصل المقصودُ مِنْ هدايتهم على التمام إلا بصبره على جفائهم ومشاهدة ضلالهم ، فلا يتصرَّفُ هو إذاً إلا بالإذنِ الخاص ، لا بالإذنِ العام كغيره ، فذلك التأديب تعليم وترييض للمستقبل ، لا عقوبة عن ذَنْبٍ كما يعتقدُهُ مَنْ جَهِلَ ، وباطنُ ذلك التأديب يدلُّ على الاعتناء العظيم بيونس عليهِ السلام ، والتشريف له بتولّي المولى العظيم لتربيته وترييضه بلطيف تدبيره ، ولم يكلْهُ في ذلك لنفسِهِ ، ولا لأحدٍ مِنْ عبيدِهِ
As for the story of Yunus (peace be upon him): there is no text indicating a sin. It only mentions that he fled and went angrily, both referring to his people — i.e., he fled from them and went angry due to their disbelief. Avoiding the people of disbelief and abandoning one's homelands are among the greatest acts of obedience if they came from someone else. However, Allah, glorified be He, alerted Yunus (peace be upon him) through that discipline that he is not like others in this, because he is among the special ones of His presence, sent for the guidance of creation from Him. The desired objective of their guidance is not fully achieved except by his patience with their harshness and witnessing their error. So he does not act except by special permission, not general permission like others. That discipline is teaching and training for the future, not punishment for a sin as those who are ignorant believe. The inner meaning of that discipline indicates the great care for Yunus (peace be upon him) and his honor by the great Lord undertaking his upbringing and training with delicate planning, and He did not entrust him in that to himself or to any of His servants.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an interpretation of the story of Prophet Yunus (Jonah) to defend his impeccability. Sanusi begins by stating that the Qur'anic text does not explicitly mention a sin. What is mentioned is that Yunus 'fled' (abaqa) and 'went angrily' (dhahaba mughadiban), but these refer to his leaving his people due to their disbelief. Avoiding disbelievers and leaving one's homeland are actually among the greatest acts of worship if done by someone else (i.e., a normal person). However, Allah reprimanded Yunus because he is not like others: he is a special prophet sent to guide his people, and guidance requires patience. Therefore, he needs special permission to act, not the general permission that others have. So the discipline was teaching and training for the future, not punishment for a sin. The deeper meaning is that it shows Allah's great care for Yunus, personally training him, not leaving him to himself or to any other creature.

أبق
مغاضباً

Correction: Sanusi explains that no text indicates a sin; his actions were a form of dutiful piety, but as a prophet he needed special permission, so the discipline was training, not punishment.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Prophet Yunus's discipline was not punishment for sin but a training for his unique mission, showing Allah's special care for him.

Refuting Sinful Interpretations of David's Story
Sanusi cites authorities to deny that David committed any sin in the incident with the two litigants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Sunni position on the incident involving Prophet David and the two litigants, and why attributing major sins to prophets is rejected.

Core Idea
The Qur'anic account of David's test does not imply moral sin; the fault was only a hasty judgment.

This lesson addresses a common misunderstanding about Prophet David. Some storytellers and exegetes have inserted narratives from corrupted sources suggesting that David committed grave sins. Sanusi, following Qadi 'Iyad, firmly rejects these and offers the correct interpretation based on the Qur'an and sound scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the authoritative tone and citations.
2
Identify the authorities cited
List the scholars mentioned: 'Iyad, al-Samarqandi, Qatadah, Ahmad ibn Nasr, Abu Tammam, al-Dawudi. Understand their roles in the argument.
Each supports the rejection of sinful narratives.
3
Understand the key terms
Focus on 'fatannahu' (tested) and 'awwab' (penitent/obedient). See how they are interpreted to avoid implying sin.
These terms are central to the correct understanding.
4
Grasp the limited fault
The only fault attributed to David by al-Samarqandi is a hasty judgment in saying 'He has wronged you' based on one litigant's claim. This is a minor error, not a moral sin.
This preserves prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا قصة داودَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : فقال عياض في ( الشفا ) : لا يجوز أنْ يُلتفت إلى ما سَطَرَهُ فيها الأخباريون عن أهل الكتاب الذينَ بدلوا وغيّروا، ونقلَهُ بعضُ المفسّرينَ ، ولم ينص الله تعالى على شيءٍ مِنْ ذلك، ولا ورد في حديث صحيح ، والذي نص الله عليه قوله : وَظَنَّ دَاوُدُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّاهُ إلى قولِهِ وَحُسْنَ مَتَابِ (ص: ٢٤ - ٢٥) وقولُه فيهِ : أَوَّابٌ (ص: ١٧) ، فمعنى «فتناه » : اختبرناه، وأوَّابٌ قال قتادة : مطيع . ثم حكى عن السمرقندي : أنَّ ذنبه الذي استغفرَ منهُ قولُهُ لأحدِ الخصمين : لَقَدْ ظَلَمَكَ (ص: ٢٤)، فظلمَهُ بقولِ خصمِهِ، وإلى نفي ما أُضِيفَ في الأخبار إلى داود عليهِ السلامُ مِنْ ذلكَ ذهبَ أَحمدُ بنُ نصر وأبو تمام وغيرُهما مِنَ المحققين، قال الداودي : ليس في قصَّةِ
As for the story of David (peace be upon him): 'Iyad said in al-Shifa: 'It is not permissible to pay attention to what the storytellers have written about it from the People of the Book who altered and changed, and some exegetes have transmitted it, and Allah Almighty has not stated anything of that, nor has it come in a sound hadith. What Allah has stated is His saying: "And David thought that We had tested him..." up to His saying "and good return" (Sad 24-25), and His saying about him: "often returning" (Sad 17). So the meaning of 'We tested him' is We tried him, and 'awwab' means penitent, said Qatadah: obedient. Then he related from al-Samarqandi that his sin for which he sought forgiveness was his statement to one of the two litigants: 'He has certainly wronged you' (Sad 24). So he wronged him by the statement of his opponent. And to deny what has been attributed in the reports to David (peace be upon him) of that... went Ahmad ibn Nasr, Abu Tammam, and other investigators. al-Dawudi said: There is nothing in the story of...'
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a critique of sinful interpretations of the story of Prophet David (Dawud). Sanusi begins by quoting Qadi 'Iyad from al-Shifa, who says we should ignore the fabrications of the storytellers (akhbariyyun) based on distorted reports from the People of the Book. The Qur'an does not specify a sin, and there is no authentic hadith. The Qur'anic verses only mention that David thought he was tested (fatannahu), meaning tried, and he is described as awwab (penitent, obedient). Then Sanusi narrates from al-Samarqandi that David's sin was merely his hasty judgment against one of the two litigants by saying 'He has wronged you' based on the opponent's claim, which was a mistake but not a moral sin. Then he mentions that scholars like Ahmad ibn Nasr and Abu Tammam rejected sinful reports. The passage ends with al-Dawudi stating that there is nothing in the story (to support sin).

السمرقندي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think David committed adultery or murder based on the story of the two litigants.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the only fault was a hasty judgment, not a major sin, preserving prophetic infallibility.

Key Takeaway

Defending Prophet Yunus from the Implication of Sin
Author interprets Yunus verse to show he did not intend sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse about Prophet Yunus is interpreted to clear him from the implication of sin through linguistic and logical reasoning.

Core Idea
The verse does not imply sin; 'restrict' not 'power' is the correct meaning.

This passage tackles a common misinterpretation of a Quranic verse about Prophet Yunus. By analyzing the linguistic meaning and logical implications, the author shows that the verse actually proves the Prophet's innocence. Let's read the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Pay attention to the verse quote and the author's immediate clarification.
2
Understand the linguistic clarification
Notice how the author reinterprets 'لن نقدر عليه' to mean 'would not restrict him' rather than 'would not have power over him'.
This shift in meaning is crucial to the entire defense.
3
Follow the logical proof
Trace the author's argument: if someone intends sin, they fear punishment; since Yunus thought he would not be restricted, he did not intend sin.
The argument uses a necessary implication to establish the Prophet's innocence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قوله تعالى : ﴿ فَظَنَّ أَن لَّن نَّقْدِرَ عَلَيْهِ ﴾ [الأنبياء : ۸۷] : فمعناه : فظن أن لن نُضيِّقَ عليهِ فيما فعلَ مِنَ الخروج عن قومِهِ ؛ لأنَّهُ عليهِ السلام لم يَتعمَّد في ذلك معصيةً ، ولا قصد مخالفة ، ويدلُّ على ذلكَ ما أخبر الله تعالى بهِ عنه هنا مِنْ ظَنّهِ أنْ لن يُضيَّقَ عليهِ ؛ لأنَّ ذلكَ مستلزم قطعاً لعدم قصدِهِ عليهِ السلامُ المعصية ؛ إذ مَنْ قصد معصية خافَ تضييق الله تعالى عليه بالعذاب ضرورةً وإِنْ كانَ مِنْ أدنى المؤمنينَ ، فكيف بأعلاهم وهم رسل الله تبارك وتعالى ؟!
As for His statement, Most High: {And he thought that We would not restrict him} [Al-Anbiya: 87], its meaning is: he thought that We would not narrow (the circumstances) upon him regarding what he did of leaving his people; because he, peace be upon him, did not deliberately commit disobedience in that, nor did he intend opposition. And that is indicated by what Allah, Most High, informed about him here of his thinking that We would not narrow upon him; because that necessarily entails the absence of his intent, peace be upon him, of disobedience; since whoever intends disobedience necessarily fears Allah's narrowing upon him with punishment, even if he is from the lowest of the believers; so how about the highest of them, and they are the messengers of Allah, Blessed and Most High?!
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Prophet Yunus against the misinterpretation of the Quranic verse. The author first cites the verse "وَظَنَّ أَن لَّن نَّقْدِرَ عَلَيْهِ" which could be misread as 'he thought We would not have power over him.' The author clarifies that 'لن نقدر عليه' here means 'We would not restrict him' or 'make things difficult for him,' not a denial of God's power. The reason is that Yunus did not intend sin or opposition; he left his people out of divine permission. The author then provides a logical proof: if someone intends a sin, they necessarily fear God's punishment (having the situation narrowed upon them). Since Yunus thought that God would not narrow upon him, this shows he did not intend sin. This argument uses the prophet's own state of mind as evidence of innocence. The rhetorical conclusion emphasizes that if even the lowest believer fears punishment when sinning, then prophets—the highest creation—would certainly fear and avoid sin. Thus, the verse does not imply any sin on Yunus's part.

Key Terms
الأنبياء
المعصية
تضييق
الظن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse implies Allah was powerless over Prophet Yunus or that Yunus doubted Allah's power.
Correction: The word 'قدر' here means 'to restrict' or 'narrow,' not 'to have power over.' The verse actually shows Yunus expected mercy and did not intend sin.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue is the correct meaning of 'لن نقدر عليه' in the story of Yunus?
A) That Allah had no power over him.
B) That Allah would not restrict or narrow upon him.
C) That Yunus thought he could escape Allah's judgment.
D) That Yunus doubted Allah's ability.

Key Takeaway
The verse about Prophet Yunus, when properly understood, actually affirms his sinlessness and does not imply any wrongdoing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a Quranic verse that seems to attribute a shortcoming to a prophet, does your heart immediately defend them, or do you entertain doubts? What does your reaction reveal about your reverence for Allah's chosen ones?
?
The author argues that even the lowest believer fears Allah's restriction when sinning. Examine your own life: when you commit a sin, do you truly fear Allah's punishment, or do you feel a sense of security? How can you cultivate a deeper fear of Allah's restriction?
?
This lesson shows that the Prophet's own state of mind (lack of fear of restriction) proves his sinlessness. If you were in a situation where you might be misunderstood, would your internal state reflect innocence or guilt? What step will you take today to align your inner state with obedience to Allah?

Defending Prophet Dawud from Fabricated Narratives
Author cites authorities to reject sinful interpretations of Dawood's story.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars defend Prophet Dawud from false narratives by distinguishing between Quranic truth and fabricated Israelite stories.

Core Idea
Prophet Dawud's repentance was not from grave sin but from a minor lapse in judgment, and the false stories are rejected.

The story of Prophet Dawud is often distorted by unreliable sources. Sunni scholars like Qadi 'Iyad and Ali ibn Abi Talib reject these fabrications. In this lesson, we examine the author's defense of Dawud from false narratives, focusing on what the Quran actually says and what scholars have clarified.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Let the author's argument and the citations of authorities come through.
The passage begins with a reference to Qadi 'Iyad's al-Shifa.
2
Identify the authorities cited
Notice the scholars quoted: Qadi 'Iyad, al-Samarqandi, Ahmad ibn Nasr, Abu Tamam, al-Dawudi, and Ali ibn Abi Talib. Each contributes to rejecting false narratives.
These authorities form a chain of verification against unreliable stories.
3
Understand the true nature of Dawud's repentance
Focus on al-Samarqandi's explanation that Dawud's 'sin' was a hasty judgment based on one litigant's claim, not adultery or murder. His repentance was out of prophetic awe and fear of Allah.
This aligns with the Quran's description of Dawud as 'oft-returning' (awwab).
4
Reflect on the rejection of fabricated stories
The author emphasizes that the Israelite stories are confused and not to be trusted. Ali ibn Abi Talib threatened severe punishment for those who spread them. Consider why this defense is important for the integrity of prophethood.
This connects to the broader Islamic principle of protecting prophetic dignity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قصة داودَ عليه الصلاةُ والسلام : فقال عياض في ( الشفا » : « ) لا يجوز أنْ يُلتفت إلى ما سَطَرَهُ فيها الأخباريون عن أهل الكتاب الذينَ بدلوا وغيّروا، ونقلَهُ بعضُ المفسّرينَ ، ولم ينص الله تعالى على شيءٍ مِنْ ولا ورد في حديث صحيح ، والذي نص الله عليه قوله : ذلك وَظَنَّ دَاوُردُ أَنَّمَا فَتَنَّهُ ... إلى قولِهِ وَحُسْنَ مَتَابِ اصَ ﴾ : ٢٤ - ٢٥] وقولُه فيهِ : أَوَابُ ﴾ [ص: ۱۷] ، فمعنى «فتناه » : اختبرناه و أوَّابٌ ، قال قتادة : مطبع . ثم حكى عن السمرقندي : ( أنَّ ذنبه الذي استغفرَ منهُ قولُهُ لأحدِ الخصمين : ﴿ لَقَدْ ظَلَمَكَ ﴾ [صَ : ٢٤] ، فظلمَهُ بقولِ خصمِهِ ، وإلى نفي ما أُضِيفَ في الأخبار إلى داود عليهِ السلامُ مِنْ ذلكَ . . ذهبَ أَحمدُ بنُ نصر وأبو تمام وغيرُهما مِنَ المحققين ، قال الداودي : ليس في قصَّةِ داود وأوريا خبرٌ يثبتُ ، ولا يُظَنُّ بنبي محبةُ قتل مسلم وقيل : إِنَّ الخصمينِ اللَّذين اختصما إليه في نِتاجِ غنم ، ظاهر الآية ( انتهى ) قلتُ : ولا شكٍّ أنَّ في كتب بني إسرائيل في هذه القصَّةِ تخليطاً عظيماً لا يليقُ أَنْ يُلتفتَ إليهِ ، وقد قالَ علي بن أبي طالب رضيَ اللهُ عنهُ : ( مَنْ حَدَّثَ بما قال هؤلاءِ القُصَّاص في أمرٍ داود .. جلدتُهُ حدَّينِ ؛ لِمَا ارتكبَ مِنْ حرمةِ مَنْ رفعَ اللهُ قدرَهُ )) وأما استغفارُه عليه الصلاة والسلام وبكاؤُهُ وتضرُّعُهُ : فجار على المعهودِ مِنْ حالِ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام في إجلالهم المولى الكريم ، وخوفهم منه ، وهيبتهم له على قَدْرِ معرفتهم به .
As for the story of Dawud, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Iyad said in al-Shifa: "It is not permissible to pay attention to what the historians have recorded in it from the People of the Book who altered and changed, and which some commentators have transmitted, and Allah the Most High has not explicitly stated anything of it, nor has it come in a sound hadith. And what Allah has explicitly stated is His saying: {And Dawud thought that We had tried him... to His saying: and goodly return} [Sad: 24-25] and His saying in it: {oft-returning} [Sad: 17]. So the meaning of 'tried him' is: We tested him, and 'oft-returning'—Qatada said: obedient." Then he narrated from al-Samarqandi: "That his sin for which he sought forgiveness was his statement to one of the two litigants: {He has certainly wronged you} [Sad: 24]; so he wronged him by the statement of his opponent." And to negating what has been added in the reports about Dawud, peace be upon him, from that—Ahmad ibn Nasr, Abu Tamam, and others from the verifiers went. Al-Dawudi said: "There is no report about the story of Dawud and Uriah that is established, and it should not be thought of a prophet that he loved killing a Muslim." And it is said: "Indeed, the two litigants who presented their dispute to him were concerning the progeny of sheep—the apparent meaning of the verse." Then he said: I say: There is no doubt that in the books of the Children of Israel regarding this story there is great confusion that is not worthy of attention. And Ali ibn Abi Talib, may Allah be pleased with him, said: "Whoever narrates what these storytellers have said about Dawud... I will flog him twice, for the violation of the sanctity of one whose status Allah has raised." As for his seeking forgiveness, peace and blessings be upon him, and his weeping and supplication: it is in accordance with the accustomed state of the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, in their veneration of the Generous Lord, their fear of Him, and their awe of Him according to their knowledge of Him.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Prophet Dawud against false narratives that imply sin. The author begins by citing Qadi 'Iyad from al-Shifa, who rules that it is impermissible to rely on stories from the People of the Book (Israelite traditions) that have been altered. Only what Allah explicitly states in the Quran—that Dawud thought he was being tested, and that he repented—is valid. The meaning of 'فتناه' is 'We tested him,' and 'أواب' means obedient. Then the author reports al-Samarqandi's interpretation that Dawud's only 'sin' was saying to one litigant that the other wronged him, which was a hasty judgment based on the opponent's claim—not a sin of desire or murder. The author notes that verified scholars like Ahmad ibn Nasr and Abu Tamam negate any added sinful acts. Al-Dawudi adds that there is no established report about Dawud and Uriah, and it is unthinkable that a prophet would love killing a Muslim. The author then adds his own comment: the Israelite books contain great confusion, and 'Ali ibn Abi Talib threatened severe punishment for those who spread such false stories. Finally, the author explains Dawud's repentance: prophets are always in a state of veneration, fear, and awe of Allah, and their seeking forgiveness is due to minor lapses in optimal conduct, not major sins.

Key Terms

الأخباريون
الشفا
القُصَّاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the Bible stories about Dawud and Uriah are true, implying Dawud committed adultery and murder.
Correction: The author affirms these stories are fabricated and rejected by reliable Islamic sources; the Quran only mentions a hasty judgment and sincere repentance, not grave sin.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what was the real 'sin' of Dawud for which he sought forgiveness?
A) He committed adultery and murder.
B) He made a hasty judgment based on one litigant's statement.
C) He abandoned his people like Yunus.
D) He married multiple wives unlawfully.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Dawud's repentance was not from grave sin but from a minor lapse in judgment, and Islamic authorities strongly reject fabricated Israelite stories about him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story about a prophet that seems to tarnish his character, do you immediately reject it based on Islamic teachings, or do you let it linger in your heart and mind? What will you do next time?
?
The prophets wept and sought forgiveness out of awe and love for Allah, not because they committed serious sins. How often do you seek forgiveness for your own minor mistakes and moments of heedlessness? Do you truly feel that awe of Allah in your daily life?
?
Ali ibn Abi Talib threatened severe punishment for those who defamed Dawud. Are you careful to protect the honor of the prophets in your own speech and by rejecting false stories, even when they are popular?

Prophethood
beginner
