The Wisdom of the Prophet's Marriage to Zaynab
Author defends the marriage by citing divine legislation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divine legislation to abrogate a pre-Islamic custom, not a personal act.

Core Idea
This marriage was a divine law, not a personal desire.

Critics have questioned the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh, but the Quran itself reveals its true purpose. In this passage, the author explains that the marriage was a legislative act from Allah to remove a social restriction. By reading this, you will see how the Prophet's action was in obedience to divine command and had a clear legal objective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author focuses only on what Allah revealed in the Quran, dismissing other narratives.
The passage is a direct defense based on scriptural authority.
2
Identify the legislative purpose
The author states that the marriage was to legislate the permissibility of marrying the former wives of adopted sons. Find the Quranic verse and understand its message.
The verse is the core evidence.
3
Contrast with the pre-Islamic custom
Before Islam, adopted sons were treated like biological sons in terms of marital prohibitions. This marriage abrogated that custom. Reflect on how this change removed hardship for believers.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's obedience
The Prophet's action was not based on personal desire but on divine command. This defends his character against accusations.
This reinforces his prophethood and moral integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قصة نبينا وسيّدِنا ومولانا محمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مَعَ زيدٍ مولاه وزينب رضي الله تعالى عنهما : فليسَ يصح فيها إلا ما ذكر مولانا جلَّ وعزّ في كتابه العزيز ؛ مِنْ كونه سبحانه وتعالى زَوَّجَ لنبينا عليهِ الصلاة والسلام زينب بعدَ فِراقِ زيد لها ، وشرع بذلك إباحة تزويج حلائل الأدعياء ، وأَنَّهُنَّ لا يُلحَقْنَ في التحريم بحلائل أبناء النسبِ فقال جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ فَلَمَّا قَضَى زَيْدٌ مِنْهَا وَطَرًا زَوَحْنَكَهَا لِكَيْ لَا يَكُونَ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ حَرَجٌ فِي أَزْوَج أَدْعِيَا بِهِمْ إِذَا فَضَوْا مِنْهُنَّ وَطَرًا ﴾ [الأحزاب : ٣٧] .
As for the story of our Prophet and Master and Patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with Zayd his freed slave and Zaynab, may Allah be pleased with them both: nothing is authentic in it except what our Lord, Mighty and Majestic, mentioned in His noble Book; of Him, Exalted and Most High, having married Zaynab to our Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, after Zayd's separation from her, and thereby legislating the permissibility of marrying the former wives of adopted sons, and that they are not included in the prohibition with the former wives of biological sons. So He said, Majestic is He who speaks: {So when Zayd completed his desire from her, We married her to you so that there might be no difficulty for the believers in (the matter of) the wives of their adopted sons when they have completed their desire from them} [Al-Ahzab: 37].
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Prophet Muhammad's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh, which was criticized by hypocrites and later misinterpreters. The author states that only what Allah explicitly reveals in the Quran is true: Allah Himself married Zaynab to the Prophet after Zayd divorced her. The purpose was to abrogate the pre-Islamic custom that an adopted son's former wife is like a biological son's former wife and thus prohibited. The Quranic verse makes clear that this marriage was a legislative act to remove hardship for believers, not a personal desire. The author cites the verse to demonstrate that the Prophet's action was in obedience to divine command and had a clear legal objective: to establish the permissibility of marrying the ex-wives of adopted sons. Thus, any suggestion of impropriety or personal motive is rejected.

Key Terms
زيد
زينب
حلائل الأدعياء
التحريم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the Prophet married Zaynab out of lust or personal desire.
Correction: The author clarifies that the marriage was a divine legislation to establish a new ruling, as stated in the Quran.

Checkpoint
What was the legislative purpose of the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab according to the passage?
A) To increase his wives for political alliance.
B) To allow believers to marry the former wives of their adopted sons.
C) To show that adopted sons are like biological sons in all rulings.
D) To honor Zaynab because she was from a noble family.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divine legislation to permit believers to marry the ex-wives of adopted sons, abrogating a pre-Islamic prohibition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a command from Allah contradicts a deeply ingrained social custom in your life, do you rush to justify your own desires or submit immediately? What custom do you hold onto that might actually be a barrier to full obedience?
?
The Prophet ﷺ personally endured slander to legislate a change for the believers. Are you willing to bear discomfort or criticism to uphold a truth that benefits others, even if it costs your reputation?
?
This marriage removed 'haraj' (difficulty) for the community. Is there a believer in your life whom you have made 'difficulty' for by holding them to a standard Allah Himself has not required? How will you remove that burden today?
